when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師 , 她確實做了一些 , 但真正的狀況是說未來會比這個要來得多 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這傢伙出現了 , 艾倫•圖靈 , 在1936年 , 再次發明了電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器是完全機械化的
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turing的機器完全是理論性的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩位都是從數學的觀點來的 , 但圖靈告訴我們一件非常重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他為電腦科學奠下了數學基礎 , 說: 「 不論你怎麼製造電腦 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不管你的電腦是不是機械化 , 像是babbage是 , 還是電子化的 , 像是電腦是今天 , 還是在未來 , 或是在未來 , 細胞 , 還是再一次機械化 , 一旦我們進入了奈米科技 ,
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 讓它變得微小 。 這些東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	在某種意義上計算的本質
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做教堂調查 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	所以 , 突然間 , 你就有了這個連結 , 說這東西babbage真的是一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它能夠做到我們現今用電腦所做的一切 , 只有很慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了讓各位知道它有多緩慢 , 它有大約1k的記憶體 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它用了打孔卡 , 被餵進去 , 它的跑步速度大約是第一台zx81的慢了一萬倍 。
it did have a ram pack .	它的確有一個拉姆派克 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	若想的話 , 你可以多增加許多額外的記憶 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 今天這又將我們帶到什麼境界 ?
so there are plans .	所以有計畫 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在斯丁丹 , 科學博物館存檔中 , 有數百個計劃和數千頁的筆記 , 由查爾斯•巴貝奇寫下 , 關於這個分析引擎 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中有一套計畫我們稱之為 「 計劃28 」 , 那也是我以doronswaade為起點的慈善機構的名字 , 他是科學博物館的計算師 , 也是推動計劃建造不同引擎的人 , 我們的計劃是要建造它 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在肯辛頓這裡 , 我們會建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個專案計畫有許多零件要做 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	其一是babbage的檔案掃描
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這是已經完成的 。 第二 , 是研究所有這些計畫 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是模擬那台機器的電腦模擬 , 最後一部分就是在科學博物館建造它 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它建造時 , 你會終於能夠理解電腦如何運作 , 因為與其在你面前有一小片晶片 , 你必須看著這件巨大的事 , 然後說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶體在運作 , 我看到cpu在運作 , 我聽見它在運作 。 我可能聞到它的味道 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在這兩者之間 , 我們要做一個模擬
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	babbage自己寫道 , 他說一旦分析引擎存在 , 它肯定會引導未來的科學課程 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有建造它 , 因為他總是在做新的計畫 , 但當它真的被建造起來時 , 當然 , 在1940年代 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我讓你們稍微了解一下 , 用一個影片 , 它的樣子 , 呈現出cpu機制運作的一部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	所以 , 這只是三組齒輪 , 它會補充 。 這是加法的機制 , 所以你想像一下這個巨大的機器 。
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年時間 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年代發生之前 , 我們將擁有
thank you very much .	非常感謝大家 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這個影像充斥的演講中 , 亞倫•亞瑟伯特蘭德展示了他最近的三個項目 , 關於人性和我們的居住地 , 在他的系列中驚人的 「 地球 」 , 來自全球的 「 個人訪談 」 , 在他的網路專案計畫中 , 他的六十億人 , 他的即將拍攝 「 家 」 , 記錄了人類對環境的影響 , 透過吸收影片來記錄人類的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、電影、未來、人性、媒體、攝影 ,
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	yanartbertrand在廣角捕捉脆弱的地球
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球有很大的影響 , 可以透過飛機來到這裡旅行 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中排放了9噸的二氧化碳 ; 那是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來到這裡 , 來談談生態 , 一年內我排放的二氧化碳和法國人一樣多 。
so what do i have to do ?	那我該怎麼做呢 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	我回家時必須殺死法國人 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我得要用另一種方式來抵消碳 , 就像我每次一樣 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的工作是展現我們對地球的影響 。

in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在亞伯達省 , 人們在非營利組織工作 , 24小時 , 以七小時盡可能的提煉出石油 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們對石油的結局了解

but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們每年使用的石油比我們發現的還多三倍 。

coral reef in new caledonia .	新卡多尼亞的珊瑚礁

for the past 30 years i've been closely watching the earth and its dwellers from high up in the sky .	過去30年來 , 我一直很密切地看著地球和它的dwellers , 來自天空的高空 。
our life is tied to the wellbeing of our planet .	我們的生命和我們星球的福祉綁在一起 。
we depend on water , forests , deserts , oceans .	我們依賴水、森林、沙漠、海洋 。
fishing , breeding , farming are still the world's foremost human occupations .	捕魚、繁殖、養殖 , 仍然是世界上最主要的人類職業 。
and what binds us together is far greater than what divides us .	把我們結合在一起 , 遠比我們分裂的更偉大 。
we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們都共享著同樣的需求 , 對於地球的禮物──同樣的願望──能在我們自己身上升起 , 變得更好 。
and yet we carry on raising walls to keep us apart .	然而 , 我們卻帶著養育牆來讓我們分離 。
today our greatest battle is to protect the natural offerings of our planet .	現今 , 我們最大的戰役就是要保護地球的自然提供 。
in less than 50 years we've altered it more thoroughly than in the entire history of mankind .	在不到50年的時間裡 , 我們已經更徹底地改變了它 , 超過了整個人類的歷史 。
half of the world's forests have vanished .	世界上一半的森林已經消失
water resources are running low .	水資源的運行率很低 。
intensive farming is depleting soils .	密集的農場正在耗盡土壤 。
our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能源來源不穩定 ,
the climate is changing .	氣候正在改變 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們正在瀕臨絕種的自己 。
we're only trying to improve our lives .	我們只想改善生活
but the wealth gaps are growing wider .	但財富差距在成長更廣 。
we haven't yet understood that we're going at a much faster pace than the planet can sustain .	我們尚未明白 , 我們的速度比地球能維持的快得多 。
we know that solutions are available today .	我們知道現今的解決方案是可行的 。
we all have the power to change this trend for the better .	我們都有能力改變這個趨勢 , 讓它變得更好 。

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在tedxboston的演講中 , 理查德•雷斯尼克展現出健康照護的廉價和快速基因序列 , 將健康照護顛覆 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、醫療保健、科學、科技
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查德•雷斯尼克:歡迎來到基因革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	女士們先生們 , 我向你們介紹人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體一 , 左上角
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下角是性染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女人有兩份大的x染色體 ; 男人有x , 當然 , 還有那份y的小複本 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	抱歉男孩 , 但這只是一小件事 , 讓你變得不一樣 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以如果你放大這個基因組 , 那麼你看到的是這個雙螺旋結構--生命的代碼--這四個生化字母 , 或者我們稱之為鹼基 , 對吧 ? 即c , g和t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組中有多少 ? 30億 。
is that a big number ?	這是一個很大的數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 每個人都可以隨意丟大數字 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但事實上 , 如果我把一個鹼基放在這1280個像素的每一個像素上 , 800個解析度螢幕上 , 我們會需要3000個螢幕來觀察基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	所以它真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	也許是因為它的大小 , 一群人 , 順便一提 , y染色體決定要將它定序 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	所以 , 15年後 , 事實上 , 大約40億美元之後 , 基因組被定序並發行 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	在2003年 , 最後的版本被公開 , 他們繼續著手進行研究 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	這一切都是在一個看起來像這樣的機器上完成的 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每一基地的成本大約是一美元--一個非常緩慢的做法 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我來這裡是要告訴各位 , 世界已經完全改變 , 你們都不知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	所以現在我們要做的是 , 我們拿一個基因組 , 做大約五十本 , 我們把這些複製品剪成小五十個資料庫 , 然後我們把它們做定序 , 大量平行 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	接著 , 我們將它帶入軟體中 , 我們重新組合它 , 告訴你們故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	所以 , 給大家看一下這是什麼樣子的圖片 , 人類基因組計畫:3gb , 對 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	一台在其中一台機器上運行:一週內200gbas 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	今年夏天 , 這兩百人將會改變到六百人 , 沒有這種速度減慢的跡象 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以 , 一個鹼基的價格 , 為了定序一個鹼基 , 已經下跌了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	相當於你在1998年把車子裝滿了氣體 , 等到2011年 , 現在你可以開到木星兩次 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口、pc定位 , 所有醫學文獻、摩爾定律、古老的定序方式 , 這裡有所有新的東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是一張木頭尺度 ; 你通常不會看到像這樣上升的線條 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	所以 , 全世界人類基因組測序的能力大約是今年的5萬到10萬個人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	我們會根據被放置的機器知道這點 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	這是預期在可預見的未來中一年會有兩倍、三倍 , 或四倍之多 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 有一個實驗室 , 代表所有能力的20% 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	叫做北京基因組學研究所
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	順道一提 , 中國人絕對要贏得這場比賽 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學有什麼意義 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	所以 , 一個女人37歲 。
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她用 「 階段二 」 雌激素受體乳癌 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受手術、化療和放射線治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後 , 她又回來了 「 階段三 」 卵巢癌 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次用手術和化療治療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後 , 她在42歲回來 , 患有更多卵巢癌 , 更多的化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她帶著急性骨髓性白血病回來 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她進入呼吸衰竭 , 八天後死亡 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 這位女士接受治療的方式 , 只要十年的時間 , 看起來就會像血管一樣 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	而是因為像我這位同事rickwilson在華盛頓大學的基因研究所的人決定去看一下這位女士後遺症
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他進行測序 , 取出皮膚細胞 , 健康的皮膚 , 還有癌症的骨髓 , 他在幾週內完成了兩種基因組的測序 , 沒什麼大不了的 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	接著 , 他比較了軟體中的這兩個基因組 , 他發現 , 在其他東西當中 , 是一個刪除 , 一個2000個基對的刪除 , 在一個叫做tp53的基因中 , 大約有300億個鹼基 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你這個基因中有這種嚴重的突變 , 你一生中有90%的可能性會得到癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	不幸的是 , 這並不能幫助這位女性 , 但它的確有嚴重、深刻的影響 , 影響到她的家人 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果他們有相同的突變 , 且他們得到了這個基因測試 , 且他們了解它 , 那他們就可以去取得普通的螢幕 , 他們可以在早期抓到癌症 , 且有可能活得更長壽 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	讓我向各位介紹現在的貝利雙胞胎 , 在兩歲時被診斷出腦性麻痺 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的母親是一位非常勇敢的女性 , 她不相信症狀並不符合 , 透過一些英雄的努力和大量的網路搜尋 , 她能夠說服醫學界 , 事實上 , 他們還有別的東西 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們所擁有的是各式各樣的肌張力不全症 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以他們被給了貓頭龍 , 他們的症狀確實有所改善 , 但它們並不完全是不尋常的 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	結果 , 照片裡的先生是一位叫joebeery的人 , 他很幸運能成為一家名為生命科技的公司的首肯 。
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	它們是這兩家公司的其中一家 , 讓這些龐大的基因體定序工具成為一家 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	他的做法是讓他的孩子進行測序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現 , 在一個叫做 「 彈簧 」 的基因中有一系列突變 , 負責產生血清素 , 其他東西 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以在貓咪的頂端 , 他們給這些孩子們一種血清素的先驅藥品 , 現在有效地正常了 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	各位 , 若沒有完整的基因序列 , 這絕對不會發生 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	當時這是幾年前的成本是10萬美金
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	今天是一萬美元 。 明年是一千美元 。
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	在它100美元後的一年 , 給予或花一年 。
that's how fast this is moving .	這就是這個移動的速度 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	這裡有小nick喜歡蝙蝠俠和松槍 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	結果尼克在兒童醫院出現 , 肚子像飢荒受害者 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	不是說他不吃東西 , 而是當他吃的時候 , 他的腸子基本上會打開 , 糞便會外漏到他的腸子裡 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	所以一百場手術之後 , 他看著他的媽媽說: 「 媽 , 請幫我祈禱 。 我在這麼多的痛苦中 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的小兒科醫生剛好有臨床遺傳學的背景 , 他完全不知道發生了什麼事 , 但他說: 「 讓這個孩子的基因序列 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	而他們發現的是 , 一個由控制細胞死亡的基因中單點突變 。
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	所以 , 理論是 , 他對於食物本質上所發生的事產生了一些免疫反應 , 那是自然反應 , 造成一些程式化的細胞死亡 。
but the gene that regulates that down is broken .	但是調節下來的基因是壞掉的 。
and so this informs , among other things , of course , a treatment for bone marrow transplant , which he undertakes .	當然 , 這也說明了他接受骨髓移植的治療 。
and after nine months of grueling recovery , he's now eating steak with a1 sauce .	經過九個月的辛苦復原之後 , 他現在用a1醬汁去吃牛排 。
the prospect of using the genome as a universal diagnostic is upon us today .	將基因組當作普遍診斷的前景 , 今天就在我們身上 。
today , it's here .	今天 , 在這裡 ,
and what it means for all of us is that everybody in this room could live an extra five , 10 , 20 years just because of this one thing .	這對我們所有人的意義是 , 在座的每個人都能過多五年、十年、二十年 , 只因為這一件事 。
which is a fantastic story , unless you think about humanity's footprint on the planet and our ability to keep up food production .	這是個很棒的故事 , 除非你考慮人類在地球的足跡 , 以及我們保持食物生產的能力 。
so it turns out that the very same technology is also being used to grow new lines of corn , wheat , soybean and other crops that are highly tolerant of drought , of flood , of pests and pesticides .	結果發現 , 同樣的技術也被用來種植玉米、麥子、黃豆和其他農作物 , 這些農作物非常包容乾旱、洪水、害蟲和殺蟲劑 。
now look , as long as we continue to increase the population , we're going to have to continue to grow and eat genetically modified foods , and that's the only position that i'll take today .	現在 , 看看 , 只要我們繼續增加人口 , 我們就得要繼續種植和吃基因改造食物 , 這是我今天唯一要採取的位置 。
unless there's anybody in the audience that would like to volunteer to stop eating ?	除非觀眾中有人願意自願停止飲食 ?
none , not one .	沒有 , 沒有一個 。
this is a typewriter , a staple of every desktop for decades .	這是一部打字機 , 數十年來 , 每一台桌面的釘子 。
and in fact , the typewriter was essentially deleted by this thing .	事實上 , 打字機基本上被這個東西刪除了 。
and then more general versions of word processors came about .	然後更廣泛的文字處理器出現了 。
but ultimately , it was a disruption on top of a disruption .	但 , 最終 , 它在顛覆的過程中造成了瓦解 。
it was bob metcalfe inventing the ethernet and the connection of all these computers that fundamentally changed everything .	是bobmetcalfe發明了ththernet和所有這些電腦的連結從根本上改變了一切
and suddenly we had netscape , and we had yahoo and we had , indeed , the entire dotcom bubble .	突然間 , 我們有了netscape , 我們有了yahoo , 我們的確有了整個網點泡泡 。
not to worry though , that was quickly rescued by the ipod , facebook and , indeed , angry birds .	不用擔心 , 很快就被ipod、臉書、以及憤怒的鳥類救回來了 。

so i just recently had to buy life insurance .	所以我最近才剛買了生命保險 。
and i was required to answer: a . i have never had a genetic test , b . i've had one , here you go , and c . i've had one and i'm not telling .	我被要求回答:我從來沒有過基因測驗 , b.我有過一個測驗 , 來了 , 然後c 。 我有一份 , 我沒說 。
thankfully , i was able to answer a , and i say that honestly in case my life insurance agent is listening .	謝天謝地 , 我得以回答a , 我誠實的說 , 以免我的生命保險經紀人在傾聽 。
but what would have happened if i had said c ?	但如果我說c , 會發生什麼事 ?
consumer applications for genomics , they will flourish .	消費者應用在基因組學上 , 他們會蓬勃發展 。

so anybody who's here today with your significant other , just turn over to them and swab their mouth , send it to the lab and you'll know for sure .	所以 , 今天在場的任何一個人 , 都帶著你顯著的他人 , 轉向他們 , 換他們的嘴巴 , 送到實驗室 , 你肯定會知道 。

and it looks really good .	而且看起來真的很好 。

but imagine if my genome were deidentified , sitting in software , and a third cousin's genome was also sitting there , and there was software that could compare these two and make these associations .	但 , 想像一下 , 如果我的基因被確認了 , 坐在軟體中 , 第三位表弟的基因也坐在那裡 , 有軟體可以比較這兩者 , 並做出這些關聯 。
not hard to imagine . my company has software that does this right now .	不難想像 。 我的公司有軟體 , 現在就這樣做 。
and so imagine one more thing: that that software is able to ask both parties for mutual consents , " would you be willing to meet your third cousin ? "	所以 , 再試想一件事:那個軟體能夠要求兩黨都同意 , 「 你願意去見第三位表兄弟嗎 ? 」

daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	danielkraftmos--他的骨髓礦工--一個新裝置 , 很快地將救命的骨髓移植到捐贈者身上 。 他強調 , 成年的幹細胞在骨髓中能被用來治療許多末期疾病 , 從帕金森氏症到心臟病 。
biology , biotech , health , health care , medicine , science , technology	生物學、生物科技、健康照護、醫藥、科學、科技等 ,
daniel kraft invents a better way to harvest bone marrow	danielkraft發明了一個更好的方法來收割骨髓 。
so i am a pediatric cancer doctor and stemcell researcher at stanford university where my clinical focus has been bone marrow transplantation .	我是史丹佛大學的小兒科癌醫生和史丹佛大學的幹細胞研究員 , 我的臨床焦點是骨髓移植 。
now , inspired by jill bolte taylor last year , i didn't bring a human brain , but i did bring a liter of bone marrow .	現在 , jillboltetaylor去年的啟發 , 我並沒有帶一個人腦 , 但我確實帶了一公升的骨髓 。
and bone marrow is actually what we use to save the lives of tens of thousands of patients , most of whom have advanced malignancies like leukemia and lymphoma and some other diseases .	而骨髓 , 其實就是我們用來拯救數萬名病患的性命 , 其中大部分有先進的惡性腫瘤 , 如白血病、淋巴瘤 , 以及其他一些疾病 。
so , a few years ago , i'm doing my transplant fellowship at stanford .	所以 , 幾年前 , 我在史丹佛做移植研究 。
i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術室 。 我們這裡有bob , 他是志工捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他的骨髓送到全國 , 拯救一個患有白血病的孩童 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以實際上 , 我們要如何採收這種骨髓 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一整個o.r.的團隊 , 麻醉 , 護士 , 還有另一位醫生從我身邊 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	bob在桌上 , 我們拿了這個小針 , 你知道的 , 不是太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	我們的做法是把這個放進軟組織裡 , 用針筒刺進硬骨頭 , 吸收這個技術名詞 , 每次用針筒 , 大約有10ml的骨髓 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	然後把它交給護士 。 她把它插進一根錫子裡 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把它交回給我 。 我們一而再 , 再而三地這樣做 。
about 200 times usually .	通常大約有200次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	結束後 , 我手上就有一台叫車 , 更不用說bob , 它的屁股看起來更像這樣 , 就像瑞士起司一樣 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道嗎 , 這個程序在大約40年來都沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	可能有更好的方法來做這件事 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想到了一個微小的入侵方法 , 一個我們稱之為 「 骨髓採取器 」 的新裝置 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	而骨髓採礦者 , 它的運作方式呈現在此 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們標準的視障患者
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	不是進入骨頭幾十次 , 而是一次 , 進入到臀部前面或臀部後面 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有一個彈性、有力的導管 , 帶著一個特殊的電線尖端 , 會留在骨髓的殘酷部位 , 跟著臀部的輪廓移動 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以它會讓你非常快速地抱負 , 或吸出豐富的骨髓 , 很快地穿過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以在同一入口處多次通過 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快地 , bob就能得到一個穿刺 , 局部麻醉 , 做這個收成一個病人 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了幾個原型 。 我在史丹佛拿到一筆小額的經費 。
and played around with this a little bit .	並稍微隨心所欲的玩耍
and our team members developed this technology .	而我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們得到了兩隻大型動物 , 豬的研究
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們發現 , 出乎我們的意料 , 我們不僅得到骨髓 , 我們還得到十倍的幹細胞活動 , 比起一般的裝置 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置在去年才剛被食品及藥物管理局批准 。
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這是一位活病人 , 你可以看到它跟著四周的彈性曲線
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	這裡會有兩個人 , 同一個病人 , 來自同一個洞 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是在當地麻醉下進行的 , 做為一種病患 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	同樣的 , 我們得到的幹細胞比同一個病人的標準方法要多三到六倍 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	所以 , 你為什麼要在乎 ? 骨髓是成體幹細胞的非常豐富的來源 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很大的潛力 , 但尚未進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成體幹細胞遍佈全身 , 包括我們骨髓裡的血液循環幹細胞 , 我們用它做為幹細胞療法 , 已經用了超過四十年 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去十年間 , 使用骨髓幹細胞的爆炸 , 來治療病人的其他疾病 , 比如心臟病、血管疾病、人體運動、組織工程 , 甚至在神經學上 , 用來治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們才剛出櫃 , 正在商業化 , 今年 , 2.0年的骨髓採礦者世代 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望能讓更多的幹細胞脫離出來 , 轉化成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	可能會鼓勵更多人簽名成為潛在的救命骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	它甚至可能讓你銀行自己的骨髓幹細胞 , 當你更年輕、健康時 , 用在未來應該需要它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最終 , 這是我們骨髓移植手術的照片 , 他們每年聚集在史丹佛 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們在未來有更多這樣的倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪者garretlisi在宇宙中展示了有爭議的新模型 , 也許只是回答了所有的大問題 。 如果沒有其他東西 , 它是最美麗的八維模型 , 由你所見過的基本粒子和力量 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、科技
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	在他對萬物的理論上 , garretlisi
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 , 老兄 。 看看那些殺手方程式 。 甜心 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	其實 , 接下來的18分鐘 , 我會盡我所能的盡力去描述粒子物理學的美麗 , 沒有方程式 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	結果發現 , 我們可以從珊瑚身上學到很多東西 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗且不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每一塊珊瑚頭都由成千上萬個聚苯二甲酸酯組成
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些聚苯二甲酸酯會持續地發育和分裂成基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這是一個超級聰明的珊瑚 , 我們可以單靠一個個體 , 問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問 , 他在這個特定的地點 , 與鄰居相比 , 是否只是機會 , 或命運 , 或什麼 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	在把溫度調高之後 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題完全是愚蠢的 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可以是相當的意思 , 你看 , 我有衝浪疤 , 可以證明這一點 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這個聚酯會持續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居非常清楚地對他有相同的複本 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他也在其他地方 , 把他們當作分開的個體來體驗 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚來說 , 分支成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	不像我們 , 一個超智能的珊瑚會特別準備去了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學非常準確地描述我們的宇宙是如何運作的 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實是持續分成不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	對我們人類來說 , 這是件很奇怪的事 , 因為我們只能感受到一種可能 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這個量子怪異性最初是由erwinschraindinger和他的貓所描述 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓比較喜歡這個版本 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個設備中 , 薛丁格在一個裝有放射性樣本的箱子中 , 根據量子力學定律 , 分支成一個放射性和狀態 , 不存在 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在樣本放射線的分支中 , 釋放出毒藥和薛丁格已死 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實的其他分支中 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	這些真實是被每一個個體分開的 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	就算看得出來 , 另一個也不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這似乎對我們來說很奇怪 , 因為我們每一個人只會經歷一個個別的存在 , 而我們無法看到其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	這就好像我們每一個人 , 像薛丁格 , 都是分成不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們 , 這是世界在微小的尺度運作的方式 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	它可以用一個句子來總結:所有可能發生的事 , 都會發生 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不表示一切都會發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	物理學的其他部分則是描述可能發生的狀況和無法發生的狀況 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們一切都歸功於幾何學以及基本粒子的相互作用
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	只有在這些互動完全平衡的情況下才會發生 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我來描述一下我們對這些粒子的認識 , 它們是什麼 , 以及它們是如何運作的 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這個機器中 , 一束質子和反質子被加速到接近光速的速度 , 並在撞擊中聚集 , 產生出一股純粹的能量 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量馬上被轉換成亞原子粒子的噴霧 , 有偵測器和電腦用來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這台巨大的機器--日內瓦的大型強子對撞機有17英里的圓環 , 當它在運作時 , 能畫出蒙特利市的五倍之多的能量 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法準確預測哪些粒子會在任何個別碰撞中產生
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性都被實現了 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理學確實告訴我們哪些粒子可以產生
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子的質量和能量必定跟質子和反質子一樣多 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何比這能量限制更大質量的粒子都不會產生 , 而對我們仍然看不見 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這種新粒子加速器如此令人興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它會把這個能量極限推到前所未有的七倍以外 , 所以我們很快就會看到一些新粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但 , 在談談我們可能看到的是什麼之前 , 先讓我描述一下我們已經知道的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	有一整個亞原子粒子的動物園
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大部分人都熟悉電子 。
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在座的很多人都把他們推來推去 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也有一個中立的夥伴 , 叫做微中子 , 沒有電荷 , 也沒有很小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相對的 , 上下夸克有很大的質量 , 三者結合 , 讓原子內的質子和中子 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些物質粒子都來自左手邊和右手邊的品種 , 都有帶有反粒子的夥伴 , 帶有反電荷 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也有較少熟悉的第二代和第三代 , 和第一代有相同的載荷 , 但質量也較高 。
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子都和各式各樣的力粒子互動 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力通過光子的粒子互相作用電荷物質
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	還有一種很弱的力 , 叫做 「 不可想像力 」 , 這種弱力只會和左撇子有所互動 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克之間的強力作用 , 帶有不同的載荷 , 叫做色荷 , 帶有三種不同品種:紅色、綠色和藍色 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪罪murraygellmann為這些名字--他們是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 還有重力 , 它透過質量和旋轉和物質相互作用 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是 , 這裡有一種不同的載荷 , 和每一種力量有關 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種不同的力與物質相互作用 , 根據每個粒子所擁有的相應載荷 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個還沒被看見的粒子 , 但我們很確定存在 , 就是希格斯粒子 , 它會給所有其他粒子帶來質量 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是看到這個希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎可以確定它會 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最偉大的奧秘是我們可能看到的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	接下來我要讓你們看看這場演說的結尾 , 一個美麗的可能性 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	現在 , 如果我們用它們的旋轉和載荷來計算這些不同的粒子 , 有226種 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	那是很多粒子可以持續追蹤的 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	自然界的基本粒子似乎很奇怪 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們根據他們的指控來繪製它們 , 有些美麗的圖案就會出現 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的電荷是電荷
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有電荷 , 負電荷 , 夸克則有電荷 , 三分之一 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以當兩個上夸克和一個下夸克結合成一個質子時 , 它的電荷會加上一個質子 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也有反粒子 , 它有反電荷 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現 , 電荷其實是另外兩種載荷的組合:超荷和弱荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們散播出超荷和弱荷 , 並在這個二度載荷空間中繪製出粒子的載荷 , 電荷就是這些粒子沿著垂直方向坐的地方 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力相互作用 , 根據它們的超荷和弱荷 , 會產生這種模式 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這被稱為 「 統一的電子滅絕模型 」 , 它在1967年被放在一起 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	我們之所以只熟悉電荷 , 而不是這兩種都是因為希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的希格斯粒子有很大的質量 , 打破了這個電子表格的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	讓弱粒子具有很大的質量 , 會讓弱力非常弱 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	由於這個巨大的希格斯玻色子沿著水平方向坐著 , 電磁學的光子仍然無質量 , 並沿著這個載荷空間的垂直方向與電荷互動 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁力和弱力是由這個在二度空間中的粒子載荷所描述的模式
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以把強力透過它的兩個載荷方向傳遞出去 , 並沿著這些方向來繪製質子粒子的載荷 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以在四度載荷空間中畫出來 , 投射到像這樣的二度空間中 , 這樣我們就可以看見它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	每當粒子相互作用時 , 大自然就會把東西保持在完美的平衡 , 沿著這四個載荷方向前進 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果一個粒子和反粒子碰撞 , 它會造成能量爆裂 , 造成四個載荷方向的總載荷為零 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	此時 , 任何東西都可以被創造出來只要它有相同能量 , 並保持完全零的載荷 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	比如 , 這種弱力粒子和它的反粒子可以在碰撞中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在進一步的互動中 , 指控總是保持平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個弱粒子可以腐化成一個電子和一個反中子 , 這三個仍然是零電荷 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以 , 這些載荷的模式不只漂亮 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	它們告訴我們 , 什麼是互動被允許發生的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四度空間中旋轉這個載荷空間 , 讓它更好地觀察強烈的交互作用 , 這個很好的六角形對稱 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強相互作用中 , 一個強力粒子 , 比如這個 , 會和有顏色的夸克互動 , 比如這個綠色的夸克 , 給一個夸克 , 用不同的顏色載荷這個紅色的顏色 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強相互作用每秒發生幾百萬次發生在我們身體的每一個原子裡 , 把原子核放在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四種載荷相對應三種力量並不是故事的結局
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們還可以再納入兩項載荷 , 對應到重力 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們納入這些 , 每個物質粒子都有兩個不同的旋轉載荷 , 旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以他們都分開了 , 在六度載荷空間中給予不錯的圖案 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間中旋轉這個圖案 , 看到它相當漂亮 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	此時此刻 , 這種模式符合我們目前對於大自然如何建造的最佳知識 , 在這些基本粒子的微小尺度下 。
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們肯定知道的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	其中的一些粒子在實驗的極限 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個模式 , 我們已經知道這些微小尺度的粒子物理學 。 宇宙如何用這些微小的尺度運作 , 是非常美麗的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要討論一些關於我們還未知的新古老想法 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要用數學單獨的擴展這個模式 , 看看我們能不能把手放在整個enchilada上 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想找到我們宇宙的所有粒子和力量 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想用這張圖來預測新的粒子 , 我們會看到何時實驗達到更高的能量 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	所以粒子物理學中有個古老的想法 , 這種已知的載荷模式 , 這種不太對稱的模式 , 會從一個更完美的模式中浮現出來 , 會和希格斯粒子如何打破電子化的模式 , 來給電磁化 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要用新的載荷方向來引進新的力量 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們引入一個新方向時 , 我們會猜測粒子的載荷是什麼 , 沿著這個方向進行轉動 , 然後我們可以和其他的粒子一起旋轉 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們明智地猜測 , 我們就能在六個載荷維度中建立標準載荷 , 把它當作是這個更完美的對稱 , 在七個載荷維度中 , 將這個更完美的圖案建構出來 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	這個特定的選擇對應於1973年由巴蒂和薩拉姆引發的一個大統一理論 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看這個新的統一模式時 , 我們可以看到幾個缺口 , 粒子似乎缺少了 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這是統一理論的運作方式 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	一個物理學家尋找更大、更對稱的圖案 , 包含了被建立的圖案 , 做為子物質 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	較大的模式能讓我們預測從未見過的粒子的存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這個統一模型預測了這兩種新力粒子的存在 , 它應該會像弱力一樣 , 只會變弱 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在我們可以在七度空間中旋轉這一組載荷 , 並考慮一個關於粒子的奇怪事實:物質的第二代和第三代 , 在六度載荷空間中有著完全一樣的載荷 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並非獨一無二的被它們的六個載荷給辨識出來 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們坐在標準載荷空間的對方位置 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 那我們就能把獨特的新載荷分配給每個粒子 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	然後我們可以在八度空間中旋轉 , 看看整個圖案是什麼樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	這裡我們可以看到第二代和第三代的物質 , 與第一代的對稱性有關 , 叫做 「 試驗性 」 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	在八度空間中這種特殊的載荷模式其實是數學中最美麗的幾何結構之一 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	它是最大的例外小組 , e8 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊言團體是平滑、曲線的形狀有248個維度
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	圖案中的每一點都對應到這個非常複雜且美麗的形狀的對稱性 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	e8形狀的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論中的彎曲時空 , 解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	和量子力學一起 , 這個形狀的幾何學可以描述所有關於宇宙如何在最小的尺度下運作的一切 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這種形狀生活在八度載荷空間中的圖案 , 非常美麗 , 它總結了上千種可能的互動 , 在這些基本粒子之間的相互作用 , 每一個都只是這個複雜形狀的一個面向 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們旋轉它時 , 我們可以看到許多其他錯綜複雜的圖案 , 包含在這個當中 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	有了特定的旋轉 , 我們可以沿著對稱軸來往下看這個圖案 , 同時看到所有的粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	這是個非常美麗的物體 , 和任何統一一樣 , 我們可以看到一些空洞 , 在那裡 , 新粒子需要這種模式 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	新粒子應該有20個缺口 , 其中兩個缺口已經被派塔拉姆粒子給填滿了 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從它們在這個圖案中的位置 , 我們知道這些新粒子應該是比如希格斯粒子 , 但有顏色充電 , 和強力互動 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填入這些新粒子完成了這個圖案 , 給了我們完整的e8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8圖案有著很深的數學根 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	被許多人認為是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這個偉大數學美麗的物體可以描述粒子互動的真相以最小尺度來描述
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	自然界被數學所描述的這個想法並不是全新的想法 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	1623年 , 伽利略寫了這句話: 「 大自然的大本書 , 它不斷地展開我們的眼睛 , 用數學的語言寫著 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形 , 和其他幾何圖形 , 沒有它 , 人類是不可能理解它的單一個字 ; 若沒有這些 , 就會有一個人在黑暗的迷宮中徘徊 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的 , 我曾試著遵循伽利略的指導以描述粒子物理學的數學只用三角形、圓形和其他幾何圖形來描述 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當其他物理學家和我真的在研究這個東西時 , 數學可以和黑暗迷宮相似 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但 , 讓人放心的是 , 這個數學的核心是純粹、美麗的幾何學 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	和量子力學一起 , 這個數學把我們的宇宙描述成一個正在成長的e8珊瑚 , 有粒子在每個地方互動 , 根據一個美麗的圖案 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	隨著更多的模式出現 , 使用像大型強子對撞機的新機器 , 我們或許可以看出大自然是否使用這種e8圖案 , 或是不一樣的圖案 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個發現的過程是一場美好的冒險 , 可以參與其中 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc找到符合e8圖案的粒子那會非常、非常酷
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc找到新的粒子 , 但它們不符合這個圖案 , 那會非常有趣 , 但不適合這個e8理論 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我來說是不好的 。
now how bad would that be ?	那會有多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 很不好 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但 , 預測大自然如何運作是很冒險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論和其它類似的理論是長期拍攝的
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	一個人做了很多努力 , 知道大部份這些想法可能最後不會成真 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	理論物理學就是這樣:有很多的野生動物 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新的物理理論很像新創公司 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	就如同任何大型投資一樣 , 在不做研究時 , 很難放棄一行研究 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學上 , 如果某樣東西沒有用 , 你就得要把它丟出去 , 去試試別的 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	現在 , 維持理智和達到快樂的唯一方法 , 在這個不確定性中 , 就是在人生中保持平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我已經盡我所能過著平衡的生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著在物理、愛和衝浪中平衡我自己的三個載荷方向 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	這樣一來 , 即使我所研究的物理現象一無是處 , 我仍然知道我過著美好的生活 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著住在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	在過去的十年 , 我住在毛伊島 , 一個非常美麗的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	現在是宇宙中最偉大的謎團之一 , 對我父母來說 , 我要如何在沒有參與過任何和全職工作的情況下 , 才能存活下來 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我要讓你們知道那個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在毛伊島的家辦公室的景象 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能已經注意到這些美麗的景象很相似 , 但在稍微不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為這曾經是我在毛伊島的家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我已經選擇了很不尋常的生活 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不用擔心房租讓我花時間做我愛的事 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	過著遊牧民族的存在 , 有時是很困難的 , 但它讓我可以在美麗的地方生活 , 並保持平衡 , 在我的人生中 , 讓我很滿意 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它讓我可以花很多時間在外頭 , 用超智能的珊瑚 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級聰明人的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	所以我很高興能在這裡受邀來ted演講 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我大概了解其中的2% , 但我仍然很喜歡 。 所以我要聽起來很傻 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你對萬物的理論嘉瑞特•里西:我習慣珊瑚
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克:沒錯 。 它之所以有少數人至少很興奮 , 是因為 , 如果你是對的 , 它會把引力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以 , 你是不是說 , 我們應該把宇宙看成是宇宙中最小的事物 , 不知怎麼的 , 就是e8的可能性 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 在最小的尺度上 , 會不會有規模 ? 還是...
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	講者:嗯 , 現在我給你們看的圖案 , 與我們所知的基本粒子物理學有關 , 已經對應到非常美麗的形狀 。
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	這就是我所說的我們肯定知道的 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	那個形狀和它符合e8圖案的方式非常相似 , 可能就是圖片的其他部分 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我給你們看過的這些點的圖案 , 實際上代表了這個高維物體的對稱性 , 它會在我們所經歷的時空中扭曲、移動、跳舞 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	那就是解釋我們看到的所有這些基本粒子 。
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克里斯:但是一個弦理論家 , 正如我所理解的 , 用比較小的弦來解釋電子 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論在裡面震動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們該如何看待電子在e8中 , 與電子的關係 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	格林:不 , 它會是這個e8形狀的對稱之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 當這個形狀在時空中移動時 , 它會扭轉 。 當它移動時 , 它會扭轉我們所看到的粒子 。 克里斯:e8形狀的大小 , 它和電子的關係如何 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	對於我的照片 , 我覺得我需要這些 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	更大嗎 ? 更小嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	講者:嗯 , 據我們所知 , 電子是點粒子 , 所以這會降到最小的可能性 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以 , 這些東西在量子場理論中被解釋的方式是 , 所有可能性都會同時擴大和發展 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這就是為什麼我會用珊瑚的類比 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	如此一來 , e8的出現方式就是它會成為一個在時空中每一處附著的形狀 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	正如我所說 , 形狀扭轉方向時 , 形狀會扭轉 , 因為它在曲面上移動 , 就是基本粒子本身 。
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	所以 , 透過量子場理論 , 它們會把自己當作點來表現 , 並以那樣的方式互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我能不能再說清楚 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克:真的不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它喚起了一種奇妙的感覺 , 我當然也想了解更多這種感覺 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	但非常謝謝你來到這裡 , 這絕對是很吸引人的 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳奇性的黑猩猩研究者珍•古德曾談過塔可爾和她的其他社區計畫 , 這些計畫協助促進非洲小鎮的人與受到威脅的動物共存 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、靈長類、科學等 ,
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍•古德能幫助人類和動物一起生活 。
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 等等 。
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以去 , jambo , jambo , abend , bonsoir , 但我們也可以--oh , ooh , oooh , ooh , oooh , oooh , oooh , oooh 。
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	那是黑猩猩在晚上睡前所發出的叫聲 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽到它從山谷的一端傳到另一端 , 從一群巢穴傳到下一群 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	今天晚上我想收集我的演講 , 來自昨天傑里離開的地方 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他談到這個驚人、三歲的南方古猿孩童 , selam 。
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽說過人類透過dna側寫的歷史、家庭樹 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	這是一位古生物學家 , 已故的路易斯.勒基 , 他讓我走上研究黑猩猩的路 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	當時還蠻特別的 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	現在有點常見 , 但他的論點是因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	你可以從化石中得知非常多的樣子 , 從肌肉附著物的形狀 , 看出它們是如何生活在各種人造物身上 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但它們的行為呢 ? 這就是他想知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為不會化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張且現在是一個相當普遍的理論 , 如果我們在我們最接近的生長親戚中發現行為模式 , 或相同的行為模式 , 現今的人類 , 那麼 , 也許那些行為出現在人猿身上 , 七百萬年前的人類祖先身上 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們把這些特徵從古老的過去帶給了我們 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你去看現今處理人類演化的教科書 , 你通常會發現人們在推測早期人類的行為 , 根據黑猩猩的行為來推測 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	它們和我們一樣 , 比起其他活生生生的生物 , 我們在這個ted會議中也聽說過 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以 , 我仍然要評論黑猩猩和我們很像的方式 , 在某些方面的行為 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每隻黑猩猩都有自己的個性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我給了他們名字 。 他們可以活到六十年以上 , 雖然我們認為大部分的人可能不會在野外生存到六十歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	沃茲爾先生 。 雌猩猩在11或12歲時 , 生了她的第一個寶寶 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	那裡 , 她每五、六年就有一個嬰兒 , 一個長時間的童年依賴期 , 當孩子在護理時 , 晚上和母親同睡 , 然後背著 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信 , 這種長期的童年對黑猩猩來說很重要 , 就像我們在學習時期一樣 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在演化過程中變得更加複雜 , 以不同形式的動物 , 我們發現學習在個體的生命歷史中扮演著更重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	而年輕的黑猩猩花很多時間觀察他們的長輩做了什麼 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道他們有能力模仿他們看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 以這種方式 , 不同工具的行為 , 在所有不同黑猩猩族群中 , 已經在非洲研究過這些行為 , 如何從一個世代傳承到下一個世代 , 透過觀察、模仿和實踐 , 這樣我們才能把這些工具的行為描述成原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有口語語言 。 我們已經談過了 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	它們的確有著非常豐富的姿勢和姿勢 , 其中有許多是相似的 , 甚至是相同的 , 以相同的形式呈現 , 形成在相同的情境中 。 迎接黑猩猩 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	他們也會親吻、握手、拍背對方 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	然後牠們游動然後丟石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩社會中 , 我們發現許多同情心的例子 , 前往愛和真正的利他主義 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 他們和我們一樣有著黑暗的天性 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	他們有能力極端殘暴 , 甚至一種原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	而這些非常具侵略性的行為 , 大部分的情況下 , 都會被指引去對抗鄰國社會團體的個體 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	它們非常具侵略性 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	比起其他生物 , 我相信黑猩猩 , 比起任何其他生物 , 都能幫助我們了解 , 畢竟 , 人類和動物世界之間並沒有一條尖銳的線條 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這是一條非常模糊的線 , 隨著我們更加觀察 , 它越來越模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我在1960年開始的研究至今仍持續著 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	而這些黑猩猩 , 生活在野外的複雜的社會生活中 , 幫助了我們認識到我們是其中的一部分 , 卻不分開 , 和我們共享這個星球的那些令人驚奇的動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 很讓人傷心的是 , 像世界上許多其他生物一樣 , 正在失去牠們的棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是一張從空中拍攝的照片 , 它向你展示了岡貝的森林高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	大約16年前 , 我飛越了整個區域 , 發現在公園之外 , 這片森林 , 在1960年 , 這片森林已經幾乎沒有破裂 , 沿著坦肯尼卡湖的東岸 , 那是那小小的 , 30平方公園的位置 , 那是我心目中的一個問題 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何拯救這些知名的黑猩猩 , 當居住在國家公園附近的人們在掙扎求生存時 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	居住的比土地還多 , 可能可以支援更多人 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	難民數量的增加 , 來自布羅威尼 , 和來自剛果的湖數 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	非常貧窮的人他們買不起其他地方的食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致了一項計畫 , 我們稱之為 「 塔可 」 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	用一種非常全面的方式來改善居住在公園附近村莊的人們的生活 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	由12個村莊開始 。 現在已經24歲了 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間深入探討它 , 但它包含了像樹木護理 , 最適合耕作的方法 , 現在 , 最適合耕作方式 , 幾乎像沙漠一樣的土地 , 落在這些山區 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制的方法 , 預防土壤侵蝕
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	重新找回過度使用的農地 , 這樣在兩年內 , 他們就能再次生產 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	努力協助村民從井裡取得淡水 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	或許建造一些學校教室
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 和一小群婦女合作 , 提供小額貸款的機會 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	我們得到了 , 就如同全世界的案例 , 大約有95%的貸款返回 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦予女性權力 , 與教育一起工作 , 為女孩提供獎學金 , 讓他們能完成中學 , 清楚了解到 , 在世界各地 , 隨著女性教育的改善 , 家庭規模的改善 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供關於家庭計劃和愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	這個計畫的結果是 , 保育有一些事情正在發生 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保育的現況是 , 居住在這24個村莊的農夫 , 而不是把我們當成一群白人來研究一大群猴子 , 順便一提 , 許多工作人員現在是坦尚尼亞人 , 但當我們開始塔卡爾計劃時 , 卻是坦尚尼亞隊員進入村落 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是一個坦尚尼亞隊伍和村民對話 , 問問他們有興趣什麼 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育感興趣嗎 ? 絕對不是 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康很有興趣 ; 他們對教育很有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間持續下去 , 當他們的情況開始改善時 , 他們開始更了解保育的需求 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解 , 隨著山坡的上層層被樹木給摧毀 , 所以你有這可怕的土壤侵蝕和泥土 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在開發所謂的更大型的岡貝生態系統 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這是在國家公園以外的地方 , 延伸到非常退化的土地上 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	當這些村莊有更好的生活水準時 , 他們其實是同意將百分之十到二十的土地放到高地之外 , 這樣一來 , 當樹木長回來時 , 黑猩猩就會有葉片走廊 , 牠們可以在國家公園以外的其他遺傳可行性族群互動 。
so tacare is a success .	所以tacare是成功的 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們在非洲的其他地方複製它 , 其他的荒野地區面臨到極端的人口壓力 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 非洲的問題 , 如同我們在ted的前幾天一直在討論的 , 都是重大的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	有很大一部分的貧窮
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你有大量居住的土地 , 沒有那麼肥沃 , 尤其是當你砍樹 , 把土壤開放到風力侵蝕 , 因為絕望的族群砍伐了越來越多的樹木 , 這樣他們就能嘗試為自己和家人種食物 , 會發生什麼事 ? 一定要給予什麼 。
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	不只是非洲的問題 , 還有其他發展中國家的問題 , 的確 , 到處都是 , 我們對地球做了什麼事 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道的 , 著名的科學家e.o.wilson說 , 如果地球上每一個人都能依據歐洲或美國人的平均生活標準來看 , 我們需要三個新星球 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	今天 , 他們說四個 。 但我們沒有他們 。 我們只有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	發生了什麼事 ? 我的意思是 , 這個問題是 , 在這裡 , 可說是走過地球最聰明的生物 , 帶著這個卓越的大腦 , 能夠由這些ted會議闡述的科技 , 然而我們卻在破壞我們唯一的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民 , 在他們做出重大決定之前 , 常常會坐下來問自己: 「 這個決定如何影響我們現在的七代人 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	現今 , 重大的決策──我並不是特別在談非洲 , 而是已開發國家──有數百萬美元的重大決策 , 數百萬人 , 通常會根據 「 這會如何影響到下一次股東會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	而這些決定會影響非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始環遊非洲 , 談到黑猩猩所面臨的問題 , 以及牠們消失的森林 , 我了解到 , 非洲的許多問題 , 會越來越多 , 能夠解決以前殖民地剝削的問題 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始在非洲外旅行 , 在歐洲演說 , 在美國演說 , 去亞洲 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都有這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	你們知道我在說的那種 , 我說的污染
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣通常會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水資源也許是本世紀中我們要面對的最關鍵的議題之一 , 隨處可見的水受到農業、工業及家庭化學物質污染 , 這些化學物質仍然被世界各地噴灑 , 看似無能為力從過去的經驗中獲利 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林正在被砍伐 ; 像海嘯之類的影響會越來越嚴重 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們已經談過土壤侵蝕
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們和其他溫室氣體一起燃燒化石燃料 , 沒有魯莽的燃燒 , 所以 , 導致氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 在世界各地 , 人們開始相信 , 我們的氣候發生了一些非常錯誤的事 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	世界各地的氣候都混雜在一起 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	而且是那些受影響較嚴重的窮人
it's africa that already is affected .	是非洲已經受到影響 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉沙漠以南非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱情況更糟糕 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨來臨時 , 它經常會導致洪水 , 加上苦惱 , 以及貧窮、飢餓和疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	而生活在土地無法支撐的地區 , 貧窮到無法買食物 , 無法搬離的地區 , 因為整片土地已經被降解 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以你在樹木被砍伐時 , 會得到沙漠化、令人毛骨悚然 ,
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	而這種東西不只在非洲 , 遍佈全世界 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 我並不意外 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇到許多年輕人 , 他們似乎失去了希望 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為在這個特別聰明的大腦之間 , 會不會有某種隔閡 ? 那種ted科技所展現出來的大腦 , 而人類的心 ? 用非科學的角度來說 , 用愛和同情的角度來說 , 會不會有某種隔閡 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	而這些年輕人 , 當我和他們談話時 , 基本上他們不是憂鬱症 , 就是冷漠 , 或痛苦 , 或憤怒 。 他們說 , 或多或少是一樣的 , 「 我們有這種感覺 , 因為我們覺得你已經妥協了我們的未來 , 且我們無能為力 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經妥協了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每當我看著他們 , 我想我們是如何傷害這個美麗的星球 , 從我年紀開始 , 我就感受到這個絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	這就導致了這個計畫 , 我們稱它為根與芽 , 它始於坦尚尼亞 , 現在散播到全世界97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	這是象徵性的 。 根製造堅定的基礎 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	射線看起來似乎很小 ; 要到太陽──它們能穿過磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆視為我們在地球上所面臨的所有問題 , 環境和社會問題 。 這是希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	世界各地成千上萬的年輕人都可以突破 , 可以為所有生物創造一個更美好的世界 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根與芽的最重要的訊息是:我們每一個人都做出改變 , 每一天都一樣 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有一個選擇 。 在座的每一個人 , 我們都有選擇要做出什麼樣的改變 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	窮人別無選擇 , 而是我們要改變事情 , 讓窮人也有選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根與芽的團體都選擇了三個計畫 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	這取決於他們年紀多大 , 以及哪個國家 , 不論他們是在城市或鄉村 , 不論是哪種計畫 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們現在有從幼兒園到大學的計畫 , 有越來越多的成人開始他們自己的根與芽的團體 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	而每一個團體在他們之間選擇 , 三種不同的計畫 , 讓這個世界變得更美好 , 意識到所有這些不同的問題都互相連結 , 互相影響 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	所以他們其中一個計畫是幫助自己的人類社群 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	然後 , 如果他們能夠的話 , 他們可能會募到錢來幫助世界其他地方的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	他們的計畫之一是幫助動物不只是野生動物、家居動物 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	他們的其中一個計畫是幫助我們共同的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	這一切都是學習在和平和和諧中生活的訊息 , 在我們的家庭、我們的社區、國家、文化之間、宗教和自然世界之間的訊息 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然的世界 。 我們不能以我們現有的速度去摧毀它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們沒有比這個星球還多 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	只要在非洲挑選一兩個項目 , 即根與槍擊團體正在進行的項目 , 一兩個項目只在坦尚尼亞、烏干達、肯亞、南非、剛果拉茲維爾、獅子山、喀麥隆和其他團體 。 如我所說的 , 它在世界上97個國家中 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們種植樹木 , 種植有機蔬菜
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營工作 , 和雞販賣雞蛋 , 為了少量的錢 , 或只是用它們來餵飽他們的家人 , 並感受到自豪和賦權 , 因為他們不再無助 , 依賴他人用他們的蔬菜和雞肉 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它被用在烏干達 , 給予一些心理上的幫助 , 來實現士兵的幫助 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	做像這樣的計畫 , 把它們自己帶出來 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次 , 他們是社會上有用的成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們也在監獄裡有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以 , 現在沒有時間有更多的根與芽 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但喔 , 他們也致力於愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	那是根與芽的重要要素 , 有著較年長的孩子和較年輕的孩子對話 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	而不需要懷孕之類的 , 年輕人從其他年輕聽得更好 , 而不是成年人聽得更好 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 。 這就是我在世界各地被問的問題: 「 珍 , 你看過這麼多可怕的東西 , 你看過你的黑猩猩數量從一百萬隻 , 到一百五十萬隻 , 和許多其他動物一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失了 , 曾經有森林的沙漠
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? 」 嗯 , 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能來參加像ted這樣的會議 , 沒有希望 , 你能嗎 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 還有希望 。 其中一個是這個了不起的人類大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	我的意思是 , 想想科技 。
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	我非常興奮 , 最後 , 來到談堆肥式廁所的人面前 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	它是我的一個嗜好者 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們只要把這些水沖下梯 , 水就很糟了 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	接著談到再生能源極為重要 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們是否關心地球給我們的孩子 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	我們有多少人有孩子或孫子、姪女、姪子 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們在乎他們的未來嗎 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們關心他們的未來 , 我們身為世界各地的菁英 , 我們可以做些什麼 。 我們可以做出選擇 , 選擇我們每天如何生活 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買什麼、穿什麼、
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	而選擇用問題來做出這些選擇 , 這會如何影響我周遭的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	在他或她長大之後 , 會如何影響我孩子的生命 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或是我的孫子 , 或其它的
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	所以 , 人類的大腦 , 和人類的心結合 , 我們加入世界各地 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	這就是ted的幫助 , google也幫助我們 , esri也幫我們繪製了gmbe國家公園的地圖 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有這些我們可以使用的科技
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在我們把它們連結起來 , 已經開始發生了 , 不是嗎 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	你們今天下午已經聽說過了 , 這已經開始發生了 。
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這種改變 , 這種改變 。 若我們關心未來 , 我們就必須要有所改變 。
