and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	下一個原因 , 希望大自然是驚人的韌性 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以把一個完全被摧毀的區域 , 只要時間 , 或許還能協助它再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	其中一個例子是塔卡爾計畫 。
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我告訴過你 , 看似死去的樹木 , 如果你不再把它們當火燒掉 , 你不需要因為你有很多木頭 , 那麼五年內 , 你就可以有一棵三十英呎長的樹 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	而動物 , 幾乎在滅絕的邊緣 , 可以得到第二次機會 。 這是我的下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	這很鼓舞人心 。 這也帶給我最後一類的希望 , 在過去的兩天中 , 我們聽到了這麼多關於這一點:這種不屈不撓的人類精神 。 這種對人類精神的堅定決 , 人類精神的韌性 , 如此一來 , 那些你認為會被貧窮、疾病、或疾病給打擊的人們 , 有時會被用在手上 , 帶著他們的一部分 , 帶著他們在社會上的一部分 , 帶著他們在改變世界的一部分 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	想想看 , 一兩個離開非洲的人 , 真的很鼓舞人心 。
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以做一份很長的清單 , 但很明顯的 , 曼德拉 , 來自17年辛苦的體力勞工 , 23年的監禁 , 有著這驚人的寬恕的能力 , 讓他能帶領他的國家走出種族隔離的邪惡政權 , 沒有血庫 。
ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	kensarowiwa , 在奈及利亞 , 他接下了巨大的石油公司 , 雖然全世界各地的人都竭盡所能 , 但卻處決了 。
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人如此激勵人心 。
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人 , 是非洲年輕人所需的榜樣 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	我們也需要一些環保的榜樣 , 我今天已經聽過其中一些 。
so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	所以我很感謝這個機會再次分享這個訊息 , 和ted的每個人 。
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望我們之中的一些人能聚在一起討論這些事情 , 特別是根與芽的計畫 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	最後一個詞是這整個會議中心的年輕女子 , 我今天見到她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她非常興奮 , 有了她的認證 。 她的根與芽 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她在daressalaam的領導階層
she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說幫助她做她正在做的事
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	我非常非常興奮 , 能見到她 , 看到一個年輕人 , 當他們被賦予權力的例子 , 因為有機會採取行動 , 讓世界變得更美好 , 真正是我們明天的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家dancohen分享了一些關於海洋和我們生活中的塑膠污染的艱難事實還有一些關於如何解放塑膠漩渦的想法
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色、任務藍色、海洋、塑膠等 ,
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	黛安娜•柯恩:關於塑膠污染的艱難真相 。
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是視覺藝術家 , 我也是塑膠污染聯盟的共同創辦人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我一直在和塑膠袋合作 , 我把這些塑膠袋剪下來 , 縫合在一起 , 過去二十年間 , 我的藝術作品的主要材料 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成二和三維的作品 , 雕塑和裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	在與塑膠共事八年後 , 我有些作品開始裂縫 , 分解成更小的塑膠碎片 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 太好了 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	和我們一樣是短暫的 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	在我更進一步的教育塑膠方面 , 我其實意識到這是件壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	塑膠會分解成小塊 , 因為它總是塑膠的 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們發現很多在海洋環境中
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	接著 , 在過去幾年中 , 我學到了太平洋垃圾貼片和垃圾漩渦 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	我的初步反應和我認為這是很多人對學習的第一反應就是: 「 天啊 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們得去外面清理這個東西 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以 , 我真的開發了一個提案 , 要用一艘貨櫃船出去 , 還有兩艘退役的漁船、一架起重機、一台跳速機 , 以及一台冷卻機 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	我的意圖是 , 出門去蓋房 , 提高對於這個議題的認知 , 並開始拿起塑膠 , 把塑膠做成小塊和冷的模板 , 可以用在被開發出來的社區中 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始和實際去過河岸的人談話 , 研究海洋環境中的塑膠問題 , 到此為止 , 我了解到 , 將它清理成一個很小的桶子 , 相對於每天在世界各地生產的量 , 實際上我需要回頭看看更大的照片 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更大的原因是:我們需要找到一個方法來關掉水龍頭 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要切斷單一次使用和丟棄塑膠的噴霧劑 , 每天都要進入海洋環境 , 以全球性的規模來看 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	所以 , 看著這一點 , 我也了解到 , 我真的很生氣 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不只關心塑膠 , 你還想想像在太平洋中間 , 我所學到的現在已經有11個塑膠漩渦 , 可能是世界上五大洋的塑膠 。
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	不只是那個我關心的塑膠垃圾漩渦--也是超市裡塑膠的漩渦 。
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超市 , 而我所有的食物都是用塑膠包裝的 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的飲料都是用塑膠包裝 , 即使在健康食物市場也一樣 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也關心冰箱裡的塑膠 , 我關心的是塑膠和毒素 , 從塑膠滲入我們體內 , 進入我們的體內 。
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我和一群其他人一起 , 他們都在探討這個議題 , 我們創立了塑膠污染聯盟 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有許多正在努力的倡議 , 但有些是非常基本的 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	一是:如果我們在海洋中發現的海底碎片中有80%到90%都是塑膠 , 那為什麼我們不稱它為什麼 。
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	回收每個人的書 , 都是關於 「 永續 」 和 「 綠化 」 的書 , 用的是回收的概念 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	你把某樣東西放進一個垃圾桶 , 不用再想了 。
what is the reality of that ?	那其中的現實是什麼 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 我們的塑膠回收率不到7% 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你真的深入研究它 , 特別是在塑膠瓶中 , 大部分只會下降 , 或發動 , 或運送到中國 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它會被循環 , 變成較少的東西 , 而玻璃瓶可以再次成為玻璃瓶 , 或者再次被使用 , 塑膠瓶永遠不會是塑膠瓶 。
so this is a big issue for us .	所以這對我們來說是個大問題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	另一件我們在看並要求人們去思考的事情是 , 我們在 「 減少、再利用、回收 」 的前面加入了第四個r , 那就是拒絕 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	每當可能 , 拒絕單純使用和丟棄的塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案存在 ; 有些是很古老的學者 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我現在正在收集這些很酷的畢氏容器 , 用它們來取代用它們 , 而不是用它們來儲存食物 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我正在為自己和我的家人做一項服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	很容易拿起一個不鏽鋼瓶或玻璃瓶 , 如果你在旅行 , 卻忘了帶著不鏽鋼瓶 , 用水或過濾水填充它 , 而不是買塑膠瓶的水 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我猜我想對在場的各位說 , 我知道你們對這個議題了解很多 , 那就是 , 這在海洋中是個很大的問題 , 但這是我們身為消費者所造成的問題 , 我們可以解決 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們可以藉由提高對問題的意識來解決這個問題 , 並教導人們選擇替代方案 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 無論何時可能 , 要選擇替代方案 , 來單純使用塑膠 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把這些浪潮分解到我們的海洋中 , 為此 , 拯救我們的海洋 , 拯救我們的地球 , 拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	這段影片來自麻省理工學院的pattiemaes的實驗室 , 由pranavfrotry推出的 , 是ted的buzzz 。 這是個可穿戴式裝置 , 配上一個投影機 , 可以鋪路來和我們環境互動 。 想像一下 「 少數民族報告 」 , 接著是一些 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	展示、設計、介面設計、科技
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	派蒂•馬斯和帕納•密特里第六音聖節 。
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我一直在想這個問題 , 我們是否能進化或發展出第六感 , 這種感覺會給我們無縫的取得和容易取得的代謝或資訊 , 可能存在於某個地方 , 可能是有相關的資訊 , 來協助我們做出正確的決定 , 決定我們即將要面對的一切 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	你們當中有些人可能會爭論 , 嗯 , 今天的手機不是已經做到了嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會說不 。
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted這裡遇見某人這是最頂尖的網絡地點 , 當然 , 在你不握某人的手時 , 然後說: 「 你能不能在我拿出手機google你 ? 」
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或當你去超市的時候 , 你站在那一大道不同類型的衛生紙上 , 你不會拿出你的手機 , 然後打開瀏覽器 , 去一個網站 , 試著決定哪些不同的衛生紙是最環保的購買工具 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以 , 我們沒有很容易取得所有相關的資訊 , 只能協助我們做出最佳決定 , 決定下一步要做什麼 , 以及要採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以 , 我在媒體實驗室的研究小組已經在開發一系列的發明 , 讓我們能輕易取得這些資訊 , 且不需要使用者改變他們的行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	我在這裡展開我們最新的努力 , 目前為止 , 最成功的努力 , 這個過程仍然是個工作 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	我現在穿著這個裝置 , 我們已經把它和架子上的零件拼湊在一起 , 順便說一句 , 此時此刻 , 只需350美元 。
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我穿著攝影機 , 只是個簡單的網路攝影機 , 一個可攜帶、電池充電的投影系統 , 上面有一面小鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些元件會在我的口袋裡通訊到我的手機 , 它的作用是通訊和計算設備 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在影片中 , 我們看到我的學生帕納拉夫失業 , 他真的是實施和設計這整個系統的天才 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們看到這個系統讓他走向任何表面 , 開始用他的雙手去和他前面投射的資訊互動 。
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	系統會追蹤四隻顯著的手指 。
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個例子中 , 他戴著你可能認得的簡單標記蓋子 。
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要比較時髦的版本 , 你也可以用不同的顏色來畫你的指甲 。
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	攝影機基本上追蹤了這四隻手指 , 並辨識出他製作的任何手勢 , 這樣他就可以去 , 比如說 , 一張長灘的地圖 , 放大 , 等等 。
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	系統也能辨識出具代表性的手勢 , 比如 「 拍照 」 手勢 , 然後拍下你面前的任何東西的照片 。
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	當他走回媒體實驗室時 , 他可以直接走到任何一面牆上 , 投射他拍攝的照片 , 將它們整理起來 , 等等 , 再用所有天然的手勢 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	所以 , 你們當中有些人很可能是兩年前 , 看到傑夫•漢的示範 , 或者有些人可能會想: 「 嗯 , 這不是看起來像微軟的表面桌嗎 ? 」
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	是的 , 你也用自然的手勢互動 , 雙手等等 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	但這裡的差別是 , 你可以用任何表面 , 你可以走到任何表面 , 包括你的手 , 如果沒有其他東西可以取得 , 並和這些投影的資料互動 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	這個裝置是完全可攜帶的 , 而且可以是......
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	所以 , 其中一個重要的差別是它完全是行動的 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	另一個更重要的不同是 , 在大量生產中 , 明天它不會比現在的手機要花更多的成本 , 實際上 , 包裝看起來不會比我在脖子上穿著的這個版本還時髦 。
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	但除非讓你們其中一些人活得像tomcruise在《少數報告》裡那樣酷炫的幻想 , 我們之所以會很興奮 , 是因為它真的能作為這第六感的設備之一 , 讓你能對眼前的事物有相關的資訊 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	我們看到帕納進入超市 , 購買一些紙巾 。
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起一個產品時 , 這個系統可以辨識出他拿起的產品 , 用的是圖像辨識或標記技術 , 給他綠光或橘色的燈光 。
he can ask for additional information .	他可以要求額外的資訊
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	所以 , 這裡的這個選擇是特別好的選擇 , 因為他個人的準則 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	在座有些人可能希望衛生紙有最白白的 , 而不是最環保的選擇 。
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡拿起一本書 , 他可以拿amazon評分 , 它會被投射在書的封面上 。
this is juan's book , our previous speaker , which gets a great rating , by the way , at amazon .	這是胡安的書 , 我們之前的講者 , 順帶一提 , 在亞馬遜的評價很棒 。
and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	所以 , 帕納把書的頁面翻轉了 , 接著 , 可以看到書本讀者留言的額外資訊 , 也許是他最愛的評論家所寫的評論 , 等等 。
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他轉到某個特定的頁面 , 他可能會找到我們朋友的註解 , 給他一點點額外的資訊 , 關於那一頁的任何事 。
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀報紙--它從來不需要過時 。
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你可以得到你正在閱讀的事件的影片註冊--你可以得到最新的體育分數等等 。
this is a more controversial one .	這是個比較有爭議的
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你在ted和某人互動時 , 也許你可以看到標籤上的一個字雲 , 和那個人在他們的部落格和個人網頁上的字詞有關 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這個案例中 , 學生對攝影機很感興趣 , 等等 。
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你前往機場的路上 , 如果你拿起你的登機經過 , 它可以告訴你 , 你的飛行遲緩了 , 大門改變了 , 等等 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	如果你需要知道當下的時機是什麼 , 就跟在你的手臂上畫手錶一樣簡單 。
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	這就是我們目前正在發展的第六感 , 讓我們能無縫接觸所有相關資訊 , 關於我們可能碰到的事物 。
my student pranav , who's really , like i said , the genius behind this .	我的學生帕納 , 像我說的 , 他是這背後的天才 。
he does deserve a lot of applause because i don't think he's slept much in the last three months , actually .	他的確值得鼓掌 , 因為我覺得他在過去三個月內睡得不多 。
and his girlfriend is probably not very happy about him either .	他的女朋友也可能對他不太高興 。
but it's not perfect yet , it's very much a work in progress .	但它還不完美 , 它是很大的進步 。
and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	誰知道 , 或許在十年內 , 我們將帶著終極第六感大腦植入人體 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	2001年9月11日 , 艾瑞斯•艾爾瓦菲有種強大的友誼 , 出生於無法想像的損失 。 羅德里格茲的兒子在世貿中心的攻擊事件中被殺害 ; 艾爾瓦菲的兒子zacariasmoussaoui被定罪於那些襲擊中的角色 , 並在期待找到和平 。 這兩個媽媽們漸漸漸漸漸漸開始了解和尊重彼此 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治、
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	9/11癒合:那些發現原諒、友情的母親們
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	斐利斯•羅德里格茲:我們今天在這裡 , 是因為我們有大多數人認為不尋常的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	然而 , 現在對我們來說卻很自然 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次發現我兒子在2001年9月11日的世貿中心
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們不知道他是否還在36小時後就死了 。
at the time , we knew that it was political .	當時 , 我們知道那是政治的 。
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們害怕我們的國家會如何以我們兒子的名義為名--我的丈夫 , 奧蘭多 , 我和我們的家人 。
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	當我看到它--然而 , 透過震驚 , 驚恐的震撼 , 以及我們生活中可怕的爆炸 , 真的 , 我們沒有復仇 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾個星期後 , zacariasmoussaoui被指控有六個數字的陰謀犯下恐怖主義 , 而美國政府向他索取了死刑 , 如果被定罪 , 我和我先生在公開場合反對 , 公開場合 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過這個和透過人權團體 , 我們和其他幾個受害者的家人聚在一起 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我在媒體上看到aicha , 當她的兒子被指示時 , 我心想: 「 多麼勇敢的女性 。
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	有一天我想見到那個女人當我更強壯的時候 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我還在深深的悲痛中 ; 我知道我沒有力量 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道有一天我會找到她 , 或是我們會找到對方 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當人們聽到我兒子是受害者時 , 我馬上得到同情 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們學到她的兒子被指控的話 , 她沒有得到同情 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她的痛苦和我一樣 。
so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	所以我們在2002年11月見面 , 艾卡現在會告訴你們這是怎麼一回事 。
aicha elwafi: good afternoon , ladies and gentlemen .	aichaelwafi:午安 , 各位先生女士 。
i am the mother of zacarias moussaoui .	我是zacariasmoussaoui的母親 。
and i asked the organization of human rights to put me in touch with the parents of the victims .	我要求人權組織讓我與受害者的父母接觸 。
so they introduced me to five families .	所以他們向我介紹了五個家庭 。
and i saw phyllis , and i watched her .	然後我看到了phyllis , 我看著她 ,
she was the only mother in the group .	她是群體中唯一的母親 。
the others were brothers , sisters .	其他人則是兄弟姊妹
and i saw in her eyes that she was a mother , just like me .	我在她的眼裡看到她是母親 , 就像我一樣 。
i suffered a lot as a mother .	身為母親 , 我遭受許多苦難 。
i was married when i was 14 .	我在14歲時結婚 。
i lost a child when i was 15 , a second child when i was 16 .	我十五歲時失去了一個孩子 , 第二個孩子 , 那時我十六歲 。
so the story with zacarias was too much really .	zacarias的故事實在太多了 。
and i still suffer , because my son is like he's buried alive .	而我仍然痛苦 , 因為我的兒子就像他被活埋一樣 。
i know she really cried for her son .	我知道她真的為她的兒子哭了 。
but she knows where he is .	但她知道他在哪裡 。
my son , i don't know where he is .	我的兒子 , 我不知道他在哪裡 。
i don't know if he's alive . i don't know if he's tortured .	我不知道他是否還活著 。 我不知道他是否遭受折磨 。
i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他發生了什麼事 。
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	這就是為什麼我決定要說我的故事 , 讓我的痛苦對其他女性也很正面 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	對所有的女人而言 , 所有能給予生命的媽媽 , 你可以回饋 , 你可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	由於我們是女性 , 因為我們是女性 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們一定要手牽手 , 一起做點什麼 。
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	不是對抗女性 , 而是對我們、我們女人、我們的孩子 。
i talk against violence , against terrorism .	我對抗暴力 , 對抗恐怖主義 。
i go to schools to talk to young , muslim girls so they don't accept to be married against their will very young .	我去學校和年輕、穆斯林女孩交談 , 讓他們不接受婚姻對抗她們的意志很年輕 。
so if i can save one of the young girls , and avoid that they get married and suffer as much as i did , well this is something good .	所以 , 如果我能拯救其中一個年輕女孩 , 並避免她們和我一樣結婚和受苦 , 嗯 , 這是好事 。
this is why i'm here in front of you .	這就是我在你們面前的原因 。
pr: i would like to say that i have learned so much from aicha , starting with that day we had our very first meeting with other family members which was a very private meeting with security , because it was november 2002 , and , frankly , we were afraid of the superpatriotism of that time in the country those of us family members .	pr:我想說我從aicha那學到了很多 , 從那天開始 , 我們第一次和其他家庭成員會面──那是非常私人的──和安全的會面 , 因為那是2002年11月 , 坦白說 , 我們害怕在那個國家中那個時代的超級多種族主義──我們這些家庭成員 。
but we were all so nervous .	但我們都好緊張 。
" why does she want to meet us ? "	「 她為什麼要和我們見面 ? 」
and then she was nervous .	接著 , 她很緊張 。
" why did we want to meet her ? "	「 我們為什麼會想見她 ? 」
what did we want from each other ?	我們對彼此渴望什麼 ?
before we knew each others' names , or anything , we had embraced and wept .	在我們知道彼此的名字 , 或任何東西之前 , 我們已經擁抱和哭泣了 。
then we sat in a circle with support , with help , from people experienced in this kind of reconciliation .	接著 , 我們圍坐在一個圈中 , 帶著支持、協助 , 從人們經歷過這種和解 。
and aicha started , and she said , " i don't know if my son is guilty or innocent , but i want to tell you how sorry i am for what happened to your families .	然後aicha開始 , 她說: 「 我不知道我兒子是有罪還是無辜 , 但我想告訴你們 , 我是多麼遺憾 , 為了你家裡發生的事 。
i know what it is to suffer , and i feel that if there is a crime , a person should be tried fairly and punished . "	我知道痛苦是什麼 , 我覺得如果有罪 , 一個人應該被公平地審判並處罰 。 」
but she reached out to us in that way , and it was , i'd like to say , it was an icebreaker .	但她用那樣的方式向我們伸出援手 , 我想說 , 那是一個冰箱 。
and what happened then is we all told our stories , and we all connected as human beings .	接下來發生的事 , 我們都說了我們的故事 , 我們都以人類的身分連結在一起 。
by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	到了下午的時候 , 大約是午餐後的三小時 , 我們覺得我們永遠都認識彼此 。
now what i learned from her , is a woman , not only who could be so generous under these present circumstances and what it was then , and what was being done to her son , but the life she's had .	我從她身上學到的 , 是一個女人 , 不僅可以在這些當下的情況下這麼慷慨 , 還有當時的狀況 , 還有她兒子的人生 , 還有她所擁有的人生 。
i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有遇過有這麼辛苦人生的人 , 從我自己的完全不同的文化和環境 。
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有一種特別的連結 , 我很珍視它 。
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我想這一切都是為了害怕他人 , 但踏出那一步 , 然後意識到: 「 嘿 , 這不是那麼難 。
who else can i meet that i don't know , or that i'm so different from ? "	我還能碰到誰 , 不知道我不知道 , 還是我和誰這麼不同 ? 」
so , aicha , do you have a couple of words for conclusion ?	所以 , aicha , 你有幾個字可以做結論嗎 ?
because our time is up .	因為我們的時間到了 。
aw: i wanted to say that we have to try to know other people , the other .	艾:我想說我們必須試著去認識其他人 , 另一個 。
you have to be generous , and your hearts must be generous , your mind must be generous .	你必須要慷慨 , 你的心一定要慷慨 , 你的心一定要慷慨 。
you must be tolerant .	你一定要寬容 。
you have to fight against violence .	你必須對抗暴力 。

this is what i wanted to say .	這是我想說的 。
too much of the world lacks access to clean drinking water . engineer michael pritchard did something about it inventing the portable lifesaver filter , which can make the most revolting water drinkable in seconds . an amazing demo from tedglobal 2009 .	世界上太多缺乏乾淨的飲用水 。 工程師麥可.普立查做了些事情 , 發明了可攜式的生活水手過濾器 , 能在幾秒鐘內讓水喝得最好 。 2009年tedglobal的一個驚人的示範 。

i'd like to talk about a couple of things today .	今天我想談談幾件事 。
the first thing is water .	第一件事是水 。
now i see you've all been enjoying the water that's been provided for you here at the conference , over the past couple of days .	現在我看到你們都很享受在研討會上提供的水 , 在過去的幾天裡 ,
and i'm sure you'll feel that it's from a safe source .	我相信你們會覺得這是從安全的來源
but what if it wasn't ?	但如果不是這樣呢 ?
what if it was from a source like this ?	如果是從像這樣的源頭來的呢 ?
then statistics would actually say that half of you would now be suffering with diarrhea .	接著 , 統計數字會說你們當中有一半的人會因為腹瀉而受苦 。
i talked a lot in the past about statistics , and the provision of safe drinking water for all .	過去我談了很多關於統計 , 以及為所有人提供安全飲用水的條例 。
but they just don't seem to get through .	但它們似乎沒有通過 。
and i think i've worked out why .	我想我已經想出了原因 。
it's because , using current thinking , the scale of the problem just seems too huge to contemplate solving .	這是因為 , 用目前的思考 , 問題的規模似乎太大了 , 無法去思考解決 。
so we just switch off: us , governments and aid agencies .	所以我們只關掉:我們 , 政府和援助機構 。
well , today , i'd like to show you that through thinking differently , the problem has been solved .	今天 , 我想讓你們知道 , 透過不同的思考 , 問題已經被解決了 。
by the way , since i've been speaking , another 13 , 000 people around the world are suffering now with diarrhea .	順帶一提 , 自從我開始演講之後 , 世界上有一萬三千人現在正遭受腹瀉的苦難 。
and four children have just died .	而四個孩子剛剛過世 。
i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了lifesaver濾水瓶 , 因為我生氣了 。
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我和大部分人一樣 , 在2004年聖誕節過後的隔天 , 當我在看亞洲海嘯爆發的毀滅性新聞 , 在電視上播放 。
the days and weeks that followed , people fleeing to the hills , being forced to drink contaminated water or face death .	之後的日子 , 人們逃到山丘上 , 被迫喝下被污染的水 , 或面對死亡 。
that really stuck with me .	那真的很困擾我 。
then , a few months later , hurricane katrina slammed into the side of america .	接著 , 幾個月後 , 卡崔娜颶風危入美國的邊緣 。
" okay , " i thought , " here's a first world country , let's see what they can do . "	「 好吧 , 」 我心想: 「 這裡是第一個世界國家 , 咱們來看看他們能做什麼 。 」
do you know it took five days to get water to the superdome ?	你知道要花五天才能讓水到超級其間嗎 ?
people were shooting each other on the streets for tv sets and water .	人們在街上互相槍擊電視機和水 。
that's when i decided i had to do something .	那時我決定我得要做點什麼 。
now i spent a lot of time in my garage , over the next weeks and months , and also in my kitchen much to the dismay of my wife .	現在我花了很多時間在我的車庫 , 在接下來的幾週、幾個月 , 在我的廚房裡 , 也常常讓我太太失望 。
however , after a few failed prototypes , i finally came up with this , the lifesaver bottle .	然而 , 在幾次失敗的原型之後 , 我終於想到了這個 , 救星瓶 。
okay , now for the science bit .	好了 , 現在對科學一點點
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在lifesaver之前 , 最好的手過濾器只能過濾到大約200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌大約是200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以一個200奈米的細菌將會穿過一個200奈米大的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面 , 最小的病毒大約是25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	所以那肯定會穿過那200奈米的洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	生命安全氣孔是15奈米 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以 , 沒有任何東西能穿透 。
okay , i'm going to give you a bit of a demonstration .	好 , 我要給你們一些示範 。
would you like to see that ?	各位想看一下嗎 ?
i spent all the time setting this up , so i guess i should .	我花了很多時間設定這個設定 , 所以我猜我應該要
we're in the fine city of oxford .	我們在牛津的美好城市裡
so someone's done that up .	有人這樣做 。
fine city of oxford , so what i've done is i've gone and got some water from the river cherwell , and the river thames , that flow through here . and this is the water .	美好的牛津城 , 我所做的是 , 我去了一些河流的水 , 還有河流 , 流過這裡 。 這就是水 。
but i got to thinking , you know , if we were in the middle of a flood zone in bangladesh , the water wouldn't look like this .	但我得想 , 如果我們在孟加拉的洪水區中間 , 水不會像這樣 。
so i've gone and got some stuff to add into it .	所以 , 我去了一些東西 , 來加點東西 。
and this is from my pond .	而這是從我的池塘來的 。
have a smell of that , mister cameraman .	聞一下攝影師的味道 。
we're just going to pour that in there .	我們只會把它倒進去 。
michael pritchard: okay . we've got some runoff from a sewage plant farm .	michaelpritchard:好的 。 我們從污水廠的農場取得了一些跑步 。

the lifesaver bottle works really simply .	lifesaver濾水瓶的運作非常簡單 。
you just scoop the water up .	你只要把水潑上去 ,
today i'm going to use a jug just to show you all . let's get a bit of that poo in there .	今天我要用一顆評判來向你們展示 。 讓我們來看看那裏的一大便 。
that's not dirty enough . let's just stir that up a little bit .	這樣還不夠髒 。 讓我們稍微攪拌一下 。
okay , so i'm going to take this really filthy water , and put it in here . do you want a drink yet ?	好了 , 所以我要把這個非常骯髒的水放在這裡 。 你還想喝嗎 ?
okay . there we go .	好的 。 開始了 。
give it a few pumps . okay ?	給它幾個幫浦 。 好嗎 ?
that's all that's necessary .	這一切都是必要的 。
now as soon as i pop the teat , sterile drinking water is going to come out .	一旦我把茶吃掉 , 無菌的飲用水就會跑出來 。
i've got to be quick . okay , ready ?	我得快點了 。 好 , 準備好了嗎 ?
there we go . mind the electrics .	開始了 , 注意電流 。
that is safe , sterile drinking water .	那是安全的、無菌的飲用水 。
there you go chris .	你去了克里斯 。

let's see chris's program throughout the rest of the show . okay ?	我們來看看克里斯在節目的其他部分 。 好嗎 ?
okay . lifesaver bottle is used by thousands of people around the world .	好的 。 世界各地成千上萬的人使用lifesaver濾水瓶 。
it'll last for 6 , 000 liters .	它會持續延續六千公升 。
and when it's expired , using failsafe technology , the system will shut off , protecting the user .	當它過期時 , 使用失敗安全的技術 , 系統會關閉 , 保護使用者 。
pop the cartridge out . pop a new one in .	把帶狀物丟出去 , 再放一個新的 。
it's good for another 6 , 000 liters .	對另外六千公升有益 。
so let's look at the applications .	所以 , 我們來看看應用程式 。
traditionally , in a crisis , what do we do ?	傳統上 , 在危機中 , 我們該怎麼做 ?
then , after a few weeks , we set up camps .	接著 , 幾週後 , 我們設立營地 。
and people are forced to come into the camps to get their safe drinking water .	而人們被迫進入營地以取得安全的飲用水 。
what happens when 20 , 000 people congregate in a camp ?	當兩萬人聚集在難民營時 , 會發生什麼事 ?
diseases spread . more resources are required .	疾病傳播 。 需要更多的資源 。
the problem just becomes selfperpetuating .	問題只會變成自我發展 。
but by thinking differently , and shipping these , people can stay put .	但藉由不同的思考 , 以及運送這些 , 人們可以保持置身事外 。
they can make their own sterile drinking water , and start to get on with rebuilding their homes and their lives .	他們可以自製無菌的飲用水 , 開始重建他們的家園和生活 。
now , it doesn't require a natural disaster for this to work .	現在 , 這不需要自然災害才能成功 。
using the old thinking , of national infrastructure and pipe work , is too expensive .	使用舊思維 , 國家基礎設施和管子的工作 , 實在太昂貴了 。
when you run the numbers on a calculator , you run out of noughts .	當你在計算機上運行數字 , 你就會跑出 「 沒問題 」 。
so here is the " thinking different " bit .	這就是 「 思考 」 的部分 。
instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	與其運送水源 , 和使用人造過程來完成它 , 讓我們使用大自然 。 她有一個絕佳的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從那裡取水 , 免費地把它運送到那邊 , 然後把它丟到山上、河流上 , 和溪流上 。
and where do people live ? near water .	而人們住在哪裡 ? 靠近水源 。
all we've go to do is make it sterile . how do we do that ?	我們所要做的只是讓它變得更加穩定 。 我們該怎麼做 ?
well , we could use the lifesaver bottle .	嗯 , 我們可以用lifesaver濾水瓶
or we could use one of these .	或者 , 我們可以用其中一種
the same technology , in a jerry can .	同樣的科技 , 在一個jerry罐裡 ,
this will process 25 , 000 liters of water ; that's good enough for a family of four , for three years .	這會處理25 , 000公升的水 ; 這對一個4 , 3年的家庭來說是好的 。
and how much does it cost ?	又要花多少錢呢 ?
about half a cent a day to run .	每天大概要花半分錢才能跑 。
so , by thinking differently , and processing water at the point of use , mothers and children no longer have to walk four hours a day to collect their water .	所以 , 透過不同的思考 , 並在使用時處理水分 , 母親和孩子不再需要每天走四個小時來收集他們的水 。
they can get it from a source nearby .	他們可以從附近的源頭取得
so with just eight billion dollars , we can hit the millennium goal's target of halving the number of people without access to safe drinking water .	所以只要八十億美元 , 我們就能達到千禧目標的目標 , 讓人們無法取得安全的飲用水 。
to put that into context , the u . k . government spends about 12 billion pounds a year on foreign aid .	為了說明這一點 , 英國政府每年花大約一百二百億英鎊在國外援助上 。
but why stop there ?	但為什麼就這樣停下來 ?
with 20 billion dollars , everyone can have access to safe drinking water .	只要兩百億美元 , 每個人都能取得安全的飲用水 。
so the threeandahalf billion people that suffer every year as a result , and the two million kids that die every year , will live .	每年有三十五億人遭受痛苦 , 每年有兩百萬個孩童死亡 , 將會活下來 。
paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	paddyashdown宣稱我們生活在歷史上的一刻 , 權力在改變前所未有的方式 。 在他在tedxbrussels的演講中 , 他列出了他所見到的三大全球轉變 。

there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	有一首詩是一位非常有名的英文詩人在十九世紀末寫的 。
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	據說在1930年代 , 在邱吉爾的腦中迴盪 。
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	詩的內容是: 「 在夏日的伊德爾山上 , 水流很懶 , 哈克我聽到遙遠的鼓聲 , 就像夢想中的聲音 , 在地球的路上 , 很遙遠、很低、很大、很大、很大、很大、很大、很快就會消逝 。 」
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩有興趣的人 , 這首詩是《shropreshirelad》由a.e.豪斯曼寫的 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但 , 豪斯曼也了解 , 在尼爾森的交響曲中也聽到了 , 十九世紀的漫長、炎熱、銀色的夏天正要來臨 , 我們即將邁入史上最可怕的一段時期 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	這些時期 , 各位先生女士 , 伴隨著亂流 , 常常是血 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	我給你們的訊息是 , 我相信我們會被譴責 , 如果你願意 , 只活在歷史上的那些時刻之一 , 那時 , 建立權力的秩序已經開始改變 , 而世界的新外觀 , 現存的新勢力已經開始形成 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	今天我們很清楚地看到 , 幾乎總是有很高的動盪時間 , 很困難的時代 , 很多時候都很血腥 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	對了 , 大約每一世紀都會發生一次 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你可能會爭辯說 , 上次發生的事──那是豪斯曼的感受──邱吉爾的感受──也就是 , 當權力從舊的國家傳過去 , 歐洲的舊勢力──橫跨大西洋──美國的新興勢力──美國本世紀初 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 進入了過去曾有過的歐洲權力發揮的真空 , 是兩個充滿血腥的災難 , 發生在上個世紀 , 第一部分和第二部分:兩次世界大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	毛澤東曾經把他們稱為歐洲內戰 , 這可能是比較精確的描述方式 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位先生女士 , 我們住在其中一個時代 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我今天想談談三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	首先 , 首先這兩項 , 是關於權力的轉變 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二個是關於我想要參考的新維度 , 這是從來沒有發生過的 。
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但 , 讓我們來談談權力的轉變 , 會發生在世界各地 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	今天的情況是 , 在某種意義上 , 恐嚇人的原因是它從來沒有發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們已經看到日後的權力轉移──希臘傳給羅馬的權力──以及在歐洲文明期間發生的權力轉移──但我們看到了一些稍微不同的東西 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	對於權力 , 不只是從國家轉變為國家 。
it's also moving vertically .	它也垂直地移動 。
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	現今的情況是 , 被放置的權力 , 持有責任 , 持有法律的統治 , 在國家國家的制度中 , 現在已經遷移到很大的全球階段 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	全球化的權力 , 我們談到全球化的市場 , 但實際上卻是真正的權力全球化 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在國家的層級上 , 權力是指責法治的主題 , 在國際階段 , 權力不是這樣 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台和全球舞台 , 現在掌權在哪裡:網路的力量、衛星廣播的力量、金錢轉換者的力量──這廣大的貨幣轉換者──現在可說是交易所必要的32倍──該是金錢轉換者所需的金錢──如果你喜歡的話 , 金融推銷員最近已經把我們全部帶到我們的膝蓋 , 多國企業的力量現在已經比中型國家更大了32倍 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些生活在一個沒有規範的全球空間 , 沒有法治的主題 , 也可能讓人們不受限制 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	現在 , 這樣就適合強而有力的時刻 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	總是適合那些最有權力在沒有限制的空間中運作的人 , 但歷史的教訓是 , 不久後 , 不受規範的空間不再受限於法律的規則 , 不只受到你想要的事物──國際貿易、網路、網路等等 。 還有你不想要的事物──國際犯罪、國際恐怖主義 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	911事件的揭示是 , 即使你是地球上最強大的國家 , 然而 , 那些居住太空的人 , 甚至可以攻擊你 , 即使在你最具代表性的一個九月的早晨 , 你也能攻擊你 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	據說 , 大約有百分之六十的四百萬美金被帶到資助911事件的資金中 , 其實是通過雙胞胎塔的機構 , 9/11摧毀了 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	你看 , 我們的敵人也用了這個空間──大眾旅行、網路、衛星廣播──能夠繞過它們的毒害 , 也就是破壞我們的系統 , 以及我們的方式 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	不久後 , 或遲早 , 歷史的規則是 , 權力的統治必須遵守 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	因此 , 正如我所相信的 , 我們這個時代的一個現象是權力的全球化 , 那麼 , 我們這個時代的挑戰之一就是把統治者帶到全球 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信在我們面前的數十年 , 將來會有更大或更小的動盪 , 我們越能達成這個目標:把治理帶到全球 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	現在請注意 , 我不是指政府 ,
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是在說設立一些全球民主制度
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順帶一提 , 我自己的觀點是 , 女士們先生們 , 這是不太可能透過更多的聯合國機構來完成的 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 我們就得發明
the world needs an international forum .	世界需要一個國際論壇
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一個手段 , 你可以合法化國際行動 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但 , 談到全球空間的統治時 , 我猜 , 不可能透過更多的聯合國機構創造出來的 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	它會發生在強大的團結在一起 , 建立以條約為基礎的系統、以條約為基礎的協議 , 來治理那個全球空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你看 , 你可以看到他們正在發生 , 已經開始浮現 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:以條約為基礎的組織 , 完全以條約為基礎的組織 , 然而 , 強大到能容納最有權力的美國 , 如果有必要的話 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	京都:掙扎著要創立一個以條約為基礎的組織 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	g20:我們現在知道我們必須組成一個機構 , 一個能夠把統治權帶到金融空間給金融空間 , 來推測財務 。
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	這就是g20的成果 , 一個以條約為基礎的機構 。
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有一個問題 , 我們等一下會再回來談這件事 , 那就是 , 如果你把最強大的力量集合在一起 , 在以條約為基礎的機構中 , 把規則填滿那個治理空間 , 那麼 , 那些剩下的弱者又會發生什麼事 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	這是個大問題 , 我們會在一秒鐘內回來 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一個訊息是 , 如果你要通過這些動亂 , 或多或少衝動 , 那麼 , 我們的成功會很大的做法 , 取決於我們有能力把合理的統治權帶到全球 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	看著這個開始發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二點是 , 我知道我不需要和像這樣的觀眾談這件事 , 但權力不只是垂直轉移 , 同時也在水平轉移 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你可能會爭辯說這個故事 , 文明的歷史 , 一直以來 , 文明聚集在海洋周圍 , 帶著最先到達地中海的文明 , 近期在西方國家大西洋的後代 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	在我看來 , 我們現在看到的是權力的基本轉變 , 廣泛地說 , 遠離各國聚集在大西洋的大西洋各地 , 聚集在太平洋岸邊的國家 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	這始於經濟實力 , 但這就是一直以來的開端 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外國政策的發展 , 軍事預算的擴增 , 發生在世界上其他日益增長的政策上 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我認為 , 這不是從西方移轉到東方的轉變 ; 有些不同的事情正在發生 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我的猜測是 , 值得注意的是 , 美國在未來的十年、十五年 , 仍然會保留在地球上最強大的國家 , 但她握有權力的情境現在已經徹底改變了 ; 徹底改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	五十年來 , 最不尋常的年度 , 歷史中 , 我們有一個完全的單向世界 , 每個羅盤的針頭 , 都得要被它的位置給推薦到華盛頓 , 一個獨特的巨人所的世界最適合 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但這不是歷史上常見的案例 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在正在浮現的是歷史上更正常的案例 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你開始看到一個多極化的世界的出現
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	到目前為止 , 美國一直是我們世界的主要特徵 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	他們會保留最強大的國家 , 但他們會是越來越多極地世界中最強大的國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	當然 , 我自己猜測 , 中國的權力基礎建設中心當然是中國對偉大的源頭並不平滑 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	這將是相當嚴重的 , 因為中國在解放她的經濟之後開始民主化她的社會 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但那是不同的討論主題 。
you see india , you see brazil .	看到印度、巴西、
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	你可以看到 , 現在世界看起來 , 對我們歐洲人來說 , 更像十九世紀的歐洲 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	十九世紀的歐洲 , 一個偉大的英國外交大臣 , 坎寧 , 用來形容它是 「 歐洲的權力音樂會 」 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	當時有一個平衡 , 一個五等的平衡 。
britain always played to the balance .	英國總是扮演平衡的角色 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎和柏林聚在一起 , 英國和維也納和羅馬聚在一起 , 提供反平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	請注意 , 在一個單一世界所主宰的時期 , 你有固定的盟友nato , 華沙特 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	一個固定的權力極端代表固定結盟 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但 , 權力的多極端 , 意味著轉變和改變盟友 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	這就是我們所處的世界 , 我們將逐漸看到我們的同盟國並沒有固定下來 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	坎寧 , 偉大的英國國務卿曾說過: 「 英國有共同的利益 , 但沒有共同的盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們會漸漸看到 , 即使我們西方國家會伸出援手 , 必須伸出援手 , 超越大西洋勢力圈圈 , 才能和他人結盟 , 如果我們想要讓世界的事情完成的話 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	請注意 , 當我們進入利比亞時 , 西方並不夠好 , 我們得要帶其他人進來 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	我們必須把阿拉伯聯盟帶進來 。
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我的猜測是伊拉克和阿富汗是西方最後一次嘗試自己這麼做的時候 , 我們還沒成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我的猜測是 , 我們已經到了400年末的開始--我說400年--因為它是鄂圖曼帝國的終結--西方的權力、西方的制度和西方的價值觀 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道嗎 , 直到現在 , 如果西方國家團結起來 , 它可以在世界各個角落提出和解 。
but that's no longer true .	但這已經不是事實了 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	以第二次世界大戰後最後一次的金融危機為例 。
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方國家聚集了布雷頓森林機構、世界銀行、國際貨幣基金組織──問題解決了 。
now we have to call in others .	現在我們必須打電話給別人 。
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們必須創造出g20
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	現在我們必須達到超越西方朋友的舒適圈 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我為各位做一個預測 , 這可能更讓人驚訝 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我猜我們現在已經到了四百年的盡頭 , 那時西方勢力已經夠大了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	人們對我說: 「 中國人 , 當然 , 他們永遠不會讓自己參與世界各地的和平活動 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	喔是嗎 ? 為什麼不行 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊在藍色貝雷特下服役 , 在藍色旗幟下服役 , 在現今的聯合國指令下服役 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	有多少美國人 ? 11 。
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	什麼是最大的海軍訴求 , 來處理索馬利海盜的問題 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國海軍的內容
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	當然 , 他們是商業的國家 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	他們想讓海道保持開放
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	漸漸地 , 我們得要和我們不共享價值觀的人做生意 , 但 , 若有誰 , 我們就會共享共同的利益 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	這是一種全新的角度來看世界 , 現在正在興起 。
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	接下來是第三個因素 , 完全不同 。
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	現今 , 在我們的現代世界 , 由於網路 , 由於人們在這裡所談到的各種事物 , 一切都和一切連結在一起 。
we are now interdependent .	我們現在是互相依賴的
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們現在被關在 , 作為國家 , 作為個體 , 從來沒有如此 , 從來沒有如此 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國與國之間的關聯 , 嗯 , 它始終存在 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交的重點在於管理國家的相關性 。
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們密不可分 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	你得到墨西哥的豬流感 , 24小時後的查爾斯戴高爾機場就有問題了 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟下降了 , 整個崩潰 。
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	俄羅斯的腳步有火災 , 非洲的糧食暴動 。
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都深切、深切、深切地互相連結 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	這意味著 , 一個國家單獨行動的概念 , 不和他人連結 , 不和他人合作 , 不再是一個可行的提案 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為一個國家的行動不被限制自己也不足以控制國家本身的領土因為在國家之外的影響現在已經開始影響他們內在的狀況了
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我曾是英國最後一個小帝國戰爭的年輕士兵 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 我的國家對於一件事的辯護 , 只有一件事:我們的軍隊有多強壯 , 我們的空軍有多強壯 , 我們的海軍有多強壯 , 我們的盟軍有多強壯 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	那時候敵人就在牆外
now the enemy is inside the walls .	現在敵人就在牆內
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	現在 , 如果我想要談我的國家辯護 , 我得要談談健康部長 , 因為流行病對我的安全造成威脅 , 我得要談談農業部長 , 因為糧食安全對我的安全造成威脅 , 我得要談談談 , 我得要談談談到工業部長 , 因為希臘基礎設施的脆弱 , 對於我們的敵人來說 , 如同我們從網路戰爭中看到的一樣 , 我得要談談談談我的國家 , 在我的國家中 , 誰已經進入了777年時 , 誰會發生什麼事 ?
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	不再是這樣一個國家的安全對於其士兵及其國防部來說 , 是很重要的 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	它的能力會鎖定它的機構 。
and this tells you something very important .	這說明了一件非常重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴各位 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 垂直構建 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模式上 , 垂直階級化 , 專門化的工作任務 , 指令結構是完全錯誤的結構 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	在商業中你知道我們這個時代的典範結構 , 各位先生女士 , 就是這個網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	它是你網絡的能力 , 無論在你的政府或外部都很重要 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	這是阿什唐的第三定律 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順帶一提 , 不要問我關於艾希登的第一條法則和第二條法則 , 因為我還沒發明過 ; 如果有第三條法則的話 , 聽起來總是比較好 , 對吧 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	ashdown的第三個法則是 , 在現代 , 每件事都和一切有關 , 最重要的是你能做什麼 , 就是你能和他人做些什麼 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	關於你的結構 , 最重要的一點是--不論你是政府 , 不論你是軍事紀錄 , 不論你是不是商人 , 你的交際點 , 你的交際點 , 你的能力和他人網絡的能力 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你明白在工業上 ; 政府不會 。
but now one final thing .	但現在有最後一件事了 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是這樣 , 各位先生女士 , 我們現在被關在一起 , 以一種前所未有的方式 , 以前從來就不太一樣 , 那麼這也是我們彼此的命運 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 也是第一次 , 集體防衛 , 已經主宰我們為國家安全的概念 , 已經不夠了 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	以前 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落更強大 , 我就安全了 ; 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強大 , 我就安全了 ; 我的同盟國 , 比如北約組織 , 比他們的同盟更強大 , 我就安全了 。
it is no longer the case .	不再是如此了 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	大規模毀滅性武器的出現 , 意味著我與敵人有著越來越多的命運 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我還是外交組織在1970年代與日內瓦的蘇聯談判時 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們明白我們和他們分享了命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全是不夠的
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平已經來到北愛爾蘭因為雙方意識到零和遊戲是行不通的
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們和敵人分享了命運 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	在中東 , 和平的一個偉大的障礙是 , 雙方 , 雙方 , 雙方 , 雙方 , 不論是以色列 , 我認為 , 巴勒斯坦人 , 都不了解他們有共同的命運 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以突然間 , 女士們先生們 , 一直以來 , 那些有遠見的詩人和詩人的提議 , 變成我們必須認真看待公共政策 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 以一首詩作結 。
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰•唐恩的偉大詩作
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 不要為誰發出鈴聲 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 「 沒有人是孤島 」 。
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	它說: 「 每個男人的死都影響著我 , 因為我參與了人類 , 不要要求他們說鐘聲誰響了 , 它會為我摧毀 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	對約翰•唐尼來說 , 道德的推薦
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為 , 方程式的一部分是為了我們的生存 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到長壽和健康的路 , danbuetner和團隊研究世界的 「 藍色區塊 」 , 他們的長者與vim和vigor共存的社區 , 記錄了年齡 。 在tedxtc , 他分享了9個常見的飲食和生活習慣 , 讓他們在100歲前 , 一直困擾著他們 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物、文化、探索、食物、健康、生命、科學、科學、
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuettner:如何活到100+
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	丹麥的雙胞胎研究指出 , 大約只有百分之十的人平均壽命 , 在某些生物限制之內 , 由我們的基因來決定 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	剩下的90%則由我們的生活方式主宰 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以藍色區塊的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式 , 我們就能想出長壽的事實公式 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問美國人平均壽命的最佳公式 , 他們可能無法告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽說過南灘飲食 , 或阿特金斯飲食 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有美國食品食物金字塔
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們的是
there is what doctor oz tells us .	這是奧茲醫生告訴我們的 。
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實是有很多的困惑 , 真正能幫助我們活得更久 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該跑馬拉松還是做瑜伽 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該吃有機肉還是應該吃豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	談到補充品時 , 你應該把他們帶走嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	這些荷爾蒙或逆水池呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	目的是否有成效 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	靈性 ? 那我們如何社交呢 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	嗯 , 我們找到長壽的方法是和國家地理協會合作 , 國家老化研究所 , 找出四個人口確認地理定義的區域 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	然後帶一組專家團隊到那裡去 , 以方法說明這些人的做法 , 讓跨文化的瓦解 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後我要告訴各位 , 那個幻覺是什麼 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先 , 我想要破除一些常見的迷思 , 談到長壽的問題 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是 , 如果你非常努力 , 你可以活到一百歲 。
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 美國5000人中只有1人活到100歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	即使它是美國成長最快的人口統計 , 還是很難達到100 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是 , 我們不是為了長壽而寫程式 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們為所謂的 「 繁衍成功 」 所寫的程式 。
i love that word .	我很喜歡這個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	這讓我想起了我的大學日子 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家稱之為 「 成功 」 , 意思是你有孩子的年齡 , 接著是另一個世代 , 當你的孩子有孩子時的年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在那之後 , 演化的效應完全消失了 。
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳類動物 , 如果你是老鼠或大象 , 或人類 , 在兩者之間 , 則是相同的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以 , 要達到100歲 , 你不只要有美好的生活方式 , 你也要贏得遺傳彩票 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有一些治療可以協助緩慢、反轉 , 甚至停止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	想想看 , 有99件事情可以讓我們變老 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	剝奪你腦中的氧氣短短幾分鐘 , 那些腦細胞死亡 , 它們永遠不會回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	玩網球太硬了 , 在你的膝蓋上 , 毀了你的軟骨 , 軟骨永遠不會回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈可以堵塞 。 我們的大腦可以用斑塊來燃燒 , 我們可以得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	出錯是有太多事情發生的 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 用一個 " t. " 來計算 , 我們在這裡談的是國家債務數字 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	那些細胞每8年一次輪流一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當它們轉身時 , 就會造成一些傷害 。 造成損害 。
and it builds up exponentially .	並且以指數的方式建立起來 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	這有點像我們都有披頭四的專輯或老鷹專輯的日子 , 我們會用膠帶來複製 , 讓我們的朋友複製那膠帶 , 很快地 , 帶著成功的世代 , 錄音帶聽起來像垃圾 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	嗯 , 同樣的事情也發生在我們的細胞上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個65歲的人老化的速度比一個12歲的人要快125倍 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有辦法減緩老化或停止老化 , 我在這裡幹嘛 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	嗯 , 事實上 , 最好的科學告訴我們 , 人體的能力 , 我的身體 , 你的身體 , 大約90年 , 女性多一點 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但這個國家的預期壽命只有78歲 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以 , 在路線的某個地方 , 我們在桌子上留下了大約12年的美好年頭 。
these are years that we could get .	這些是我們能得到的年份 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 多年來 , 大多都沒有慢性病、心臟病、癌症 , 以及糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為 , 要讓這些失蹤年齡最好的方法 , 就是去看世界各地的文化 , 實際上正在經歷它們的文化 , 人們活到比我們高出一百倍到十倍的年齡 , 平均壽命多出十幾年 , 中年死亡率是這個國家的一小部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們發現我們的第一個藍色區塊 , 離義大利海岸大約有125英里 , 位在薩丁尼亞島 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整個島嶼 , 島嶼大約有一百四十萬人 , 但只有在高地 , 一個叫做努奧羅省的地區 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	在這裡 , 男性最長壽的地區 , 比我們在美國的比我們多出十倍的百歲人瑞 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這個地方 , 人們不只達到100歲 , 還會用非凡的積極來做 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	102歲的老人仍然騎腳踏車去工作 , 砍柴 , 還能打敗比他們年輕60年 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史實際上回到了基督的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	其實是被隔離的青銅時代文化
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地是如此地惡劣 , 大多是牧羊人 , 偶爾會規律、低密度的身體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	牠們的飲食主要是以植物為基礎 , 以牠們能帶到田裡的食物為基礎 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出一種未發酵的全麥麵包 , 叫做卡塔音樂麵包 , 用杜魯姆麥做成的乳酪 , 一種來自草食品動物的乳酪 , 所以在omega-3脂肪酸上 , 而不是omega-6脂肪酸 , 一種來自玉米動物的葡萄酸 , 比世界上任何已知的葡萄酒含量都高三倍 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但我認為真正的秘密是他們組織社會的方式 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	而薩丁尼亞社會最突出的元素之一就是他們如何對待老年人 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到在美國 , 社會平等似乎在24歲時達到高峰 ?
just look at the advertisements .	只要看一下廣告 ,
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞這裡 , 年紀越大 , 你就越能得到你所擁有的平等 , 你就越能為之慶祝 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你走進薩丁尼亞的酒吧 , 而不是看到體育插座的游泳日曆 , 而是看到月曆的百歲人瑞 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	結果發現 , 這不僅對你的老化父母有益 , 還能讓他們和家人保持親近 , 大約是四到六年的預期壽命研究顯示 , 這對那些家庭的孩子有益 , 他們的死亡率和疾病的比率較低 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	也就是所謂的祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們在地球的另一端發現了第二個藍色區塊 , 位於東京南方八百英里處 , 位於俄亥俄州的阿基拉哥 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okinawa其實是161個小島
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	而在主島的北方 , 這是世界長壽的地點 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這是最古老的雌性族群被找到的地方 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	這個地方 , 人們有著世界上最長的失能預期壽命 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	牠們活很久 , 很快地在睡眠中死去 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你 , 在性行為之後 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們比美國人平均壽命長七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	在美國 , 百歲人瑞的五倍 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	在美國 , 結腸癌和乳癌的比率是五分之一 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	以及心血管疾病的比率的六分之一
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	而這個文化促成了這些數字的事實 , 強烈指出他們有東西可以教導我們 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 以植物為基礎的飲食 , 裡面滿是大量有色的蔬菜 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	和美國人一樣 , 吃大約八倍的豆腐
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比他們吃的食物更顯著 , 就是他們怎麼吃的 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各種小策略可以避免過度飲食 , 如你所知 , 這在美國是很大的問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略:他們從較小的盤子裡吃下的食物 , 所以他們每坐著時傾向都會少吃點卡路里 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其服務家庭風格 , 在你說話時 , 你可以無意識地吃東西 , 他們服務櫃檯 , 把食物帶走 , 然後帶到桌子上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們還有一個3000歲的年紀我認為是有史以來最偉大的飲食建議
it was invented by confucius .	它是由混蛋發明的 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	而那個飲食就是所謂的哈拉、哈茨基、布飲食 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	這只是一個小小的說 , 在他們的餐前提醒他們在胃時不要再吃東西了 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	大概要半小時 , 才會有完整的感受 , 才能從你的肚子傳到你的大腦 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	記住要停止百分之八十 , 它會幫助你不去做這些事 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 就像薩丁尼亞 , 奧納瓦有幾個社會建構 , 我們可以把長壽聯想起來 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道孤立會致命 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	十五年前 , 美國人平均有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在已經降到一半了 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你幸運地出生在okinawa , 你生在一個系統中 , 自動擁有五十個朋友 , 跟著你在人生中旅行 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱它為moai 。 如果你在一個你預期會碰到好運氣的moai身上 , 如果你遇到壞事 , 孩子會生病 , 家長會死 , 你總是有人背著 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這個特別的moai , 這五位女士已經在一起了97年 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們把成年人的生活分成兩區 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	我們的工作生活有生產力
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	通常這意味著退休給簡單的椅子 , 或是下到亞利桑那州去打高爾夫球 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在okinawan語言中 , 根本沒有退休的字眼 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	相反地 , 有一個字反映了你的一生 , 那個字就是 「 生存 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	大約翻譯了 , 意思是 「 你早上起床的原因 」 。
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對於這位102歲的karate大師來說 , 他的ikigai正帶著這件武術 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這位百歲的漁夫來說 , 一週要捕魚 , 持續捕魚 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 。 國家老化研究院實際上給了我們一個問卷給這些百歲人瑞 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題 , 他們在文化上很有文化上的缺點 , 那些把問卷問卷的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikigai是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道為什麼早上醒來
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對這位一百二歲的女子來說 , 她的ikigai只是她的曾曾孫女 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩位女孩在101歲半前分離 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 拿著曾曾曾孫女的感覺是什麼樣的 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	然後她把她的頭放回去 , 說: 「 感覺就像跳上天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得那是個很棒的點子 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理的編輯希望我能找到美國的藍色區域 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有一陣子我們在明尼蘇達的草原上 , 實際上 , 百歲人瑞的比例很高 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有離開的年輕人
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們再次轉向資料 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現美國最長壽的族群 , 位於加州的羅馬林達 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	冒險家是保守的方法論者 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們在星期五慶祝安息日的安息日 , 直到星期六日落 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	一個24小時的庇護所 , 他們稱它為
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循五個小習慣 , 向他們傳達非凡的長壽 , 相較於說話 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均每位女性平均壽命是80歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對一位冒險女性來說 , 她們的預期壽命為89 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	差別在於 , 男性之間的差異更高 , 他們預期會比美國人的對手多活大約11年 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	現在 , 這個研究追蹤了大約七萬人三十年 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	史特林研究 。 而且我認為它最能說明這個藍色區塊計劃的前提 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是一個異族群 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	是白人、黑人、西班牙人、亞洲人
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一的共通點是一組非常小的生活方式習慣 , 他們大部分的人生都遵循著儀式 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們直接從聖經中取下他們的飲食 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	基因:第一章 , 第二章 , 第29節 , 上帝談到樂園和種子 , 還有一座關於綠色植物的史丹札 , 很可能缺少的就是肉 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們認真看待這個聖所 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時 , 不論他們多忙 , 他們在工作上有多緊張 , 孩子們需要被驅使 , 他們停止一切 , 把焦點放在他們的神、他們的社交網路上 , 然後 , 在宗教中 , 天生就要走了 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這其中的力量並不是偶爾完成而已 , 權力是每週完成一次 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	一點都不困難 , 一點都不花錢 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	冒險家也傾向與其他的冒險家相處 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一場冒險派對 , 你不會看到人們在關節轉彎 , 或滾動一個關節 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	取而代之的是他們在說下一個大自然走路、交換食譜 , 沒錯 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們會以深刻且可衡量的方式影響彼此 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這是一種文化 , 讓艾爾斯沃雷漢有所保留 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	艾爾斯沃雷漢九十七歲 。
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是一名多萬富翁 , 但當一個包商要六千美金來建造一個隱私的圍籬時 , 他說: 「 為了那樣的錢 , 我自己來做 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以 , 接下來的三天 , 他出去購物水泥 , 到處拖著桿子 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可以預測 , 或許在第四天 , 他最後進到手術室 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不像桌上的那個人 ; 那個做開心手術的那個人 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	九十七歲時 , 他仍然每個月做二十次開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	艾德•羅林斯 , 103歲 , 一個活躍的牛仔 , 從他的早晨開始游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	在他喜歡的週末 , 放到板子上 , 丟到屋頂尾巴 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子其實住在雙胞胎城市這裡 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她從抬起重量的那一天開始 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎著腳踏車
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	然後她進到她的根部 , 1994年彩色的cadillacseville , 淚光從聖貝納迪諾高速公路上流下 , 在那裡 , 她仍然為七個不同組織的組織當志工 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我曾參加過19場硬體探險活動 。
