i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我大概是唯一一個你會遇到的人 , 騎著他的腳踏車穿越撒哈拉沙漠 , 沒有防曬霜 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我要告訴各位 , 沒有任何冒險比和瑪格•狄頓一起開槍更駭人 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 一個陌生人是我還沒見過的朋友 ! 」 她會對我說:
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	所以 , 這三種文化中的共同點是什麼 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們都在做些什麼 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們成功歸結為九 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 我們從此以後已經完成了兩次藍色區域探險活動 , 這些共同的探測器也都有成效 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	首先 , 我準備要講一個結論 , 沒有一個練習 , 至少我們看待運動的方式 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	取而代之的是 , 他們建立了自己的生命 , 這樣他們會不斷地被推入身體活動中 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這百歲的琉球女人上下地板 , 每天坐著三十或四十次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子裡 , 上上下樓梯 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次去商店 , 或去教堂 , 或去朋友家 , 都會有一場散步 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何便利 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有按鈕可以做院子工作或房子工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想要混蛋糕 , 就要用手做 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	跑步機燃燒的卡路里也一樣多 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做有意的身體活動時 , 是他們享受的事物 。 他們傾向於走路 , 唯一證實的方式可以脫離認知的衰退 , 他們都傾向於有個花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何用正確的方式來建立自己的人生 , 讓他們有正確的外觀 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每一種文化都需要時間下降 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 。 第七天的先生祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	okinawans有這種祖先的聯繫
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你身處在急促或壓力外時 , 會觸發一種稱為 「 炎性反應 」 的東西 , 這種反應和一切都有關 , 從阿茲海默症到心血管疾病 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你每天放慢15分鐘 , 將那發炎狀態變成更加抗炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們有目的性的字彙 , 像okinawans 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你生命中最危險的兩年 , 就是你出生的那一年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 而你退休的那一年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道他們的目的感 , 並且在他們的生活中活躍 , 那是價值約七年的預期壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽的飲食
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天喝了一點點酒 , 不是很難賣給美國人口 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	牠們傾向以植物為基礎的飲食
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不代表他們不吃肉 , 而是大量的豆子和堅果 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略可以避免過度的、小事 , 讓他們在對的時間遠離桌面 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	這一切的基礎是它們如何連結 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把家人擺第一 , 照顧他們的孩子和他們的老化父母 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都傾向屬於一個以信仰為基礎的社群 , 這價值在四到十四年的預期壽命之間 , 如果你每個月做四次 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	這裡最大的是 , 它們也屬於正確的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們不是生來就是活躍地把自己包圍在對的人身上 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從佛明罕研究中得知如果你三個最好的朋友都過胖你會過重的可能性有50%
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人在一起 , 隨著時間 , 那將會帶來重大的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反地 , 如果你朋友對休閒的想法是身體活動 , 保齡球 , 或玩曲棍球 , 自行車或園藝 , 如果你的朋友喝了一點 , 但不多 , 他們吃得很好 , 而且他們很投入 , 並且信任和值得信賴 , 這會對時間產生最大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食沒有用 , 在世界歷史上 , 沒有任何飲食對2%以上的人口有用 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計畫通常是從一月開始的 ; 它們通常是十月份做的 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	談到長壽 , 沒有短期的術語在藥丸或任何其他的方面 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但仔細想想 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 也許你能做的最重要的事 , 來為你的生活加上更多年 , 多年的生命 。 非常謝謝你 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	墨水會導電 ; 一扇清澈的窗戶 , 轉向一個開關的不透明 ; 一個會讓音樂的水母 。 所有這些東西都存在 。 卡塔琳娜莫塔斯說:該是用它來演奏的時候了 。 mota帶領我們踏上一趟驚喜和酷炫的新材料之旅 , 建議我們找出它們的好處 , 用它來做實驗 , 微調和樂趣 。
creativity , design , technology	創造力、設計、科技
catarina mota: play with smart materials	卡塔瑞娜莫塔:玩智慧材料 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我在葡萄牙有個朋友 , 他的祖父用腳踏車和洗衣機建造了一台車 , 這樣他才能運送他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他負擔不起車子 , 也因為他知道如何建造一輛 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾經有一段時間 , 我們了解事物如何運作 , 以及它們是如何製造的 , 這樣我們就能建立和修復它們 , 或者 , 最少能針對要買什麼東西做出有知覺的決定 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	許多這些做法在20世紀的後半失去了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 製造者社群和開放原始碼的模式 , 帶來了這種知識 , 關於事物如何運作 , 以及它們在我們的生活中所組成的是什麼 , 我相信我們需要帶它們到下一個階段 , 去做成的元件 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的時候 , 我們仍然知道紙張和紡織品的傳統材料是由什麼製成的 , 以及它們如何生產的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些驚人而活躍的複合物塑膠 , 會改變形狀 , 會導電的顏料 , 會改變顏色的顏料 , 會發光的布料 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以導電油墨可以讓我們畫出電路 , 而不是使用傳統印刷電路板或電線 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在我舉的這個小例子中 , 我們用它來創造出觸控感應器 , 透過打開這個小光線來對我的皮膚做出反應 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	導電油墨已經被藝術家使用 , 但近期的發展指出 , 我們很快就能用在雷射印表機和筆上 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這是一片acrylic , 注入了無色輕微的粒子 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意味著 , 雖然普通的丙烯酸鹽只會在邊緣散發光 , 這張照亮了整個表面 , 當我打開它周圍的燈光時 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	對於這種材料 , 有兩個已知的應用包括室內設計和多點觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	而熱色的顏料則會在特定的溫度變化顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以我要把這個放在一個熱板子上 , 它的溫度只比環境稍高一點 , 你可以看到會發生什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	這種材料的其中一個原理是 , 在嬰兒奶瓶中 , 在嬰兒奶瓶中 , 它會指示出 , 當內容物夠酷來喝酒時 , 它會指示出 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是一些被稱為智慧材料的常見 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年內 , 它們會在我們日常使用的許多物品和技術中 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒有飛天車科幻小說向我們保證 , 但我們能有改變顏色的牆 , 依據溫度、鍵盤 , 會捲起來 , 窗戶會變成不透明的開關 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	所以 , 我是社會科學家 , 透過訓練 , 所以 , 為什麼我今天在這裡要談智慧材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是個製造者 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我對事物的運作及製造方式感到好奇 , 也因為我相信 , 我們應該要更深入了解構成我們的世界的成分 , 而現在 , 我們對這些高科技複合物並不足夠 , 我們的未來會被製成 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧型材料很難在數量上取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	在如何使用它們時 , 幾乎沒有任何的資訊 , 且很少被說出它們是如何產生的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 現在 , 他們大部分都存在於貿易機密和專利領域中 , 只有大學和企業可以取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	所以 , 三年前 , kirsty男孩和我開始了一個計畫 , 我們叫做開放材料 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	這是個網站 , 我們 , 和其他任何想要加入我們的人 , 分享實驗 , 發佈資訊 , 鼓勵其他人在何時何地貢獻 , 並聚集資源 , 像是其他像我們一樣的自造者的研究論文和課程 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它能成為智慧材料的大型、集體的資料庫 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但我們為什麼要在乎智慧型材料如何運作 , 以及它們的組成呢 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法塑造我們不了解的東西 , 而我們不了解、使用的東西最後會塑造我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們使用的物品、穿的衣服、我們居住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活品質有深遠的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以 , 如果我們要活在一個由智慧材料構成的世界 , 我們應該要知道並了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	其次 , 同樣重要的是 , 創新一直以來都是由tinker來的 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘者 , 而非專家 , 都是發明家和改進者 , 從登山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是材料科學是複雜且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但並非總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾大學的兩位科學家了解這一點 , 當他們發表一篇論文時 , 用比較簡單的方法來製造導電墨水 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	喬登•布蘭克 , 他對化學沒有任何經驗 , 直到那時 , 讀了這篇論文 , 並在他的自造者空間中重製了實驗 , 只用了自製的物質和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤箱 , 甚至用他自己的旋渦混合器 , 基於另一位科學家/製造師的教導 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	約旦接著在網路上發表了他的成果 , 包括所有他曾經嘗試過且沒用過的東西 , 讓其他人可以研究並重製它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	所以 , 約旦主要的創新形式 , 是把一個實驗用有裝備的實驗室 , 放在芝加哥的一間車庫裡 , 用他自己製造的便宜材料和工具 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	而現在他發表了這項工作 , 其他人可以拿起他離開的地方 , 設計更簡單的過程和改進 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另一個例子我想提一下她的計畫目標是強調材料的表達特質 , 同時把焦點放在建造者的創意和技巧上 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子組件非常強大 , 它們教導我們事物如何運作 , 但它們的設計限制會影響我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	另一方面漢娜的作法是建立一系列的技術 , 來創造出不尋常的物品 , 使我們免於預先設計的限制 , 透過教導我們材料本身的知識 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	所以漢娜許多令人印象深刻的實驗中 , 這是我最喜歡的實驗之一 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	[紙喇叭]我們現在看到的只是一張紙上面有一些銅膠帶連結到mp3播放器和磁鐵
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	根據麻省理工學院的馬賽洛柯爾荷的研究 , 漢娜創造了一系列的紙喇叭 , 從簡單的銅膠帶到導電布和墨水 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約旦和許多其他製造者一樣 , 漢娜出版了她的食譜 , 讓任何人都能複製、繁衍它們 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子是最有前景的材料科學分支之一 , 它能讓我們創造出更便宜且有彈性的電子 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	所以漢娜的工藝作品 , 以及她共同發現的事實 , 打開了一連串新的可能性 , 這些可能是美學上和創新的 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以製造者有趣的地方在於我們用熱情和好奇心創造出來 , 我們不怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們經常從不規則的角度解決問題 , 在過程中 , 最後發現替代方案 , 或甚至更好的方式來做事 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 越多人針對材料做實驗 , 研究人員就越願意分享他們的研究 , 製造出他們的知識 , 我們就越有機會創造出真正能服務我們所有人的科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	我覺得有點像泰德尼爾森在1970年代早期 , 他寫道: 「 你現在必須要了解電腦了 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	那時 , 電腦是這些大型的主體 , 只有科學家在關心 , 沒有人夢想過在家中有一台 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡說: 「 你現在必須要了解智慧型材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 取得新興科技的先前知識 , 是確保我們在未來能發聲的最佳方式 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會進入玻璃泡泡 , 鎖定門 , 按下加速器 , 依賴我們的眼睛來指導我們 , 即使我們只能看見前方及後方少數的車子 。 但如果車子能彼此分享資料 , 和彼此分享他們的位置和速度 , 並用預測模型來計算路上的每個人最安全的路線 ? jenniferhealey想像一個沒有意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	jenniferhealey:如果車子可以說話 , 意外可能會是可避免的 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	面對現實吧:開車是危險的 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡思考的一件事但宗教圖像和好運魅力出現在世界各地的儀表板背叛著我們所知道的事實
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是十六到十九歲美國人死亡的主要成因 , 而這些事故中有百分之七十五與毒品或酒精無關 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒人能肯定 , 但我記得我的第一次意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我在高速公路上擔任年輕司機 , 前面的車 , 我看到煞車燈繼續下去 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我會說: 「 好吧 , 這個傢伙慢了下來 , 我也會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踩煞車
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但不 , 這傢伙不是在放慢速度 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙停了 , 死了 , 死了 , 在高速公路上停了下來 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	剛剛到65歲到零了 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我在煞車上撞了一下 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我感受到abs踢進去 , 車子還在 , 它不會停下來 , 我知道不會停下來 , 空中袋子部署 , 車子總算很快 , 幸運的是 , 沒有人受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全沒想到車停了 , 我認為我們可以做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以轉變開車的經驗 , 讓車子彼此交談 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只希望各位能稍微思考一下開車的經驗是怎樣的 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	進入你的車 。 關上車門 。 你在玻璃泡裡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感受到你周遭的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的身體裡
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是將它導向部分看不見的道路 , 在其他金屬巨人之中 , 以超人的速度 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 而你只需要指引你是你的兩隻眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好了 , 這就是你所擁有的 , 眼睛不是設計來完成這個任務的 , 但之後人們要你做一些事情 , 像是 , 你想做一個車道改變 , 他們問你做的第一件事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛從路上拿掉 。 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	別再看你要去哪裡 , 轉身 , 檢查你的盲點 , 然後開車下路 , 不看你要去哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人 。 這是開車的安全方法 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼我們要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須做出選擇 , 我看這邊 , 還是我看這邊 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會做一份很棒的工作挑選 , 選擇我們在路上要去做的事 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們忽略了一些
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們會感覺到不對或遲到的事 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	在無數的意外中 , 司機說: 「 我沒看到它來了 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信這點 , 我相信
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看這麼多 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現在的科技可以幫助我們改善這一點 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 有了車輛互相交換資料 , 我們將能看到不只是前面三部車 , 還有後面三部車 , 往右和左邊 , 同時 , 鳥類的眼睛 , 我們將能夠真正看到那些車子 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們將能夠看見前面車輛的速度 , 看看那位男士要走多快或停止 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那傢伙下降到零 , 我就會知道
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	透過計算、演算法和預測模型 , 我們將能夠看見未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能認為那是不可能的 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 那真的很困難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	其實 , 不 。 用汽車 , 這不是不可能的 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	汽車是有固定位置和速度的三維物體 。
they travel down roads .	它們會沿著道路行駛
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們會在出版前的路線行駛 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	對於在不久的將來 , 一輛車會在哪裡 , 做合理的預測並不難 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使 , 當你在你的車上 , 和一些摩托車騎士來臨時 ! 時速85英里 , 車道插座--我知道你有過這種經驗 , 不是 「 無所不在 」 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那傢伙大概在前半個小時都在路上
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人見過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10 , 20 , 30英里背後 , 有人看到那個傢伙 , 一車一車就看到那個傢伙 , 把他放到地圖上 , 他在地圖的位置 , 速度 , 估計他會以每小時85英里的速度繼續走 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你就會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為那輛車會在他的耳邊悄悄一些東西 , 比如: 「 順便一提 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車騎士 , 小心翼翼翼 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以合理地預測汽車的行為 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 它們是牛頓的物體 。
that's very nice about them .	那對他們來說是很棒的 。
so how do we get there ?	那我們該如何達到目的呢 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從一些簡單的東西開始 , 如同分享我們車子之間的位置資料 , 只是分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我在我的車裡有一台gps和一台攝影機 , 我就很精確知道我在哪裡 , 以及我要走多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我周圍的車子位置 , 有點像是他們去了哪裡 。
and same with the other cars .	其他車輛也一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以精確的知道自己在哪裡 , 並且有點模糊的知道其他車子在哪裡 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩輛車分享那些資料 , 如果他們彼此交談 , 會發生什麼事 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以準確地告訴你會發生什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	bobwang教授和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 當毛茸茸的估計結合時 , 甚至在輕鬆的交通中 , 當汽車分享gps資料時 , 我們把這個研究從電腦模擬出來 , 移到機器人測試床上 , 這些裝在這些機器人身上的感測器:stereo攝影機、gps , 以及在後備系統中常見的二維雷射測器 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們也附著一個分散的短距通訊電台 , 機器人會彼此交談 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人彼此來到時 , 它們會精確地追蹤彼此的位置 , 且它們可以避免彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在把越來越多的機器人加入混合體中 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題 , 當你拿到太多聊天器時 , 很難處理所有的包裝 , 所以你必須優先處理 , 這就是預測模型幫助你的地方 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人車子全都在追蹤預測的軌跡 , 你不會把注意力提高給那些人 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	優先考慮一個看起來有點偏離軌道的傢伙 。
that guy could be a problem .	那個人可能是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	並且可以預測新的軌跡
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他要下課了 , 還知道怎麼了 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	而且你知道你需要警示哪位駕駛者 , 才能脫身 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們也想做 , 我們要如何警告所有人 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車子怎麼能悄悄的說: 「 你需要走出去嗎 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 這取決於兩件事:一 , 車的能力 , 第二 , 駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果有一個人真的有一台很棒的車 , 但他們在手機上 , 或者 , 做點什麼 , 他們可能不會在緊急狀況中做出最好的反應 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以 , 我們開始分開研究 , 做 「 駕駛狀態模型 」 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 用一系列的三台攝影機 , 我們可以偵測到駕駛是不是向前看 , 向下看 , 在電話上看 , 或是喝一杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測意外狀況 , 我們可以預測誰、誰、哪輛車 , 都在最好的位置 , 可以走出去 , 去計算對每個人最安全的路線 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 現今這些科技的存在
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們面臨的最大問題是我們自己的意願分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我認為這是一個非常讓人不安的想法 , 我們的車會看著我們 , 和我們談談其他的車子 , 我們會在一片八卦的大海中走在路上 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信它可以用一種方式來保護我們的隱私 , 就像現在一樣 , 當我從外面看你的車時 , 我並不知道你是怎麼想的 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看你的車牌號碼 , 我真的不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車可以在背後談論我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我認為這會是一件很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我希望你能考慮一下 , 如果你真的不希望身後的青少年知道你在煞車 , 知道你要來個死胡同的停車 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	透過願意分享我們的資料 , 我們可以做到最適合每個人的 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 讓你的車八卦關於你 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	會讓道路更安全許多 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprize的創辦人彼得•戴曼迪斯談到他如何幫助史蒂芬•霍金實現他前往太空的夢想 , 藉由一起飛行到上層的大氣中 , 並在零g中體驗到無重力 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、簡短的談話、空間、科技、宇宙、宇宙 。
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	彼得•戴曼迪斯在史蒂芬•霍金上 , 在g0g中 ,
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	認識我的人都知道我有多麼熱衷於打開太空邊境 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給世界重力專家--無重力的經驗--那真是不可思議 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴你們那個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次見到他 , 透過基因組學的考古獎 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們所舉辦的競賽 , 第二個xprize , 讓第一個團隊在10天內完成100個人類基因組定序 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有所謂的基因體100個個個體 , 我們定序為其中的一部分 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡特椅子就是那個事件 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇到了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想是去太空旅行 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你去那裡 , 但我可以帶你進入無重力中 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他說: 「 絕對是 , 是的 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	嗯 , 地球上唯一能體驗zerog的方法 , 其實是搭乘悖論飛行 , 無重力飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你搭飛機 , 飛過頂端 , 沒有體重25秒 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	回來 , 你的體重是兩倍
you do it again and again .	你一而再 , 再而三地
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得到8 , 10分鐘的無重力──太空總署如何訓練他們的太空人──多久 。
we set out to do this .	我們開始著手做這件事 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才開始營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們宣布要飛stephenhawking
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一間政府機關和一間公司的航空管理員說 , 你瘋了 , 別這樣做 , 你要殺了那個傢伙 。
and he wanted to go .	他也想去 。
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們很努力取得所有的許可 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們在甘迺迪太空中心坐下來 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們舉辦了一場媒體大會 , 我們宣佈我們的目的是要做一個零拋物面鏡 , 給他25秒的零和 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果順利的話 , 我們可能會做三個拋物面鏡 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	嗯 , 我們問他為什麼想上去做這個 。
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	他所說的 , 對我來說 , 非常動人 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命正不斷增加 , 遭受災難的風險......
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為 , 如果它不進入太空 , 人類就沒有未來 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	所以我想要鼓勵公眾對空間的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們帶他到甘迺迪太空中心 , 在美國太空總署的飛天車裡面 , 進入zerog飛機的後面 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們有大約20個人捐款我們募款15萬美元捐款給和我們一起飛翔的兒童慈善團體 。
a few tedsters here .	這裡有幾位ted人 。
we set up a whole er .	我們設立了一整個急診室
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四個急診室醫生和兩位護士在飛機上 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們在監測他的血液、他的心跳、他的血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	我們有一切都以緊急狀況為出發點 ; 天知道 , 你不想傷害這個世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭降落設施起飛 , 那裡的太空梭起飛 , 降落 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	而我和我的夥伴拜倫.里克騰伯格和我很小心地把他吊成零 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他在那裡 , 我們就讓他去體驗無重力是怎樣的 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	在那第一個拋物面鏡之後 , 你知道 , 醫生說了一切都很棒 。 他在微笑 , 然後我們說 , 走吧 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二次拋物線飛行 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們真的在向艾薩克牛頓爵士致敬一顆蘋果 , 因為霍金教授在劍橋的座椅和牛頓一樣 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四次 , 第五次和第六次 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	和第七、第八節 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這位男子看起來不像一個65歲的輪椅人 。
he was so happy .	他好高興 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們活在珍貴的珠寶上 , 在我們的一生中 , 我們正在離開這個星球 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請加入我們加入這場史詩般的冒險
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫療動畫師davidbolinsky呈現出驚人的3分鐘動畫 , 呈現出細胞內的繁忙生命 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、醫療、科學、科技、視覺化 ,
david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinsky活化了一個細胞
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是個醫學插畫家 , 我來自稍微不同的觀點 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	我一直在觀察 , 自從我長大以來 , 藝術和美的真與美的表達方式 , 以及科學中的真與美 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這兩件事都是在它們的右邊 , 它們都有很美好的事物 , 會讓它們真與美 , 成為理想的事物 , 可以被科學和數學的觀點看 , 幾乎就像是科學家會想要約會的理想雙胞胎 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些是 「 真相 」 的表達方式是令人敬畏的事物 , 意思是它們是你能崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是強大的理想 , 不可思議 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨一無二的 。 它們有時是很有用的 , 通常是很久以後 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	你現在可以把一些圖片捲起來 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看著我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真與美往往對不在科學領域的人來說是不透明的 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們是用一種形容美的事物 , 通常只能讓你了解語言 , 和研究對象的語言和語法 , 來表達出真與美 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你看宇宙常數 , 那裡有人類的理想 , 在那裡你會發現生命必須從描述宇宙的數字進化而來 , 這些是非常難以理解的事物 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我被教導我身為醫學插畫師的訓練之後 , 我就試著去做的事 , 他是雕塑家 , 也是我的視覺導師 , 我想要想找出一種方法 , 來幫助人們了解生物科學的真與美 , 透過動畫、用圖片、說故事 , 讓不必要的事物不見得能被人們帶來 , 且能被教導 , 且能被理解 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今的學生通常會沉浸在一個環境中 , 他們所學到的 , 是受測者有真與美 , 嵌在其中 , 但他們被教導的方式是被拿來做比較 , 被吸引到事實和美麗並不總是顯而易見的地步 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	這就像是雞湯的舊食譜 , 你把雞煮熟 , 直到香味不見了 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想對學生這樣做 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開放教育
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	幾年前 , 我在哈佛大學的robertlue接到一通電話 , 在分子和細胞生物學部門 , 他問我我和我的團隊是否有興趣 , 並願意真正改變哈佛的醫療和科學教育是怎麼做的 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始著手一個探索細胞的專案計畫 , 探究分子和細胞生物學中與生俱來的真與美 , 讓學生可以了解一個更大的圖片 , 可以把這些事實掛在上面 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們可以有一個心智圖像 , 把細胞當作一個大型、繁忙、複雜的城市 , 被微機械人佔據 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	而這些微機械真的是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 世界各地都很羨慕奈米科技專家 , 自導性、強大、精確性、精確的裝置 , 都是用一串胺基酸做成的 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	這些微機械讓細胞移動
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們能驅動細胞複製的方式 。 它們能驅動我們的心臟 。
they power our minds .	它們驅動了我們的心靈 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以 , 我們想要做的是 , 找出我們要如何把這個故事變成一個動畫 , 它會是哈佛生物visions的中心點 , 它是一個哈佛大學為分子和細胞生物學所設立的網站 , 它會除了所有的文字資訊以外 , 把所有的教學內容都放在一起 , 讓這些學生能夠將細胞內化 , 看成它的真與美 , 並且能夠研究這個觀點 , 讓他們的想像力會被激發出來 , 以至於他們能夠發掘出新的生命 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子是怎麼組合在一起的 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們和一個主題合作 , 也就是 , 你有巨噬細胞 , 它們會從微血管向下流動 , 它們會觸碰微血管壁的表面 , 它們會從微血管壁上的細胞取得資訊 , 它們會被這些資訊 , 這些資訊會在外面的某處被發炎 , 它們無法看見和感知到 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們得到的資訊會讓他們停下來 , 造成他們內化 , 使他們需要製造所有造成他們改變形狀的各個部分 , 並嘗試脫離這種微血管 , 找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達我們必須與哈佛的科學家和資料庫模型結合這些原子精確的分子並找出它們如何移動 , 找出它們的做法 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	並想出如何以真相為真 , 實現當時的狀況 , 但事實並非如此 , 細胞裡的群眾會阻礙受害者的發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	我要給你們看的是一部三分鐘讀者消化的版本 , 是我們製作的這部電影的第一個面向 。 這是一個持續進行的專案計畫 , 要再過四、五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	我希望你們看看這個 , 看看細胞製造的路徑 , 這些小型步行機器 , 它們叫做kinesins , 採用這些巨大的載量 , 用相對大小的螞蟻來挑戰螞蟻 。
run the movie , please .	來執行電影 , 拜託 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些能驅動細胞內部的機器 , 真的相當驚人 , 它們是所有生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機器彼此互動 。
they pass information to each other .	他們會把資訊傳給彼此 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們會造成細胞內不同的事發生 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會真的製造它在果蠅所需的零件 , 從讀取基因的分子所帶來的資訊 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡的每個人 , 都有可能 , 沒有這些微機械 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 沒有這些機器 , 真的會讓這次的出席率變大 , 克里斯 , 真的很激烈 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞的fedex遞送小傢伙 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫作 「 松果 」 , 他拉了一包 , 裡面裝滿了全新的製造蛋白質 , 到細胞中所需的任何地方 , 不論是對一個細胞膜 , 不論是對一個器官 , 不論是對製造東西或修復什麼東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	而我們每個人大約有十萬個這種東西在你每一百兆個細胞中跑來跑去 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你有多懶惰的感覺 , 你都不是本質上什麼都不做 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以當你們回家後 , 我希望你們能想想這一點 , 想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	並思考一些我們正在學習的關於細胞機械的東西 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們找出了所有正在發生的事情 , 相信我 , 一旦我們搞清楚到底發生了什麼事 , 我們就真的能夠對我們健康所做的事有很大的掌控權 , 用我們在未來世代所做的事 , 以及我們能活多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能用這個來發掘更多的真相 , 和更多的美 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但 , 非常驚人的是這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 已經足夠意識到它們所需的細胞需要的是什麼 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	它們一起運作 。 它們讓細胞做它需要做的事 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	他們同心協力 , 幫助我們的身體 , 巨大的實體他們將永遠看不到適當的功能 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	享受剩下的節目 。 謝謝大家 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝琪•布朗頓計劃在她的旅行車上住了一年 , 看到了這個國家 , 但當憂鬱症開始 , 以及她的自由工作結束時 , 她的露營旅程變成了無家可歸 。 在這個親密的演講中 , 她描述了她的經歷 , 讓她成為美國無家可歸的人 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、生活、個人成長、貧窮、社會改變、社會、說故事、說故事 。
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	beckyblanton:我是無家可歸的那一年 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是作家和記者 , 我也是個瘋狂好奇的人 , 所以 , 身為記者 , 在22年間 , 我學會了怎麼做很多新事 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到如何做一件事 , 就是變得隱形 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成為了無家可歸者之一 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	在我父親在同年二月去世後 , 我辭去了報紙編輯的工作 , 決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死亡讓我非常難受 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	在我這麼做時 , 我有很多事想要去感受和處理 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一生都在露營 。 然後我決定在旅行車裡住了一年 , 去做這件事會像一趟漫長的露營旅行 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以 , 我把我的貓、我的推特推車、我的露營裝備都塞進了1975年的雪佛蘭旅行車 , 開車到日落 , 完全沒有意識到三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	一:社會等同於生活在一個永久的結構中 , 甚至是一片粉碎 , 以人的身分擁有價值 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	二:我沒意識到 , 其他人的負面觀點有多快可能會影響我們的現實 , 只要我們讓它發生 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	三:我沒意識到 , 無家可歸是種態度 , 而不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在旅行車裡很棒 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地洗澡 , 定期吃飯 ,
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間放鬆和悲傷 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但接著 , 我父親的死亡讓我感到憤怒和沮喪 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 。 而我必須得到一份全職的工作來支付這些帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	一個很溫和的春天變成很熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	而且在任何地方都不可能停車 , 不用很明顯地 , 我有一隻貓和一隻狗 , 真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓來了 , 穿過車廂的一扇開窗 ,
the doggy went into doggy day care .	小狗進入日照護 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我能夠 , 我都會在辦公大樓和卡車站使用員工淋浴間 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或是我在公共休息室清洗
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜間車廂的溫度很少降到華氏80度以下 , 讓睡眠變得困難或無法入睡 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱中腐爛 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	我胸口的冰塊在數小時之內就融化了 , 相當悲慘 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我負擔不起找到一間公寓 , 或負擔不起一間公寓 , 可以讓我有旋轉推車和貓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄他們 , 所以我待在旅行車裡 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當熱能讓我病得太重 , 無法在晚上走50英尺到公共廁所時 , 我用桶子和垃圾袋當廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天天氣進來時 , 溫度降低在冷凍之下 。 他們待在那裡 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	而我面對著全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上都停在不一樣的地方 , 這樣我會避免被警察察察察察覺到 , 並感到困惑 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我感到自己無法掌控自己的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道它是何時或如何發生的 , 但我從一個有才華的作家和記者變成了無家可歸的女性 , 住在旅行車裡 , 吸一口氣 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒有改變 。 我的智商沒有下降 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的才華、我的正直、我的價值觀、關於我的一切 , 仍然是一樣的 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我不知怎麼地改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我旋轉得越來越深 , 陷入憂鬱 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最後有人把我稱為無家可歸的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	然後我去了 , 三天沒洗澡
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我和排隊的任何人一樣驚慌和沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是沒喝醉或很高 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當幾個無家可歸的男人意識到 , 包括一個前大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不無家可歸 。 你為什麼真的在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家可歸的人並沒有把我視為無家可歸 , 但我做到了 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	接著教授聽了我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有一份工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的遊民沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給我的抗藥反應讓我有憂鬱症 , 讓我有自殺傾向 。 我記得我在想: 「 如果我殺了自己 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	一個朋友告訴我 , 不久之後 , 她聽到提姆•魯塞特 , 他是全國知名的記者 , 一直在談我在國家t.v.
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫過一篇關於我父親的文章 , 在他死前的那一年 , 是在提姆的新書裡 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他當時正在做演講電路 。 他在談我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我意識到timrussert , 前主持人 " 碰撞媒體 " 時 , 是在談我的寫作 , 當時我住在沃爾瑪超市停車場的旅行車裡 , 我開始笑了 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑是因為它到了哪裡 , 我是作家 , 還是無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	所以我去了書店 , 找到了提姆的書
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	然後我站在那裡 。 然後我重新讀我的文章 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是個作家 。
i was a writer .	我是個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	在那之後不久 , 我搬回了田納西 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我和朋友住在旅行車和沙發衝浪之間的改變 。
and i started writing again .	然後我又開始寫作
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	到了隔年的夏天 , 我是一名職業記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	當時我贏得獎項 。 我住在自己的公寓裡
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	而我不再是隱形的 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	成千上萬的人 , 全職兼職 , 住在他們的車裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續污名化並犯罪化生活在你的車輛或街道上 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以無家可歸 , 工作無家可歸 , 主要還是隱形 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇過一個人 , 讓他們參與 , 鼓勵他們 , 並提供希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神可以克服任何事物 , 如果它有希望的話 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是來這裡做無家可歸的海報女孩 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是來這裡鼓勵你們捐錢給下一個你認識的乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我來這裡是要告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不是住在哪裡、在哪裡睡覺 , 或是在任何時候 , 他們的人生狀況是什麼 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前我住在沃爾瑪超市停車場的旅行車裡 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是 , 總是找到一個方法 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxchange , 泰國的 「 保險套先生 」 , 梅秋維拉維拉迪亞 , 帶領我們走過全國大膽的計劃 , 提高生活水準 , 從1970年代開始 。 第一步:人口控制 。 而這意味著很多坦白、好笑 , 且非常有效的談到保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學、科學、
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	梅秋.維拉迪達:保險套先生如何讓泰國變得更好 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	四十年前 , 當我還是個年輕人時 , 這個國家非常非常貧窮 , 有許多許多人生活在貧窮之中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定要做點什麼 , 但我們不是從福利計畫開始 , 也不是貧窮減少計畫 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家庭規劃開始 , 遵循一個非常成功的孕育兒童健康活動 , 一組活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	所以基本上 , 沒有人會接受家庭計畫 , 如果他們的孩子沒有存活下來 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以 , 第一步:去孩子們 , 去媽媽們 , 然後跟著家庭規劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不僅僅是兒童死亡率 , 你還需要家庭計劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在讓我帶各位回到為什麼我們需要做這件事 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的案例 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每個家庭有七個小孩在成長率極高 , 只有3.3% 。
there was just no future .	只是沒有未來 。

the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	女性們說: 「 我們同意 。 我們會用藥丸 , 但我們需要一位醫生來開藥片 。 」 我們的醫生很少 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們沒有把 「 不 」 當作答案 ; 我們把 「 不 」 視為一個問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去找護士和助產士 , 他們也是女性 , 在解釋該如何使用藥丸時 , 做了很棒的工作 。

what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	其他80%的人會獨自離開他們 , 說: 「 嗯 , 他們不是醫療人員 。 」

so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以 , 就這樣 。 我們去找那些被視為問題的成因的人 , 成為解決方案 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論是哪裡的人 , 都可以和婦女一起看到船隻 , 賣東西是漂浮的市場銷售香蕉和螃蟹 , 還有避孕用品 , 不論你在哪裡找到人 , 你都會在泰國找到避孕用品 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	然後我們決定 , 為何不去宗教 , 因為在菲律賓 , 天主教會的教會相當強烈 , 泰國人民也是佛教徒 。

over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	超過25萬人被教導關於家庭計劃 , 用新的字母a計劃 , b是為了生育 , c是保險套 , 我是為了iud , v是保險套 。

and before long , the condom was know as the girl's best friend .	不久後 , 保險套就被視為女孩最好的朋友了 。
in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對窮人來說 , 鑽石不會變成這樣 , 所以保險套才是女孩最好的朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年推出了第一個小額貸款計畫 , 組織出來的女性說: 「 我們只想借給實踐家庭規劃的女性 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 照顧你的懷孕
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你不懷孕 , 你可以從我們身上拿出貸款 。 」
and that was run by them .	那是他們經營的 。
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	過了35/36年 , 還在持續下去 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村落發展銀行的一部分 ; 它不是真的銀行 , 但它是小額貸款 。
and we didn't need a big organization to run it it was run by the villagers themselves .	我們不需要一個大型組織來運作 , 由村民們自己經營 。
and you probably hardly see a thai man there , it's always women , women , women , women .	你可能幾乎看不到泰國人 , 那裡總是女人、女人、女人、女人 。
and then we thought we'd help america , because america's been helping everyone , whether they want help or not .	然後我們認為我們會幫助美國 , 因為美國一直在幫助每一個人 , 不論他們想要協助與否 。
and this is on the fourth of july .	而這是在七月四日 。
we decided to provide vasectomy to all men , but in particular , american men to the front of the queue , right up to the ambassador's residence during his [unclear] .	我們決定為所有男性提供血管切除術 , 但特別是 , 美國男士們到排隊前面 , 直接到大使館在他的[不清楚] 。

obviously , he's had his vasectomy because his hotdog is half eaten , and he was very happy .	很明顯 , 他有他的血管切除術 , 因為他的熱狗一半吃了 , 他非常高興 。

i'm not sure whether cocacola followed us , or we followed cocacola , but we're good friends .	我不確定可口可樂是否跟著我們 , 或我們跟隨可口可樂 , 但我們是好朋友 。
and so that's the case of everyone joining in .	這就是每個人加入的情況 。
we didn't have a strong government . we didn't have lots of doctors .	我們沒有強勢的政府 。 我們沒有很多醫生 。
but it's everybody's job who can change attitude and behavior .	但每個人都能改變態度和行為 。

every ministry , even judges , had to be involved in aids education everyone and we said the public , institutions , religious institutions , schools everyone was involved .	每一位行政部 , 甚至法官都必須參與愛滋病教育--每一個人--我們都說了--公共、機構、宗教機構、學校-每個人都參與其中 。

and then we went down one more step .	然後再下一步
these are primary school kids third , fourth grade going to every household in the village , every household in the whole of thailand , giving aids information and a condom to every household , given by these young kids .	這些是小學三 , 四年級的孩子 , 到村子裡的每個家庭 , 整個泰國的每個家庭 , 提供愛滋病的資訊和保險套給每個家庭 , 給這些年輕孩子 。
and no parents objected , because we were trying to save lives , and this was a lifesaver .	沒有父母會反對 , 因為我們試著拯救生命 , 這是一隻救命者 。
and we said , " everyone needs to be involved . "	我們說: 「 每個人都需要參與 。 」

and then we have this captain condom , with his harvard mba , going to schools and night spots .	接著 , 我們有這位船長的保險套 , 帶著他的哈佛mba , 到學校和夜點 。

and then we gave condoms out everywhere on the streets everywhere , everywhere .	然後我們在街上到處提供保險套 , 到處都是 。

and also , in traffic , the policemen give you condoms our " cops and rubbers " programs .	此外 , 在交通上 , 警察會給你保險套 , 我們的 「 警察和摩擦器 」 計畫 。
so , can you imagine new york policemen giving out condoms ?	所以 , 你能想像紐約警察放出保險套嗎 ?
of course i can . and they'd enjoy it immensely ; i see them standing around right now , everywhere .	當然我可以 。 而且他們會很享受 , 我看到他們現在就站在那裏 , 到處都是 。

and these were the condoms that we introduced .	這些是我們推出的保險套 。
one says , " weapon of mass protection . "	一個說: 「 大規模保護的武器 。 」

and then finally , in thailand we're buddhist , we don't have a god , so instead , we say , " in rubber we trust . "	最後 , 在泰國 , 我們是佛教徒 , 我們沒有神 , 所以 , 我們說: 「 在橡膠裡 , 我們信任 。 」
so you can see that we added everything to our endeavor to make life better for the people .	所以你可以看出 , 我們把一切加到我們的努力中 , 讓人民的生活更美好 。
we had condoms in all the refrigerators in the hotels and the schools , because alcohol impairs judgment .	我們在旅館和學校都有保險套 , 因為酒精會損害判斷力 。
and then what happened ?	然後發生了什麼事 ?
after all this time , everybody joined in .	在這段時間之後 , 每個人都加入了 。
according to the u . n . , new cases of hiv declined by 90 percent , and according to the world bank , 7 . 7 million lives were saved .	根據聯合國的統計 , 愛滋病的新案例下降了90% , 根據世界銀行的統計 , 770萬人的性命被拯救了 。
otherwise there wouldn't be many thais walking around today .	否則今天不會有很多泰國人走來走去 。
so it just showed you , you could do something about it .	所以它只顯示了 , 你可以做些什麼 。
90 percent of the funding came from thailand .	90%的資金來自泰國
there was political commitment , some financial commitment , and everybody joined in the fight .	有政治上的承諾 , 一些財務上的承諾 , 每個人都加入了戰鬥 。
so just don't leave it to the specialists and doctors and nurses .	所以 , 不要把它留給專科醫生、醫生和護士 。
we all need to help .	我們都需要幫助 。
and then we decided to help people out of poverty , now that we got aids somewhat out of the way this time , not with government alone , but in cooperation with the business community .	接著 , 我們決定幫助人們脫離貧窮 , 現在我們得到了愛滋病 , 有點不符合政府的方式 , 而不是單靠政府 , 而是與商業社群合作 。
because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為窮人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能 , 還能取得信用 。
those are the things to be provided by the business community .	那些是由商業界提供的 。
we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們試著把他們變成赤腳創業家 , 小商人 。
the only way out of poverty is through business enterprise .	脫離貧窮的唯一方法 , 就是透過企業企業 。
so , that was done .	所以 , 這件事就完成了 。
the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	經費從公司轉變成村莊 , 透過 「 樹木移植 」
it's not a free gift .	而不是免費的禮物
they plant the trees , and the money goes into their microcredit fund , which we call the village development bank .	他們種植樹木 , 錢會進入他們的微型貸款基金 , 我們稱之為村落發展銀行 。
everybody joins in , and they feel they own the bank , because they have brought the money in .	每個人都加入 , 覺得自己擁有銀行 , 因為他們把錢帶進來了 。
and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	在你能借到錢之前 , 你需要接受訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信 , 如果你想要幫助窮人 , 那些生活在貧窮之中的人 , 信用的權利一定是人權 。
access to credit must be a human right .	信用的管道一定是人權 。
otherwise they'll never get out of poverty .	否則他們永遠脫離不了貧困
and then before getting a loan , you must be trained .	然後在取得貸款之前 , 你一定要接受訓練 。
here's what we call a " barefoot mba , " teaching people how to do business so that , when they borrow money , they'll succeed with the business .	以下是我們所謂的 「 赤腳mba 」 , 教導人們如何做生意 , 這樣 , 當他們借錢時 , 他們就會成功地做生意 。

your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧手機可能會覺得像個朋友 , 但真正的朋友會給你微笑一會兒 。 在ted2013年 , 凱勒•里納多•戴莫斯 , 他是智慧型手機驅動的迷你機器人 , 他們能在散步上移動 , 將一杯咖啡滑過桌 , 用可編寫的表情來回應你 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	kellerrinaudo:一個迷你機器人是由你的手機所供電的 。
so just by a show of hands , how many of you all have a robot at home ?	所以 , 只是舉手 , 在座有多少人在家裡都有機器人 ?
not very many of you .	不是你們很多人 。
okay . and actually of those hands , if you don't include roomba how many of you have a robot at home ?	好的 。 實際上 , 如果你不包括roba , 你們當中有多少人在家裡有機器人 ?
that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這就是我們在romotive想解決的問題我和其他二十位書呆子在romotive迷戀解決的問題 。
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以我們真的想建造一個任何人都可以使用的機器人 , 不論你是八歲還是八十歲 。
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 那真的是個很困難的問題 , 因為你得要建造一個小型、可攜帶的機器人 , 它不但能負擔得起 , 它還得要是人們真的想要回家 , 還能在他們的孩子身邊做的事 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這個機器人不能令人毛骨悚然 , 或不毛骨悚然 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該要友善和可愛 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo的機器人使用你已經知道的裝置 , 把你的iphone當作他的大腦 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	藉由iphone處理器的力量 , 我們就能創造出一台飛行器 , 讓它有wi-fi的可視化和電腦視覺 , 只要一百五十美元 , 這大約是過去這類機器人所花費的百分之一 。
when romo wakes up , he's in creature mode .	當romo醒來時 , 他正處於生物模式
so he's actually using the video camera on the device to follow my face .	所以他其實是用裝置上的攝影機跟著我的臉 。
if i duck down , he'll follow me .	如果我向下揮拳 , 他會跟著我走 。
he's wary , so he'll keep his eyes on me .	他很溫暖 , 所以他會一直盯著我看 。
if i come over here , he'll turn to follow me .	如果我來這裡 , 他會轉身跟著我 。
if i come over here he's smart .	如果我來這裡 , 他很聰明 ,
and if i get too close to him , he gets scared just like any other creature .	如果我太靠近他 , 他就會像其他生物一樣害怕 。
so in a lot of ways , romo is like a pet that has a mind of his own .	所以 , 在很多方面 , romo就像一隻有自己的心智的寵物 。
thanks , little guy .	謝謝 , 小傢伙 。
and if i want to explore the world uhoh , romo's tired if i want to explore the world with romo , i can actually connect him from any other ios device .	如果我想要探索世界--呃 , romo累了--如果我想用romo探索這個世界 , 我可以真的把他從任何ios的設備聯繫起來 。

but the most important thing about romo is that we wanted to create something that was literally completely intuitive .	但關於romo , 最重要的一點是 , 我們想要創造出完全直覺的東西 。

thank you , scott .	謝謝你 , 史考特 。

so he actually streams twoway audio and video between any two smart devices .	所以他在任何兩個智慧裝置之間傳輸雙向音頻和影片 。
