you can imagine an eightyearold girl , for example , who has an iphone , and her mom buys her a robot .	你可以想像一個八歲大的女孩 , 例如 , 她有iphone , 她的媽媽買了她一個機器人 。
that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那個女孩可以拿她的iphone , 把它放在機器人上 , 寄一封電子郵件給祖母 , 住在國家的另一端 。
grandma can log into that robot and play hideandgoseek with her granddaughter for fifteen minutes every single night , when otherwise she might only be able to get to see her granddaughter once or twice a year .	奶奶可以登入那個機器人 , 和她的孫女一起玩藏著躲藏的玩具 , 每天晚上十五分鐘 , 否則她可能一年只能看到孫女一、兩次 。
so those are a couple of the really cool things that romo can do today .	這些是romo今天能做的一些很酷的事 。
but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但我只想談談我們未來正在努力的事物 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這其實是我們其中一個工程師 , dom , 在一個週末建成的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	建立在google的開放架構上 , 叫做blockly 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這讓你可以拖著、丟下這些semantic程式碼的積木 , 為你想要的機器人創造任何行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何寫程式碼來為romo創造一個行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	你可以在瀏覽器中模擬這種行為 , 也就是你在左邊看到romo在做的事 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以把它下載到你的機器人上 , 在現實生活中執行它 , 在現實生活中執行程式 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	然後如果你有你感到驕傲的事物 , 你可以和世界上所有擁有機器人的人分享它 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所以所有這些無線網路的機器人 , 實際上是互相學習的 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們之所以如此專注於建造機器人 , 讓每個人都能訓練 , 是因為我們認為個人機器人中最引人注目的使用案例是個人的 。
they change from person to person .	會因人而改變 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以 , 我們認為 , 如果你要在你家裡裝一個機器人 , 那機器人應該是你自己想像的一種展現 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	所以我希望我能告訴你個人機器人的未來是什麼樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我完全不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們確實知道的是 , 它不是十年、一百億美金 , 或一個大型的人形機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	現今個人機器人的未來正在發生 , 它將取決於小型、敏捷的機器人 , 比如romo , 以及像你們這樣的人的創造力 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以 , 我們迫不及待地想讓你們全部的機器人 , 我們迫不及待地想看看你們建造了什麼 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和行動主義者伊莎貝爾•阿言德討論女性、創意、女權主義的定義 , 當然 , 還有在這場演說中的熱情 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球議題、愛、養育、說故事、女人、世界文化 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾•阿言德訴說著熱情的故事
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常謝謝你 。 非常可怕 , 能來到這裡是最聰明的 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我來這裡是要告訴你們一些關於熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有一個猶太人說我很愛
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	什麼比真相更真實 ? 答案:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是個說故事的人 。 我想傳達出比真相更真實的東西 , 關於我們共同的人性 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都讓我感興趣 , 有些困擾 , 直到我最後寫下它們為止 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	某些主題不斷出現:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治和社會議題、自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我意識到我們身邊的奧秘 , 所以我寫下巧合 , 預兆 , 情緒 , 夢想 , 自然的力量 , 魔法 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去的20年中 , 我出版了幾本書 , 但我一直活在匿名的地方 , 直到2006年2月 , 當我帶著奧運旗在義大利的冬季奧運時 ,
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這使我成為了名人 。 現在 , 人們認得我在macy's , 而我的孫子們認為我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	允許我告訴各位我那四分鐘的名氣 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	其中一個奧運典禮的組織者 , 開幕典禮的一名 , 打電話給我 , 說我被選為旗幟管理員之一 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回覆說 , 這肯定是錯誤認同的案例 , 因為我從運動員的身份得到最大利益 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	其實 , 我甚至不確定我可以不用助行器繞過體育場 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這不是笑話 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這是第一次 , 只有女性會帶著奧運旗 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五位女性 , 代表五大洲 , 和三位奧運金牌得主 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 很自然地 , 我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	一件制服 , 她說 , 並要求我的測量結果 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我對我自己有個遠景 , 看上去像米其林人 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	到了二月中期 , 我在土爾丁 , 在那裡 , 充滿熱情的群眾歡呼 , 當時有80個奧運團隊在街上 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些運動員犧牲了在遊戲中競爭的一切 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都值得贏 , 但還有運氣的元素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	一塊積雪 , 一英寸的冰 , 風的力量 , 可以決定種族或遊戲的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 最重要的是訓練或運氣是心臟 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有無懼和堅定的心才會得到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	這一切都和熱情有關 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	渦輪的街道上滿是紅色海報宣佈奧運會的口號 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情生活在這裡 。 不是一直都是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心是驅使我們 , 並決定我們的命運 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	那是我書中角色需要的:充滿熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要mavericks , 異議人士 , 冒險家 , 局外人和叛逆者 , 他們問問題 , 彎曲規則 , 並冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座各位一樣的人 ,
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	有常識的好人並不會做出有趣的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	他們只會做好的前配偶 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育場的綠色房間裡 , 我遇見了其他旗手:三位運動員 , 演員蘇珊莎蘭登和蘇菲雅羅蘭 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	還有 , 兩位有熱情心的女性:旺加里•馬塔伊 , 來自肯亞的諾貝爾獎得主 , 她種植了三千萬棵樹 。 透過這麼做 , 她改變了土壤、天氣 , 在非洲的某些地方 , 當然還有許多村莊的經濟狀況 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	而索馬利哺乳 , 一位柬埔寨活動家 , 他熱情地對抗兒童賣淫 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	當她十四歲時 , 她的祖父賣她到一間妓院 。
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們 , 小女孩被男人強暴 , 他們相信和很年輕的處女做愛 , 會治癒她們免於愛滋病 。
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	而被迫每天接收五、十五個客戶的妓院 , 如果他們反抗 , 他們就會受到電力折磨 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在我收到制服的綠色房間裡 ,
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這不是我平常穿的那種服裝 , 但它離我所預期的米其林男人服裝很遠 。 不是很糟 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像個冰箱
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	但 , 大部分的旗幟師 , 除了蘇菲雅羅蘭 , 美麗和熱情的普遍象徵 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲雅超過七十歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她很性感 , 很小 , 很高 , 有著很深的棕色 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	現在 , 你要怎麼樣才能有深色的棕色皮膚 , 沒有皺紋 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	當在電視訪談中問到: 「 她怎麼可能看起來這麼好 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回答: 「 姿勢 。 我的背總是直 , 我不製造老人的噪音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	所以 , 這裡有一些免費的建議 , 來自地球上最美麗的女性之一 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	沒有追求 , 沒有咳嗽 , 沒有小麥 , 沒有和自己說話 , 沒有偏遠 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她並沒有這麼說 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	大約在午夜的某個時點 , 我們被召喚到體育館的翅膀 , 聲響者宣佈奧運旗 , 音樂一路開展 , 相同的音樂 , 從這裡開始 , 艾迪亞大遊行 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲雅羅蘭就在我面前 , 她比我高 , 不計頭髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她優雅地走路 , 就像非洲大草原上的長頸鹿 , 肩上拿著旗子 。 我在我的尖端拿著旗子 , 手上拿著旗子 , 這樣我的頭其實在該死的旗幟底下 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	當然 , 所有的攝影機都是在蘇菲雅 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	那對我來說是很幸運的 , 因為在我出現的大部分媒體照片中 , 雖然通常都在蘇菲雅的雙腿之間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	一個大部分男人都很想成為的地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最棒的四分鐘就是奧林匹克體育館裡的人 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	當我這樣說時 , 我的丈夫會被冒犯 , 雖然我已經向他解釋 , 我們在私下做的事通常會花不到四分鐘 , 所以他不應該親自拿 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我有這四個偉大的時刻的所有按鈕 , 因為我不想忘記它們 , 老年時破壞了我的腦細胞 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想永遠帶著奧運熱情的關鍵字 。
so here's a tale of passion .	所以 , 這裡有個關於熱情的故事 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	一年是1998年 , 地點是剛果tutsi難民營的監獄營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順道一提 , 世界上80%的難民和流離失所的人都是女性和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以稱這個地方為剛果一個死亡營地 , 因為那些沒被殺死的人 , 會死於疾病或餓死 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的主角是一位年輕女子 , 蘿絲•瑪諾 , 還有她的孩子 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕了一顆寡婦
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵強迫她看著她的丈夫遭受折磨和殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知何故 , 她想讓七個孩子活下去 , 幾個月後 , 她生了預產的雙胞胎 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用一根棍子割斷了陰莖 , 然後用自己的頭髮將它綁起來 。
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她把雙胞胎命名為 「 營地指揮官 」 , 以獲得他們的喜愛 , 並用黑茶來餵他們食物 , 因為她的牛奶無法維持它們 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當士兵在她的牢房闖進來強暴她最老的女兒時 , 她抓著她並拒絕放手 , 即使當他們拿著一把槍抵著她的頭 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎麼的 , 家人存活了16個月 , 接著 , 透過非凡的運氣 , 以及一位年輕美國男子薩夏•查諾夫的熱情之心 , 他想辦法把她放進美國救援的飛機 , 蘿絲•瑪多和她的九個孩子最後到亞利桑那州佩尼克斯•帕尼克斯 , 在那裡 , 他們現在的生活和成長茁壯 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	在斯瓦希里語中 , 繪製地圖文字的意思是偉大的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我書中的主角是堅強且充滿熱情的女性 , 如蘿絲•瑪哥多 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不把它們弄出來 , 不需要這樣做 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 到處都見到他們 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我一生都在和女性合作 。
i know them well .	我很清楚他們 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生於古代 , 在世界末日 , 在一個父系天主教和保守的家庭中 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪五歲時我是個狂暴的女權主義者雖然還沒有接觸到智利 , 所以沒人知道我是怎麼搞的 。
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就會發現 , 要為我的自由付出高價 , 為了質疑父權主義 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興能支付它 , 因為每一擊我都會收到的 , 我就能夠遞送兩次 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 當我的女兒寶拉在她二十多歲時 , 她對我說女權主義是約會 , 我應該繼續前進 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們有了難忘的戰鬥 。 女權主義是約會的 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 對於像我女兒這樣的有特權的女性 , 以及我們今天在這裡的所有人 , 但對世界上大部分的姊妹來說 , 她們仍然被迫要婚姻早婚、賣淫、強迫勞動──她們有孩子不想要或不能養活 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們對自己的身體或人生沒有任何控制權 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育 , 也沒有自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴、毆打、有時被無罪殺害 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	對現今大多數西方的年輕女性來說 , 被稱為女權主義者是種侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女權主義從來沒有性感過節 , 但讓我向各位保證 , 它從來沒有阻止我調情 , 我有嚴重的處境 , 缺乏男性 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女性主義不是死了 , 不是死了 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它已經進化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個名詞 , 改變它 , 對女神來說 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱它為phrodite , 或維納斯 , 或bimbo , 或不論你想要什麼 ; 只要我們了解它是什麼 , 我們就會支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	所以 , 這裡有另一個關於熱情的故事 , 這是個悲傷的故事 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	這個地方是孟加拉一個村莊的小女子診所
the year is 2005 .	這一年是2005年 。
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是一位年輕的美國牙衛生學家 , 她在三週假期去了診所當志工 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備清潔牙齒 , 但當她到那裡時 , 她發現沒有醫生 , 沒有牙醫 , 診所只是一間滿是蒼蠅的小屋 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	在外面 , 有一行婦女等了好幾個小時才接受治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一位病人因為她有好幾顆腐爛的臼齒 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮了解到 , 唯一的解決方法就是拔掉不好的牙齒 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她沒有申請許可 , 她從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她經常冒險 , 嚇壞了 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有適當的儀器 , 但幸運的是她已經帶來了一些非口味的 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有一顆勇敢且熱情的心 。
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她衝了一陣禱告 , 帶著行動向前走 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 病人親吻她的手
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天 , 衛生學家再抽出許多牙齒 ,
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	第二天早上 , 當她再次來到所謂的診所時 , 她的第一位病人正和丈夫在等著她 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	女子的臉看起來像個西瓜
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	它是如此的腫脹 , 以至於看不到眼睛 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	先生 , 憤怒 , 威脅要殺美國人 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮對她所做過的事感到驚恐 , 但接著 , 翻譯解釋說 , 病人的狀況和手術沒什麼關係 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她的丈夫打敗她 , 因為她不在家準備晚餐 。
millions of women live like this today .	現今有數百萬的女性像這樣生活 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是最窮的窮人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然女性會做世界上三分之二的勞動 , 但卻擁有不到世界資產的1% 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	他們的薪水比男性少 , 如果薪水完全少 , 他們會保持脆弱 , 因為他們沒有經濟獨立 , 且他們不斷受到剝削、暴力和虐待的威脅 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	事實上 , 給予女性教育、工作、控制她們自己的收入、繼承 , 以及自己的財產 , 讓社會受益 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果一個女人被賦予權力 , 她的孩子和她的家人會變得更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家庭繁榮 , 村長繁榮 , 最終整個國家也是如此 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	wangarimaathai去了肯亞的一個村莊
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和婦女談 , 解釋這塊土地是貧瘠的 , 因為他們已經砍伐和賣掉樹木 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓婦女們種植新的樹 , 澆水 , 滴下來 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	在5或6年間 , 他們有一片森林 , 土壤豐富 , 村莊也救了一命 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮和最後退的社會 , 總是那些把女性放下的人 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	但這個顯而易見的事實卻被政府和慈善事業忽略 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	給女人的計畫每一塊錢 , 20塊錢就給了男性的計畫 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性是51%的人類 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	賦予他們能力 , 將會改變一切 , 勝過科技、設計和娛樂 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以向各位保證 , 女性同心協力 , 連結、有知識 , 且受過教育 , 能把和平和繁榮帶到這個脆弱的星球上 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	在今天的任何戰爭中 , 大多數的傷亡是平民百姓 , 主要是女人和小孩 。 她們是相對的傷害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人經營世界 , 看看我們有的混亂 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是我們大多數人都在問的基本問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	參與現有的世界秩序合理嗎 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們想要一個世界 , 在那裡 , 生命是被保存的 , 且生活品質是為每個人豐富的 , 不僅是為了有特權的人 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	在一月的時候 , 我看到一幅fernandobotero的畫展 , 是在柏克萊圖書館 。
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	美國沒有博物館或畫廊 , 除了背著botero的作品之外 , 紐約畫廊也敢展出畫作 , 因為主題是阿布格萊布監獄 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	他們是酷刑的巨大畫作 , 以及權力的濫用 , 在虛擬的bottero風格中 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我沒有辦法把那些影像從我的腦海或心中得到出來 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最害怕的 , 是無罪的力量 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕權力的濫用 , 以及濫用的權力 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們這個物種中 , 雄性領袖定義了現實 , 並強迫其他群體接受那個現實 , 並遵守規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則隨時都在改變 , 但它們總是會受惠 , 在這個案例中 , 「 下滲效應 」 在經濟學上行不通 , 運作得很完美 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	虐待從梯子的頂端往下游到底部 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	婦女和兒童 , 尤其是窮人 , 在最底層
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是男士最多的退役 , 也有人可以虐待女性或孩子 。
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	透過性別、收入、種族和階級 , 我得到了少數人的力量 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為 , 時間是成熟的 , 在我們的文明中做出根本的改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但 , 對於真正的改變 , 我們需要女性的能量在世界管理階層 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要在權力的位置上有相當多的女性 , 我們需要培養男性的女性能量 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	我說的是有年輕心靈的男性 , 當然 ,
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老人是毫無希望的 ; 我們得等他們離開 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我很想擁有蘇菲雅羅蘭的長腿和傳奇的胸部 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但 , 若要做選擇 , 我寧願擁有華格麗•馬塔伊的勇士心 , 索瑪莉•母親、珍妮和玫瑰的馬雅各 。
i want to make this world good .	我想讓這個世界變得美好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 而是好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不呢 ? 這是可行的 。 看看這個房間裡所有的知識、精力、才華和科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	讓我們脫離粉絲 , 捲起袖子 , 熱情地工作 , 創造一個幾乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在一個倫敦大小的城市中 , 三千萬份餐是被服務的 。 但是所有的食物都從哪裡來 ? 建築師卡洛琳鋼鐵討論養活一個城市的日常奇蹟 , 展現出古代食物路線如何塑造了現代世界 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	卡羅琳•史黛爾:食物如何塑造我們的城市 。
how do you feed a city ?	如何養活一座城市 ?
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代最偉大的問題之一 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	然而卻很少被問及 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們理所當然地認為 , 如果我們去商店或餐廳 , 或在大約一小時內進入這間戲院大廳 , 那裡就會有食物在等著我們 , 神奇地從某處來 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你認為 , 每天在倫敦大小的城市 , 足夠的食物都必須被生產、交通、買賣、煮飯、吃飯、丟棄 , 而那種類似的事情 , 每天都要發生在地球上的每一座城市 , 都市被供應食物是很了不起的 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在這樣的地方 , 彷彿它們是世界上最自然的事物 , 忘記了這一點 , 因為我們是動物 , 我們需要吃東西 , 其實我們對自然世界的依賴和我們古老的祖先一樣 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著我們更多人搬進城市 , 自然世界被轉變為非凡的景觀 , 就像我身後的景觀 , 那是在巴西馬托格羅索的大豆田 , 為了養活我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些是非凡的景觀 , 但很少人能看到這些景觀 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	漸漸地 , 這些景觀也不只是餵飽我們 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著更多人搬到城市裡 , 更多人在吃肉 , 以至於全球每年有三分之一的穀物被餵給動物 , 而不是給我們人類的動物 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	由於它需要三倍的穀物 , 實際上需要十倍的穀物來餵飽人類 , 如果它是先通過動物 , 那就不是很有效率的餵養方式 。
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是一個急迫的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到2050年 , 據估計 , 我們的人數將是城市裡的兩倍 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	也估計 , 消費的肉和乳製品將會是兩倍 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以肉類和城市化是手上升的 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	那將會帶來一個巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	在2050年之前 , 六十億個飢餓的食肉食動物 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 。 實際上 , 如果我們隨身攜帶 , 這是我們很不可能解決的問題 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有九千萬公頃的雨林消失在創造新的可耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	雖然在同一時間我們損失了相當大量的現有的耕地供應到鹽化和侵蝕 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們也非常渴望化石燃料 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	大約需要十卡路里來生產我們西方每一卡路里的食物 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	儘管我們生產的成本很高 , 卻不重視食物 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	美國目前生產的食物有一半是被丟棄的 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	要結束這一切 , 在這漫長的過程結束後 , 我們甚至沒有辦法妥善餵飽地球 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	我們當中有十億人過胖 , 同時 , 有十億人餓死 。
none of it makes very much sense .	沒有一個是很合理的 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為現在全球80%的食物交易是由五大跨國企業所掌控的 , 這是一張很嚴格的圖片 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	隨著我們搬進城市 , 世界也在擁抱西方飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們看看未來 , 這是一種不永續的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	所以 , 我們是怎麼走到這一步的 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們該怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	首先 , 要回答一個稍微簡單的問題 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 是這個過程的開端 , 是在東邊的古老過程 , 也就是所謂的肥沃集團 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它的形狀很糟 。
and it was also fertile .	它也是肥沃的 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約一萬年前就在這裡 , 兩項非凡的發明 , 農業和城市化 , 發生在同一個地方 , 同時也發生在同一個地方 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這不是意外 , 因為農業和城市是互相束手無策的 。 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為這是我們古老的祖先第一次發現穀物 , 產生出足夠大且穩定的食物來源 , 足以支撐永久居住地 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看這些定居處是怎樣的 , 我們會發現它們是緊密的 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們圍繞著有生產力的農田 , 被大型神廟的複合體支配 , 像這一個在烏爾 , 事實上 , 靈性化、中央食物分配中心 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為那是神殿整理了收穫 , 聚集在穀物裡 , 提供給神 , 然後再提供上帝不吃回來的穀物給人民 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你願意 , 這些城市的精神和實體生活是由穀物和收穫所支配的 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 每個古老的城市都是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是所有人都這麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	很有名的是 , 羅馬在西元一個世紀前大約有一百萬公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以 , 像這樣的城市是如何自給自足的 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案是我所謂的 「 古老食物里程 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬可以取得海洋 , 這使得它能夠從很遠的地方進口食物 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是唯一能在古代世界做到這一點的方法 , 因為很難在道路上運送食物 , 這很粗糙 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	食物顯然很快就起飛了 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以 , 羅馬有效地為像卡拉奇和埃及等地方打仗 , 只為了在他們的穀物儲備上取得爪子 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 帝國的擴張是一場漫長的軍事化的購物市場 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我很喜歡這個事實 , 我只需要提到這個:羅馬事實上 , 羅馬曾經從倫敦進口牡蠣 , 在一個階段 。 我認為那是非凡的 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬透過它的胃口塑造了它的後代 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 另一件事也發生在工業前的世界 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看十七世紀的倫敦地圖 , 我們可以看到它的穀物 , 來自泰姆斯 , 沿著這張地圖的底部 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以穀物市場到了城市的南方 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	而從他們到便宜的道路也就是主要的市場也是穀物市場
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看看其中一條街道的名字 , 麵包街 , 你可以知道300年前那裡發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	當然對魚也是一樣 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚也來到河裡 。 同樣的道理 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , 比林斯門 , 著名的是倫敦的魚市場 , 直到1980年代中期才開始營運 。
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	想想看 , 這真的很不凡 。
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	其他人都帶著手機到處閒逛 , 看起來像磚頭 , 有點像是很臭的魚類 , 在港口上出現 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是關於城市食物的另一件事:一旦它的根源被建立起來 , 它們就很少會移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉類是非常不同的 , 因為 , 當然 , 動物可以走進城市 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	所以倫敦大部分的肉來自西北方 , 來自蘇格蘭和威爾斯 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以它就進來了 , 抵達西北部的城市 , 這就是為什麼史密斯菲爾德 , 倫敦非常有名的肉市場 , 地點就在上面 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	家禽從東安格利亞來 , 諸如此類的 , 到東北部 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得有點像氣象女子這樣做 。 不管怎樣 , 鳥兒都帶著腳走進來 , 用小畫布保護著我 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	然後當他們撞到便宜的東端時 , 他們就在那裡被賣掉了 , 這就是為什麼這被稱為 「 家禽 」 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看一下在工業時代之前所建立的任何城市地圖 , 你可以追溯食物進來 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你實際上可以看到它是如何被食物所塑造的 , 兩者都是透過閱讀街道的名字 , 這給你很多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街 , 在以前的人生裡 , 就是你在星期五去買你的魚的地方 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但你也必須想像它充滿了食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間是唯一一個食物被買賣的地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看看1830年史密斯菲爾德的畫面 , 你可以看到生活在這樣的城市是非常困難的 , 不知道你的食物是從哪裡來的 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你有星期日午餐 , 可能是你在窗外的三天前 , 它會在你的窗外流出或流出 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	這顯然是一個有機城市 , 一個有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	然後十年後一切都改變了
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年偉大西方的圖像 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 一些最早的火車乘客是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	所以 , 突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場了 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們被從視線和心靈中被屠殺 , 在鄉間某處 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	並通過鐵路來到城市 ,
and this changes everything .	而這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	首先 , 首次能夠在任何地方種植城市 , 真正的大小和形狀 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	以前 , 城市受到地理限制 ; 他們以前得要透過很困難的實體手段來取得食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 它們從地理上被有效地解放了 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	正如你們從這些倫敦地圖所看到的 , 在火車來臨的90年後 , 火車來臨 , 從一個小小的blob就很容易被動物帶進來 , 如此一來 , 到一個很大的流量 , 要和任何人一起進食是非常非常困難的 , 要不論是動物還是人類 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然 , 這只是開端 。 火車來了車道之後 , 真的是這個過程的結局 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	是城市的最終解放從任何明顯與自然的關係中解放出來 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	這種城市沒有氣味 , 沒有氣味 , 沒有氣味 , 肯定沒有人 , 因為沒有人會夢想在這樣的地景中行走 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們為了取得食物而做的是他們在他們的車子裡 , 開車到郊區某處的箱子 , 回來了一週的購物價值 , 想知道地球上該怎麼做 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	而這正是我們與食物和城市的關係 , 完全改變的時刻 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡 , 我們有食物曾經是城市的中心 , 城市的社會核心 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	曾經是社交活動 , 購買和賣食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前會煮飯 ; 現在只要加水 , 或一點點蛋 , 只要做蛋糕之類的 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們聞不到食物 , 看是否可以吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只要在包裝上讀到一個標籤的後面 ,
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	而且我們不重視食物 。 我們不信任它 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不再信任它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	我們不珍惜它 , 而是丟掉它 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食品系統的一個偉大的諷刺 , 就是他們已經做出了他們承諾要讓更加困難的事 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	透過在任何地方、任何地方建立城市 , 它們其實已經讓我們與最重要的關係脫離了關係 , 那就是我們和自然的關係 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	而且 , 它們也讓我們依賴系統 , 讓它們只能傳遞 , 就像我們所看到的一樣 , 是無法永續的 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	那我們該怎麼做呢 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是一個新的問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	五百年前湯瑪斯更問他自己
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他書《烏托邦》的首映 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	那是一系列的半獨立城市 , 如果聽起來很熟悉的話 , 一天走從一個人那裡 , 人人基本上都是農作的 , 在他們後花園裡種植蔬菜 , 把共用餐吃起來 , 等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我想你們可以爭辯說 , 食物是烏托邦的基本定序原則 , 即使從來沒有這樣框架過 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	這是另一個非常有名的 「 烏托邦 」 視覺 , 是埃本納默斯克韋茲的 「 花園城市 」 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的想法:一連串半獨立的城市 , 一小群大都市的東西 , 周圍有可耕作的土地 , 加入鐵路彼此 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	同樣的 , 食物可以被說是他視覺的訂定原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至被建立起來 , 但和默斯克韋茲的這個願景一點關係都沒有 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這就是這些烏托邦的想法的問題 , 認為它們是烏托邦 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是湯瑪斯•摩爾故意使用的字眼 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	那是個笑話 , 因為它從希臘得到了雙重衍生 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可以是指一個好地方 , 或沒有地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為這是一個理想的事物 , 一個想像的事物 。 我們不可能擁有它 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 作為一個概念性的工具 , 可以考慮到人類居住地的深層問題 , 這使得它不太有用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了一個替代方案 , 就是西托邦 , 來自古希臘人 , 「 西托斯 」 為了食物 , 和 「 托托托托 」 等地 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在西托邦了 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個被食物塑造的世界 , 如果我們了解到 , 我們可以把食物當作一個真正強大的工具--一個概念化的工具、設計工具 , 以不同的方式塑造世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以 , 如果我們要這樣做 , 西托邦可能會長什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	我覺得它看起來有點像這樣 。
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我必須用這張投影片 , 只是那隻狗臉上的表情 。
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	但無論如何 , 這是生活的中心的食物 , 在家庭生活的中心 , 被讚頌 , 被享受 , 人們為此佔用時間 。
this is where food should be in our society .	這是食物應在我們社會中的所在地 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但你不可能有這樣的場景 , 除非你有這樣的人 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	順帶一提 , 這些人也可能是男性 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	人們會想到食物 , 他們會想 , 他們會計劃 , 他們可以盯著一堆生菜 , 並且認得這些食物 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 。 我們是網絡的一部分 。
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為若沒有這類人 , 我們就不可能有這樣的地方 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	在這裡 , 我故意選這個 , 因為這是一個男人在買蔬菜 。
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但網絡、食物在當地種植的市場 ,
it's common . it's fresh .	很常見 , 很新鮮 。
it's part of the social life of the city .	成為城市社會生活的一部分
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為若沒有這些 , 你就不可能有這種地方 , 當地種植的食物也是地景的一部分 , 而不只是零和的商品 , 在一些看不見的地獄 。
cows with a view .	牛有著一種觀點 。
steaming piles of humus .	蒸汽堆積如山 ,
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	這基本上是把整個東西結合在一起 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近去多倫多拜訪的一個社區計畫 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	那是一座溫室 , 孩子們被告知關於食物和種植自己食物的一切 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這是一種叫凱文的植物 , 或者它是屬於一個叫做凱文的孩子的植物 。 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	但無論如何 , 這類計畫試圖將我們和大自然重新連結是極為重要的 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 對我來說 , sitopia真的是一種看待的方式 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上就是認知到西托邦已經存在於每個地方的小口袋裡 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	訣竅在於加入它們 , 用食物來當作一種看法 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這樣做 , 我們將不再把城市視為大型、都市化、沒有生產力的b團 , 就像這樣 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們會更像這樣 , 把它們看成是有生產力、有機架構的一部分 , 它們無可避免地是一部分 , 共生的連結 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	但當然 , 那也不是很棒的圖像 , 因為我們不需要再像這樣生產食物了 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要更加思考永續發展 , 這就是為什麼我認為這張圖會為我做個總結 , 是我們需要做的那種思考 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	重新思考食物塑造我們的生活的方式 。
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知道最好的圖片是從650年前開始
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	是阿布羅吉歐•洛倫澤蒂的 「 好的政府寓言 」 。
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	關於城市和鄉村之間的關係
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這個訊息非常清楚 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市照顧國家 , 國家就會照顧城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	我現在要我們問 , 阿姆布洛吉歐•洛倫澤蒂如果他今天畫了這張影像 , 會是什麼樣的畫 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	一個好的政府今天會是什麼樣的寓言 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是一個迫切的問題 。
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	這是我們必須問的 , 我們必須開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們是吃什麼的
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們需要意識到 , 世界也是我們所吃的 。
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們採用這個想法 , 我們可以把食物當作一種強大的工具 , 來塑造世界更好 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	在二十一世紀 , 凱倫•阿姆斯壯在 「 慈悲 」 發起的數週後 , 探討了宗教的角色:它的教條會會把我們分為一致嗎 ? 還是它會把我們團結在一起 , 讓人類團結起來 , 好嗎 ? 她重新審視了能夠帶動世界的信念 , 以重新發現黃金法則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	神 , ted獎 , 全球議題 , 政治 , 宗教 , tedglobal2009年 , 暴力事件
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenarmstrong:讓我們重建黃金法則 。
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來 , 我一直感到沮喪 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我敏銳地意識到同情心的核心 , 在所有重大世界的信仰中 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一種都演化出自己的版本 , 叫做黃金法則 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時 , 它是正面的版本 , 「 把所有其他人當成你想對待自己時 , 永遠對待你 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是負面的版本 「 不要對其他人做你不喜歡他們做的事 。 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你自己的內心 , 發現它是什麼讓你痛苦 , 然後拒絕 , 在任何情況下 , 去強化任何人的痛苦 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	而人們強調慈悲心的重要性 , 不只是因為它聽起來不錯 , 而是因為它有用 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現當他們實施了黃金法則如混淆所說的 「 一整天和每一天 」 , 不只是一個在做你好事的疑問 , 然後回到一個充滿貪婪和自尊的人生 , 而是要做一整天 , 你把自己從你的世界的中心奪去 , 把另一個放在那裡 , 然後超越了你自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它帶你進入了所謂的神、nirvana、rama、tao 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	超越我們所知的自我意識存在的事物 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你從來不知道很多時候 , 這對宗教生活是如此的核心 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有少數幾個很棒的例外 , 通常當宗教人士聚集在一起 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起 , 他們會爭論關於抽絲蒂固的教條 , 或執行關於仇恨的理事會 , 或對同性戀的觀點之類的 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常人們不太想要有同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時會看到 , 當我在和一群宗教人士說話時 , 一種自閉症的表情穿越了他們的臉 , 因為人們常常想反而是對的 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	這當然會破壞運動的物體 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	我為什麼這麼感激ted ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們從我的書籍研究中輕柔地帶我進入21世紀 , 讓我能在比我想像中更廣泛的觀眾演講 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我覺得這事的急迫性
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們不設法在全球實施黃金法則 , 以至於我們對待所有人 , 不論在哪裡 , 不論他們是誰 , 彷彿他們和我們一樣重要 , 我懷疑我們會有一個可行的世界 , 把我們交給下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務 , 我們這個時代的一個偉大的任務是建立一個全球性的社會 , 如同我剛剛說的 , 人們可以一起生活在和平中 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而應該做出重大貢獻的宗教 , 反而被視為問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然不只是宗教人士相信黃金法則
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的來源 , 這種有想像力的同理心 , 把自己置於另一個人的位置 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以我們有選擇 , 似乎對我而言 ,
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們可以繼續帶出或強調我們信仰的教條和寬容的面向 , 或者 , 我們可以回到拉比 。 耶穌的老年人希爾爾爾爾爾爾 , 耶穌的當代人 , 當他站在一條腿上時 , 要求他總結整個猶太教義 , 他說: 「 這對你有害 , 不要對你的鄰居有害 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	這就是所謂的 「 托拉赫 」 和其他所有東西只有評論 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	而教堂的拉比人和早期的父親說任何對仇恨的詮釋都是不合法的 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	而我們需要復甦這種精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	這不僅會發生 , 因為愛的靈魂會把我們喚醒 。
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須讓這件事成真 , 用ted推出的現代通訊來實現 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經對我們伴侶的反應感到極大的驚訝 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有一個團體要用憲章來治癒分裂 , 最近才會出現在新加坡社會 , 議會的某些成員想要在政治上實施 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 將會有一場藝術展覽 , 主導藝術家將帶領人們 , 年輕人 , 並向他們展示 , 同情心也屬於所有藝術的根源 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在整個歐洲 , 穆斯林社群都在舉辦活動和討論 , 討論著在伊斯蘭和所有信仰中的慈悲心的核心 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能停在這裡 , 它不能停止發射 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教誨 , 這是我們過錯的地方 , 全心全意地相信廣告教條 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教教學一定會引發行動 。
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	我打算在這個死日的日子裡工作 。
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	我想繼續跟我們的夥伴一起做兩件事 , 教育並刺激同情心思考 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育因為我們已經退出同情心了 。
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們常常認為這只是對某人感到抱歉而已 。
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但你當然不懂慈悲 , 如果你只是想 ,
you also have to do it .	你也必須去做
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望他們能讓媒體參與其中 , 因為媒體能協助解除我們對其他人的一些刻板印象 , 把我們從對方身上分開 。
the same applies to educators .	同樣的應用在教育工作者身上
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望年輕人能感受到充滿活力、充滿活力 , 並挑戰有同情心的生活方式 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	還看到它要求急性智能 , 而不只是一種臭味的感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想打電話給學者 , 去探索他們自己和其他人的傳統中所帶有的同情心 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	也許最重要的是 , 為了鼓勵不寬容的言論的敏感度 , 這麼一來 , 因為人們有這個憲章 , 不論他們的信仰或缺乏什麼 , 他們覺得被賦予能力去挑戰不寬容的言論 , 不寬容的言論 , 從他們的宗教領袖、他們的政治領袖、他們的政治領袖 , 從業界的船長 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們可以改變世界 , 我們有能力
i would never have thought of putting the charter online .	我從來沒有想過要把憲章放上網路 。
i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我仍然被困在舊世界中 , 一大堆的bof鰭在一個房間裡一起坐著 , 還在說著另一個古古老的陳述 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	ted向我介紹了一種全新的思考方式和呈現想法 。
because that is what is so wonderful about ted .	因為那是ted這麼美好的原因 。
in this room , all this expertise , if we joined it all together , we could change the world .	在這個房間裡 , 所有這些專業知識 , 如果我們把它全部加起來 , 我們就能改變世界 。
and of course the problems sometimes seem insuperable .	當然 , 問題有時似乎很嚴重 。
but i'd just like to quote , finish at the end with a reference to a british author , an oxford author whom i don't quote very often , c . s . lewis .	但最後我想引用一位英國作家 , 牛津作家 , 我不常引用他的話 , c.s.路易斯 。
but he wrote one thing that stuck in my mind ever since i read it when i was a schoolgirl .	但他寫了一件事 , 從我讀到學校的時候 , 一直困在我腦海裡 。
it's in his book " the four loves . "	在他的書《四項愛》中
he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說他分辨出性愛 , 當兩個人凝視、拼字 , 彼此的眼睛 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	接著 , 他把這和友情做比較 , 當兩個人站在一旁 , 就像它一樣 , 肩並肩 , 雙眼固定在一個共同目標上 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不需要愛上彼此 , 而是可以成為朋友 。
and i am convinced .	而我深信
i felt it very strongly during our little deliberations at vevey , that when people of all different persuasions come together , working side by side for a common goal , differences melt away .	我非常強烈地感受到 , 在我們對審查的小小意議中 , 當各式各樣的說服聚集在一起 , 與共同的目標一起合作時 , 差異就會融化 。
and we learn amity .	而我們學會了 「 空間 」 。
and we learn to live together and to get to know one another .	我們學著一起生活 , 認識彼此 。

david macaulay relives the winding and sometimes surreal journey toward the completion of rome antics , his illustrated homage to the historic city .	davidmacacaulay釋放了風向 , 有時還超現實的旅程 , 走向羅馬•安特斯的補充 , 他闡述了向歷史城市致敬 。

enters the courtyard and talks to the custodian , who tells him that there's been a disaster in the palazzo ; nobody's tvs are working and there's a big soccer game coming up , and the crowd is getting a little restless and a little nervous .	進入庭院 , 和那位顧客聊天 , 他告訴他 , 在palazzo有一場災難 ; 沒有人在電視上工作 , 出現了一場大型足球比賽 , 群眾也變得有點不安 , 有點緊張 。
he goes down to the basement and starts to check the wiring , and then gradually works his way up to the top of the building , apartment by apartment , checking every television , checking every connection , hoping to find out what this problem is .	他走到地下室 , 開始檢查電線 , 然後漸漸地 , 他走向大樓頂端的路 , 通過公寓 , 檢查每一台電視 , 檢查每個連線 , 希望能找出這個問題是什麼 。
he works his way up , finally , the grand staircase and then a smaller staircase until he reaches the attic .	他往上走 , 終於到了大樓階梯 , 再往上走 , 直到他抵達閣樓 。
he opens the window of the attic , of course , and there's a tablecloth wrapped around the building's television antenna .	他打開閣樓的窗戶 , 當然 , 還有一張桌布包圍著建築物的電視天線 。
he removes it , the problems are solved , everybody in the palazzo is happy .	他移除它 , 問題就解決了 , 所有在palazzo的人都很開心 。
and of course , he also solves his own problem .	當然 , 他也解決了自己的問題 。
all he has to do now , with a perfect table , is wait for her to arrive .	他現在只能用一張完美的桌子 , 等著她來到 。
that was the first attempt , but it didn't seem substantial enough to convey whatever it was i wanted to convey about rome .	那是第一次嘗試 , 但似乎還不夠實質 , 來傳達任何我想傳達的關於羅馬的事物 。
so i thought , well , i'll just do piazzas , and i'll get inside and underneath and i'll show these things growing and show why they're shaped the way they are and so on .	所以我就想 , 嗯 , 我只要做個皮雅za , 然後我會進去和底下 , 然後我會展示這些東西成長 , 並展現它們為何會塑造出它們的形式等等 。
and then i thought , that's too complicated . no , i'll just take my favorite bits and pieces and i'll put them inside the pantheon but keep the scale , so you can see the top of sant'ivo and the pyramid of cestius and the tempietto of bramante all side by side in this amazing space .	然後我就想 , 那太複雜了 。 不 , 我會把我最喜歡的部分和碎片 , 放到萬神殿裡 , 但要保持尺度 , 這樣你就能看到第一層的sant'ivo和cestius的金字塔 , 以及巴拉曼特的圖片 , 全都在這神奇的空間中 。
now that's one drawing , so i thought maybe it's time for piranesi to meet escher .	現在那是一張圖 , 所以我想也許該是皮拉內西去見escher的時候了 。
you see that i'm beginning to really lose control here and also hope .	你看 , 我已經開始真正失去控制權了 , 同時也希望了 。
there's a very thin blue line of exhaust that sort of runs through this thing that would be kind of the trail that holds it all together .	這裡有一條很細的藍色筋疲力竭 , 有點像是穿過這玩意兒的路徑 , 把它們全部放在一起 。
then i thought , " wait a minute , what am i doing ? "	接著我想: 「 等等 , 我在做什麼 ? 」
a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	一本書不僅是收集和儲存資訊的整理方式 , 還包括一系列的層次 。
i mean , you always peel one layer off another ; we think of them as pages , doing it a certain way .	我的意思是 , 你總是把一個層次拆掉 ; 我們把它們當作頁面 , 用某種方式來做 。

the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	羅馬大部分建築物的牆壁上覆蓋著傷疤 ; 幾個世紀以來 , 改變的傷疤隨著這些結構被適應而非被摧毀 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左手邊畫一個摺疊頁 , 讓你解開它 , 你可以看到它的背後 , 我所謂的傷疤組織 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到 , 在1635年 , 製造小小的窗戶是很重要的 , 因為壞人要來了 , 或其他的 。

but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	但 , 更重要的是 , 我還可以向各位展示 , 在那些偉大的建築物中 , 其中一個角落的樣子 , 有著巨大的石塊 , 或是用磚頭和黏土做成的假石塊 , 通常是這樣 。

and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	他終於得到足夠的力量 , 把梯子爬到屋頂上 , 所有的鴿子 , 一支拉紅色的氣球 , 都在那等著他 , 帶著他離開城市的牆壁 。

in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在羅馬習俗中 , 死者從來沒有埋在牆壁中 。

. that's really going to go a long way .	這真的會走很長一段路 。

and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	在這個時點 , 要傳達那種飛越城市的感覺 , 是必要的 , 且是有可能的 , 要傳遞到城市的感覺 , 而不需要移動 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	超越過西斯提烏斯金字塔--這些看起來很熟悉 , 即使你最近沒去過羅馬渡過大門 。
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這是有點不尋常的事 。

so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	所以 , 我們繞著羅馬競技場 , 穿越了卡斯馬利亞的聖瑪利亞教堂 , 以及海克力士的神殿 , 朝著河流前進 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	我們差點碰撞了帕拉扎索法蘭西歐設計的康尼索 , 由米開朗基羅建造的石頭 , 由羅馬競技場狹窄逃脫而成 。
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們俯衝過campodefiori的
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我給學生看的其中一件事 , 因為它完全否定任何觀點的規則 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為唯一重要觀點的規則是 , 如果它看起來可信 , 你已經成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你試著去了解這裡消失的點在哪裡 ; 一對夫妻在火星上 , 還有其他幾位在克雷門亞 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但在聖塔瑪莉亞戴拉的步調前的皮雅薩 , 在那裡無可避免地舉辦足球比賽 , 我們被足球打了一場 。

and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你真的想看聖塔瑪麗亞•戴拉的步調 , 這些書很靈活 , 非常有互動性 , 只要把它轉過來 , 用另一種方式來看 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	透過巷子 , 我們可以看到影響線被捕捉到 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	接著 , 鳥類在中世紀的高塔上將自己拉在一起 , 一座剩下的中世紀塔樓 , 朝著sant'agnese的教堂前進 , 向下看 , 往下看 , 往下看 , piazanavona , 我們已經談過幾次了 , 飛過了 ; 這是柏尼雕像 , 橫越了四條河 , 接著是奇妙的布洛米尼聖母堂 , 在萬神殿的直徑26英尺上停下來 , 抓住我們的呼吸 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	然後我們就可以在裡面隨處亂竄 , 因為我們飛了 , 我們不用擔心重力在這個特定的時刻 , 所以這張圖可以用任何方式在頁面上定位 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	當我們通過gesu時 , 我們會比較有成就感 ; 這並不讓人驚訝 , 用這種方式模仿建築 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	經過美好的牆壁 , 充滿了我剛剛談到的六角形 ; 美麗的雕刻被放到《暴風山》的牆上 , 諸如此類 。

straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接穿過庭院 , 進入閣樓的一扇小窗 , 有人在畫板上工作 。

as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	在我們看畫板時 , 我們看到他正在做的是 , 事實上 , 一幅鴿子剛剛拍攝的旅程地圖 , 紅線延伸到所有的視野 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要這些資訊 , 這樣我們就完成了這個理解的循環 , 你只需要讀這些段落 。
thank you very much .	非常感謝大家 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院的研究者skylarstibbits在自行組裝上運作的這個想法 , 而不是建造東西 , 我們可以創造出能自己建造的材料 , 很多dna的方式 , 將自己組裝在一起 。 這是在早期的一個大概念 ; 蒂布斯會給我們看三個精細的項目 , 暗示著自我組裝未來的樣子 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	skylartibbits:我們能否做出製造自己的東西 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天我想向各位展示我們製造東西的方式的未來 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信很快我們的建築和機器就會自行組合、複製和修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以我要給你們看我所相信的 , 是目前的製造業狀態 , 然後將它和一些自然系統做比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	所以 , 在目前的製造業狀態中 , 我們有摩天大樓兩年半的時間 。 五十萬到一百萬個部分 , 相當複雜、嶄新的、令人興奮的科技 , 在鋼鐵、混凝土、玻璃中 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人振奮的機器可以帶我們進入太空五年--[合成時間] , 二百五十萬個部分 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但在另一邊 , 如果你看一下自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種類型的蛋白質 , 可以在一萬納秒內摺疊 , 或dna有三十億個鹼基對 , 我們可以在大約一小時內複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 我們的自然系統中有這麼多複雜性 , 但它們非常有效率 , 遠比任何我們能建造的東西更有效率 , 遠比任何我們能建造的東西還要複雜許多 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	它們在能源方面更有效率 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎沒有犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	而且他們可以修復自己長壽
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以 , 天然系統有著超級有趣的東西 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們可以將它轉化為我們的建設環境 , 那麼我們建造東西的方式就有一些令人興奮的潛力 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵在於自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以 , 如果我們想要在我們的物理環境中利用自我組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	第一 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想要建造的東西複雜性 , 如此我們的建築物和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要將它們解碼成簡單的序列 , 基本上就是我們的建築物如何運作的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編寫的零件 , 可以採用這些序列來折疊 , 或重新配置 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能量來啟動 , 讓我們的零件能夠從程式中向上折疊 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要某種類型的錯誤修正冗餘來保證我們已經成功地建構出我們想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以 , 我要給你們看一些項目 , 是我和麻省理工學院的同事正在努力實現這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	前兩個是宏觀機器人和decibott 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	所以這些專案計畫是大規模的可重組機器人8英尺 , 12英尺 。 很長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	他們被機械裝置嵌入 , 感應器
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你解碼了你想要摺的是什麼 , 變成一連串的角度 , 如此負重120 , 負120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , 負120 , 負120--類似的角度 , 或轉動 , 然後你將那序列送到弦中 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位會把訊息傳給負120 , 它會旋轉到那兒 , 檢查它是否會到那兒 , 然後傳給它的鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些是傑出的科學家、工程師、設計師在這個計畫上的工作 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我覺得這真的帶到光線上:這真的是可擴展的嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 成千上萬美元 , 很多男人小時製造這個八英呎的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們真的能把這個規模擴大嗎 ? 我們真的能把機器人學嵌入每一個部分嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題 , 並且檢視被動的天性 , 或被動地嘗試進行重新配置程式 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它更進一步 , 它嘗試進行實際的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	它基本上嵌入了計算機最基本的基礎建材 , 數位邏輯閘 , 直接進入你的零件 。
so this is a nand gate .	所以這是nandgates
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一個四面體 , 就是大門要做你的計算 , 你有兩個輸入的四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中一個是使用者的輸入 , 如同你正在建造你的磚塊一樣 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另一種是從前一個磚塊放過來的
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它給你3d空間中的輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	所以 , 這意味著 , 使用者可以開始在他們想要磚頭做的事中插手 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算它之前的做法 , 以及你說你想要它做的事 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間中移動 , 上下或下 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	所以在左手邊 , [1 , 1]輸入等於0的輸出 , 會下降 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , [0、0]輸入是1的輸出值 , 會上升 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	所以 , 這意味著 , 我們的結構現在包含了我們想要建造的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們擁有所有被建構出來的資訊 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	所以這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個案例中 , 我稱它為自我複製 , 因為你的結構包含了確切的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以替換一個部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有當地的資訊都嵌在告訴大家如何修復它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以 , 你可以有東西爬上去 , 讀它 , 可以在一比一的情況下輸出 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它直接嵌入 ; 沒有外部的指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	我將展示的最後一個專案 , 叫做 「 偏見鏈 」 , 它可能是我們目前最興奮的例子 , 就是被動自組裝系統 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以它需要重組和程式 , 讓它成為一個完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	所以基本上你有一連串的元素 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素是完全相同的 , 它們是有偏見的 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以每條鎖鏈 , 或每個元素 , 都想要向右或向左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組裝鏈時 , 你基本上就是在編寫程式 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你在告訴每一個單位是否應該轉向左或左 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你搖晃鏈時 , 它會折疊成任何你編寫過的結構 , 在這個案例中 , 一個螺旋形 , 或在這個案例中 , 兩個立方體在旁邊 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	所以你基本上可以編寫任何立體的形狀或一維的 , 二維的形狀完全被動地進入這個連鎖鏈 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴了我們什麼關於未來 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為 , 它告訴我們 , 自我組裝、複製、修復、修復我們的實體結構、我們的建築、機器 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	這些部分有新的程式能力 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從那之中你就有了計算的新可能性 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們會有空間運算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物、橋樑、機器 , 我們所有的磚其實可以計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	那是驚人的平行和分散式的計算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以對此感到興奮的潛力 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為 , 我在這裡所展示的這些計畫 , 只是朝這個未來邁進的一小步 , 如果我們為一個新的自我組裝的世界實施這些新技術 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們去過月球 , 繪製了大陸 , 我們甚至去過海底兩次最深的點 。 下一代還剩下什麼去探索 ? 生物學家和探險家納森.沃夫斯提出這個答案:幾乎每樣東西 。 然後我們就可以開始 , 他說 , 帶著不可見的小世界 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學、
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	內森wolfe:剩下什麼要去探索 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我拜訪了威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在那裡榮耀一個20世紀偉大的探險家 , roychapmanandrews 。
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在他在美國自然歷史博物館的期間 , 安德魯斯帶領一系列的探險活動到未知的地區 , 比如在戈壁沙漠這裡 。
he was quite a figure .	他是個很大的人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	他後來 , 據說是印第安那瓊斯角色的基礎
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市時 , 我給一群中學學生做公開的講座 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我在這裡要告訴各位 , 如果有任何事比在ted這裡演講更令人生畏的話 , 它會試著把一千二十二歲的孩子的注意力留在一個四十五分鐘的講座上 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	在講課結束時 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但從那之後 , 有一個問題真的困住了我 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一個年輕女孩站起來 , 她問了這個問題: 「 我們應該去哪裡探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我認為 , 我們當中有許多人認為地球上偉大的探索時代已經結束了 , 對於下一代 , 他們得要去外太空或最深的海洋 , 才能找到重要的東西來探索 。
but is that really the case ?	但這真的是這樣嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	在地球上 , 是否真的沒有什麼重要的探索 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這有點讓我回想起生物史上我最喜愛的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是未被看見的世界的探險家 , martinusbeijerinck 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	所以beijerinck開始發現菸草鑲嵌病的原因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他的做法是從菸草植物中取出受感染的果汁 , 透過越來越小的過濾器來過濾 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他到了那個時候 , 他覺得一定有什麼比當時所知的細菌更小的生命形式還小 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他為他的神秘代理人想出了一個名字 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱它為 「 毒藥 」 的拉丁文 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在揭開病毒時 , beijerinck真的為我們打開了這個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒構成了我們地球上大多數的基因信息 , 比所有其他形式的生命信息還要多 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	顯然這個世界已經有極大的實用應用 , 像是天花的消滅、對子宮頸癌的疫苗出現 , 我們現在知道主要是由人類乳突病毒造成的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	而beijerinck的發現 , 這不是500年前發生的事 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	大約一百多年前 , beijerinck發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上 , 我們有汽車 , 但我們卻不知道生命形式 , 構成了我們星球上大部分的基因信息 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有了這些驚人的工具 , 可以讓我們探索未見的世界 , 像是深度定序 , 讓我們能做的不只是跳過表面 , 還能從特定物種的個別基因組來檢視 , 而是檢視整個元素 , 這些微生物的社群 , 在我們身邊 , 記錄所有這些物種的遺傳信息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以把這些技巧運用到從土壤到皮膚 , 和中間的一切 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織裡 , 我們現在正定期做這件事 , 來辨識出造成疫情爆發的原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓各位了解這如何運作 , 想像一下 , 我們從你們每一個人身上取下了一塊鼻子 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	我們通常會去尋找呼吸道病毒 , 如流感 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	我們首先會看到極大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究這些基因信息 , 我們會看到許多人類遺傳信息的嫌疑犯 , 當然 , 還有細菌和病毒信息 , 大部分是來自你鼻子內完全無害的事物 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也會看到一些非常驚人的現象 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始研究這些資訊時 , 我們會發現 , 你鼻子中大約有20%的基因信息並不符合任何我們以前見過的任何東西--沒有植物、動物、真菌或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上 , 我們完全不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於我們這些研究這種數據的小團體 , 我們當中有些人已經開始稱之為 「 資訊生物暗物質 」 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道它不是我們以前見過的任何東西 ; 它相當於我們自己的基因信息中未知的大陸 。
and there's a lot of it .	而且還有很多
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你鼻子裡有20%的基因信息是很多的生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸子 , 高達40%或50%的信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	甚至在相對比較保存的血液中 , 大約有1%到2%的資訊是暗物質無法被分類 , 不能用我們以前見過的任何東西來打字或配對 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始我們以為也許這是人造物 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度定序的工具相對很新 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但隨著它們變得越來越準確 , 我們已經判斷出這些資訊是生命的一種形式 , 至少其中有一些是生命的一種形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質的存在 , 卻只存在於嬰兒期 , 有非常令人興奮的可能性存在:埋藏在這個生命中 , 在這個遺傳信息中 , 代表著生命的特徵 , 即尚未被確認的生命 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們在探究一連串a、t、c和g時 , 我們可能會發現一種全新的生命類型 , 比如beijerinck , 會從根本上改變我們看待生物的本質的方式 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	這或許可以讓我們找出癌症的成因 , 來衝突我們 , 或是找出我們不熟悉的疫情來源 , 或是在分子生物學中創造出新的工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興地宣布 , 同時還有史丹佛大學、加州理工學院和加州大學舊金山分校的同事們 , 我們目前正開展一項計畫 , 探索生物暗物質 , 為新形式的生命存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	大約一百多年前 , 人們對病毒一無所知 , 生命的形式 , 構成了我們星球上大部分的基因信息 。
