a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能會驚嘆 , 我們可能完全沒有意識到新的人生階級 , 真的在我們的鼻子下 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	這是真的 , 我們可能已經記錄了地球上所有的大陸 , 我們可能已經發現了所有的哺乳類動物 , 但那並不表示地球上沒有任何東西可以探索 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的仁慈提供了重要的一課給下一代的探險家 , 像那位來自威斯康辛州貝洛特的年輕女孩 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我認為 , 如果我們把這個教訓說出來 , 應該是這樣的:不要假設我們目前認為有完整的故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	去過任何你選擇探索的領域裡的暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們身邊都有未知 , 他們只會等著被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳奇的科學家大衛德普斯將理論物理學放在背燒錄器上 , 討論一個更迫切的問題:我們這個物種的生存 。 解決全球暖化的第一步 , 他說 , 就是承認我們有問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、環境、全球議題、物理、科學、科技、宇宙、宇宙 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	在我們在宇宙中的位置上 , 大衛•迪赫在我們的位置 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要走出肢體 , 說出令人驚訝的話 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	我會試著這樣做 , 但我想從大家都知道的兩件事說起 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	第一項 , 事實上 , 是歷史上大多數歷史以來都已知的 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球 , 或太陽系 , 或我們的環境 , 或其他東西 , 都很適合維持我們的演化或創造 , 就像過去的思想和我們現在的存在一樣 , 最重要的是我們未來的生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現今 , 這個想法有個很戲劇性的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	我們的想法是 , 在太空船之外 , 宇宙是充滿敵意的 , 內部是我們所擁有的一切 , 我們所仰賴的一切 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一次機會:如果我們搞砸了我們的太空船 , 我們就沒有別的了 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	第二件事 , 大家都已經知道 , 和人類歷史上大多數人所相信的相反 , 事實上 , 人類不是存在的中心 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	就像史蒂芬霍金說的 , 我們只是一個典型的星球表面的化學污垢 , 它繞著一個典型的恆星在軌道上 , 它位於一個典型的銀河系的外圍 , 諸如此類的 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	大家都知道的這兩件事當中 , 第一件事是說我們處在一個很不典型的地方 , 獨一無二的適合等等 , 第二件事是說我們處在一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	特別是如果你把這兩個當作是深層的真理來活下去 , 並告知你的人生決策 , 那麼它們似乎會互相衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這不會阻止他們完全錯誤 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們是的 。 讓我從第二個開始講起:典型 。 這是典型的地方嗎 ? 嗯 , 讓我們看看四周 , 看看隨機方向 , 我們看到一面牆 , 一面化學污垢 , 而這一點也不典型宇宙 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你要做的只是往同一個方向走幾百英里 , 然後往回看 , 你不會看到任何牆壁或化學污垢 , 只看到一個藍色的星球 。 如果你走得更遠 , 你會看到太陽、太陽系 , 以及恆星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但那仍然不是宇宙的典型 , 因為恆星的星系 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	而宇宙中的大部分地方 , 宇宙中一個典型的地方 , 都沒有接近任何星系 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	讓我們更進一步 , 直到我們在銀河系之外 , 回頭看 , 沒錯 , 這裡有巨大的星系 , 有著螺旋形的手臂躺在我們面前 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	此時我們已經有10萬光年了 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但我們仍然沒有接近宇宙中典型的地方 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到達一個典型的地方 , 要到達星系間空間的一千倍之多 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那看起來像什麼 ? 典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中一個典型的地方是什麼樣子的 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	嗯 , 在巨大的花費下 , ted已經安排了高解析度的浸泡在虛擬實境中 , 呈現出來自星系間空間的景象 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	所以 , 我們能把燈關掉 , 拜託 , 我們能看到嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不太完美 , 你可以看到 , 在星系間空間中是完全漆黑的 , 漆黑的 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	它是如此的黑暗 , 如果你要看著你最近的恆星 , 那顆恆星會爆炸成一顆超新星 , 而你要直接盯著它看 , 當它的光線抵達你時 , 你仍然無法看見即使是滑翔機 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	這就是宇宙有多大、有多黑暗
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管超新星是如此的明亮 , 如此聰明 , 以致於它會在幾光年之久地奪走你死去 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	然而 , 從星系間的空間來看 , 它是如此的遙遠 , 你甚至看不到它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	那裡的溫度也很低 , 低於絕對零度三度 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	而且它非常空洞 。 真空的密度比地球上最好的技術所能創造出的真空密度低一百萬倍 。 所以 , 一個典型的地方是這樣 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這就是這個地方是多麼的典型 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	所以 , 請把燈光回來嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	現在 , 我們怎麼知道這麼遙遠的環境 , 如此不同 , 如此不同 , 如此外星人 , 從我們所習慣的任何事物中 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	嗯 , 地球--我們的環境 , 以我們的形式 , 正在創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	嗯 , 那是什麼意思呢 ? 再看看比我們剛剛從這裡看的更遠的--我是說 , 用望遠鏡--然後你會看到像星星一樣的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	他們被稱為 「 quasars 」 。 quasars原本的意思是 「 時尚之物 」 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	這意味著看起來有點像恆星的東西 。 但它們不是恆星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	而我們知道它們是什麼 。 幾十億年前 , 幾十億光年之外 , 銀河系的中心物質崩塌 , 朝向一個超大質量的黑洞前進 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	然後強烈的磁場引導了那重力崩塌的一些能量 。 有些物質 , 以極大的噴射流束形式呈現 , 帶著我覺得那是一兆個太陽 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	現在 , 人類大腦的物理學幾乎不像噴射流的物理學 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法即時存活下來 。 語言在試圖描述噴射流當中會是怎樣的情況時 , 會是如何 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	這會有點像經歷超新星的爆炸 , 但在點距離及數百萬年以來 ,
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 這種噴射流發生在數十億年後 , 在宇宙的另一端 , 有些化學污垢可以準確地描述 , 以及模型 , 然後預測 , 並解釋 , 最重要的是你的參考資料 , 在現實中發生了什麼 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個物理系統 , 大腦 , 包含一個精確的工程模型 , 另一個是quasar 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅僅是它的一種超級形象 , 雖然它也包含它 , 但一個解釋性的模型 , 體現出相同的數學關係和相同的因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這就是知識 。 如果這還不夠驚人 , 一個結構的信念也和時間的增長有關 。 那就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有這種特殊的特性 ,
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	那些實體的物體 , 不像彼此 , 儘管可能是相同的 , 永遠無法體現相同的數學和因果結構 , 並隨著時間不斷地進行 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以 , 我們是一個不一樣的化學污垢 。 這個化學污垢有普遍性 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構包含著不斷增加的精確度 , 萬物的結構 。 這個地方 , 而非宇宙中其他地方 , 是一個樞紐 , 包含在自身結構和因果的本質 , 包括整個實體現實的結構和因果關係 。 所以 , 遠離不變量 , 物理定律允許這個現象的事實 , 或甚至是強制這樣發生的事實 , 是物理世界中最重要的事情之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	現在太陽系和我們的環境是如何形成這種與宇宙其他地方的特殊關係呢 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	關於史蒂芬霍金的評論 , 有一點是正確的 , 我的意思是 , 這是真的 , 但它是錯誤的強調 。 其中一點是 , 任何特殊的物理學都沒有 。 沒有特殊的解讀 , 沒有奇蹟 。 它只用了我們現有的三樣東西 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是物質 , 因為知識的增長是資訊處理的一種形式 。 資訊處理是計算 , 計算需要一台電腦 , 根本不知道製造一台電腦是無所謂的 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是要讓媒體能有效地傳播到我們記錄我們發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三點 , 比較沒有實際性 , 但也同樣重要 , 對於開放式的知識、解釋的開放式的創造 , 是有證據的 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	現在 , 我們的環境被證據所淹沒了 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	我們剛好在三百年前就開始進行測驗 , 比如說 , 牛頓的引力定律 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但是我們以前所做的證據在地球的每一平方公尺下跌了數十億年 , 之後還會持續下跌數十億年 。 其他科學也是如此 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	就我們所知 , 發掘所有科學最基本的真理的證據 , 僅僅是為了在地球上實現 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的地點充滿了證據 , 同時也充滿了物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星系間空間中 , 這三項開放式創造知識的前提是最低的供給 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	就像我說的 , 它是空的 ; 它是冷的 ; 外面是暗的 。 還是它 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	其實 , 那只是另一個狹隘的誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為想像一個在星系間空間的立方體 , 和我們家一樣大 , 太陽系 。 現在那個立方體是非常空的 , 但這仍然意味著它包含了超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸就足以製造一個自給自足的太空站 , 裡面有一群科學家 , 他們致力於創造開放式的知識流 , 等等 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 超越現在的科技 , 甚至把來自星系間空間的氫氣聚集在一起 , 形成成其他元素等等 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但 , 重點是 , 在一個無法理解的宇宙中 , 如果某樣東西不被物理定律所禁止 , 那麼 , 什麼可能可以避免我們去做 , 除了知道怎麼做 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 它是知識的問題 , 而不是資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們能自動進行能源供應 , 因為轉化為核融合反應爐和證據 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	同樣的 , 人類的感官也是暗的 。 但你只需要用望遠鏡 , 即使是現代設計中的一個 , 向外看 , 你會看到我們從這裡看到同樣的星系 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	用更強大的望遠鏡 , 你將能夠看見恆星 , 以及行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在那些星系中 , 你將能夠進行天體物理學 , 並學習物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	當地你可以建造粒子加速器 , 學習基本粒子物理學 , 化學等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	可能最困難的科學就是生物學領域之旅 , 因為要花上數億年才能到達最近的生命之星 , 回歸到最遠的星球 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但我得告訴各位 , 抱歉 , 理查 , 但我從來沒有做過很多生物學領域旅行 , 我想我們每幾億年就能做到一次 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以事實上 , 星際空間確實包含了所有開放式知識的前提 。 任何這樣的立方體 , 在宇宙中的任何一個立方體 , 都可以成為我們所屬的中心 , 只要我們對如何做到的知識 , 即是現在就存在 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以 , 我們不是在一個獨一無二的討厭的地方 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星系間空間能夠開放解釋 , 那麼幾乎所有其他的環境都一樣 。 地球也是一樣 。 受污染的地球也是一樣 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	而極限的因素 , 在這裡和這裡 , 不是資源 , 因為資源很充沛 , 但知識 , 很匱乏 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	現在這個以宇宙為基礎的觀點 , 或許我認為應該要讓我們感到非常特殊 。 但這也應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為這意味著 , 若沒有需要具體的知識 , 能夠生存下去的宇宙挑戰 , 我們就不會生存下去 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只需要一顆超新星在幾光年之外 , 我們都會死掉 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁•雷斯最近寫了一本書 , 內容是關於我們脆弱到各式各樣的東西 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗出錯了 , 最重要的是用大規模殺傷性武器來恐怖主義 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為文明只有50%的機會能存活這個世紀 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他晚點會在會議上會談
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	現在我不認為機率是正確的類別來討論這個議題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但是我確實認同他這樣做 。 我們可以生存 , 而且我們無法生存 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但這不取決於機會 , 而是我們是否能及時創造出相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險並不是史無前例的 。 物種隨時都在滅絕 。
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明終止了 。 絕大多數的物種和所有已經存在的文明 , 現在都是歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想成為這個例外 , 那麼邏輯上 , 我們唯一的希望就是運用一個特徵來區分我們這個物種 , 而我們的文明 , 來自其他所有人的名字 , 我們與物理定律的特殊關係 , 我們創造新的解釋的能力 , 新的知識成為存在的中心 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	現在讓我把這個應用到目前的爭議上 , 不是因為我想提倡任何特定的解決方案 , 而只是為了說明我的意思 。
and the controversy is global warming .	而爭議是全球暖化
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是物理學家 , 但我不是物理學家 。 不論是全球暖化 , 我只是個層次 。 對於層次來說 , 理性的事情是要認真看待偏激的科學理論 。 根據這個理論 , 它已經太遲了 , 無法避免一場災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為如果我們目前最好的選擇是預防二氧化碳排放 , 用比如京都議定書、經濟活動的限制 , 以及數千億美元之類的巨大成本 , 那麼 , 任何合理的措施已經是一場災難 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	倡導的行動 , 甚至還沒有追求解決問題 , 只不過是稍微延後一點點 。 所以 , 它已經太遲了 , 無法避免它 , 它可能已經太遲了 , 以至任何人意識到危險之前 , 都無法避免它 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	可能在1970年代已經太晚了 , 當時最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 工業排放即將在數十億人死亡的新冰河時期 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	這堂課對我來說似乎很清楚 , 我不知道為什麼它沒有公開辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	就是我們不能一直都知道 。 當我們知道一場即將發生的災難 , 以及如何以低於災難本身的成本來解決 , 那麼就不會有太多的爭論 , 真的 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防措施 , 也沒有預防原則 , 可以避免我們尚未預見的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要一個解決問題的立場 , 而不只是解決問題 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	沒錯 , 一盎司的預防等於一磅的治療 , 但只有我們知道該預防什麼才行 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你的鼻子被打了一拳 , 那麼醫學的科學並不能教你如何避開拳擊 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學不再尋求解藥 , 只專注於預防 , 那它也很少達成 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	目前這個世界正隨著計劃著降低氣體排放的計劃 , 使得氣體的排放變得越來越大 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該要與計劃進行降低溫度的緩衝 。 計劃要活在更高的溫度上 , 不用所有成本 , 而是有效率又便宜 。 有些計劃存在 , 像是太空中的一群鏡子 , 把太陽光反射開來 , 鼓勵水生機體多吃二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	目前 , 這些是邊緣研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	他們不是人類努力面對這個問題的核心 , 也不是一般的問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	有了我們還沒意識到的問題 , 把權利的能力 , 不是避免的好運 , 絕對是我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 而是求生存的希望 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	所以拿兩塊石板 , 然後在上面刻畫 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	在其中之一 , 雕刻: 「 問題是可笑的 。 」
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	而在另一張畫裡: 「 問題是必然的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	一個掙扎的國家如何能脫離貧窮 , 如果它被困在一個不良規則的體制中 ? 經濟學家保羅羅•羅默揭示了一個大膽的想法: 「 特許城市 」 , 市政管理區 , 由國家聯盟統治 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治、
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	paulromer的激進想法:charter城市 。
take a look at this picture .	請看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	它為我們帶來了一個非常迷人的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在首都機場的路燈下做功課 , 因為他們家裡沒有電 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我還沒見過這些特別的學生 , 但我見過像他們一樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	舉例來說 , 綠色襯衫裡的那位
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	我們也給他一個名字:尼爾森 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我會賭nelson有一支手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	這就是謎題 。
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼尼爾森能取得尖端科技 , 像是手機 , 但無法取得一百歲的技術 , 讓家裡產生電燈 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	現在 , 用一個詞來說 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不良的規則可以預防這種雙贏的解決方案 , 當人們可以把新科技帶進來 , 讓像尼爾森這樣的人取得 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司在一個規則下運作 , 這條規則是說 , 它必須以很低、很低的價格銷售電力 , 事實上 , 價格低到讓它每一單位銷售 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以 , 它既不是資源 , 也不是激勵機制 , 要把許多其他用戶連結起來 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這個規則 。
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他看到 , 有可能有不同的規則 , 企業賺取小利潤的規則 , 所以他們有誘因要簽署更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	這就是電話公司nelson購買他電話的那種規則 , 由下方的電腦運作 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統知道這些規則是怎麼運作的 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變收購電力的規則 , 但卻跑進一場抗議活動中 , 來自企業和消費者想要保存現有的補助率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以 , 他陷入了規則 , 避免他讓雙贏解決方案協助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	而nelson則被困在街燈下研究 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是試著找出我們如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	我們能為改變規則發展出一些規則嗎 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想要主張 , 有一個普遍的抽象的見解 , 我們能做出實用的見解 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給人們更多的選擇 , 以及更多的領導者選擇 , 在許多國家 , 他們也是人 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 呈現這兩者之間的對立是有用的 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能想給領導者的那種選擇 , 像給予總統在電力上提高價格的選擇 , 奪走人們在經濟中想要的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望選擇能夠繼續消耗補助的電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以 , 如果你只給一面或另一面 , 你就會有張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能找到更多選擇的方法 , 那就給了我們一套改變規則的規則 , 讓我們脫離陷阱 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	現在 , 尼爾森也能取得網路 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想看規則所帶來的傷害影響 , 規則能讓人們保持在黑暗中 , 看看太空總署在晚上拍攝的照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別檢查亞洲 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大這裡 , 你可以看到北韓 , 在這裡 , 和它的鄰居相比 , 這就像是個黑洞 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	你不會驚訝的發現 , 北韓的規則會讓人們待在黑暗中 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但 , 很重要的是 , 北韓和南韓開始了一系列的規則 , 不論是法律或法規 , 都要考慮到更深層的理解、規範、文化、價值觀 , 和信念 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分開時 , 他們做了選擇 , 導致了非常多元化的道路 , 為他們一組的規則 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以我們可以改變身為人類的我們 , 可以改變我們用來和彼此互動的規則 , 做得更好 , 或更糟 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個地區 , 加勒比海
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地 , 這裡的線上 。
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也很黑暗 , 相較於這裡的鄰居 , 多明尼加共和國 , 居民數量差不多 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	這兩個國家相較於波多黎各有一半的居民是海地還是多明尼加共和國
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們的是 , 規則可能會很糟 , 因為政府很弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不只是規則不好 , 因為政府太強勢和壓迫 , 就像在北韓一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以 , 如果我們想要創造有好規則的環境 , 我們就不能只撕下 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也必須找到方法來建立
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國大幅展現出與規則合作的潛力和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回到這張圖表的一開始 , 中國是世界上的高科技領導者 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國人有先驅的科技 , 如鋼、印刷、槍枝 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國人從來沒有採用過 , 至少在那個時期 , 有效的規則 , 來鼓勵那些想法的傳播──一種利潤動機 , 可以鼓勵傳播 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	很快地 , 他們採用的規則會減緩創新 , 把中國從世界其他地方切斷 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 隨著世界其他國家的創新 , 在發展新科技的同時 , 也發展出更新的規則 , 中國人從這些進步中被切斷 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	那裡的收入停滯不前 , 因為它在世界其他地方放大 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表是比較近期的資料 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	它描繪了中國平均收入佔美國平均收入的百分比 。
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50、60年代 , 你可以看到它的範圍大約是3% 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但在七十年代後期 , 有些事情改變了 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	在中國起飛 。 中國開始趕上美國 。
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你在晚上回到地圖上 , 你可以得到一個線索 , 提示這個過程會導致中國的規則有戲劇性的改變 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最亮的地點 , 各位可以看到在線的邊緣 , 是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港是中國的一小部分 , 在20世紀大部分的時間 , 經營在非常不同的規則之下 , 比起當時從事市場經濟工作的其他法則 , 並且由英國管理 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是一個讓數百萬人可以去的地方 , 從大陸開始 , 到像縫紉襯衫一樣的工作 , 做玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 若要取得收入增加的過程 , 技能會造成非常快速的成長 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港也是典範 , 讓像鄧小平這樣的領導人可以複製的模式 , 當他們決定把所有的大陸都移向市場模式 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但鄧小平直覺地了解到提供人民選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其強迫中國的每個人立即轉移到市場模式 , 他們採用的只是創造一些特殊的區塊 , 以某種意義來說 , 可以做到的 , 是英國所做的:讓有機會與市場規則合作 , 讓那些想要選出來的人參與 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們在香港周圍創造了四個特殊的經濟區:中國可以來這裡工作的區塊 , 都市長得很快 ; 還有外國公司可以進來做東西的區塊 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	在香港旁邊的一個區塊有個城市叫做深圳
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那個城市裡 , 有一家台灣公司 , 製作了在座許多人的iphone , 他們用中國人的勞工搬到深圳 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以 , 在四個特區之後 , 有14個沿海風箏 , 以相同的意義打開 , 最後在這些人們可以選擇的地方 , 展現出成功 , 因為他們提供的優勢 , 他們集結在一起 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	展現了成功 , 導致了整個經濟模式的共識 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	現在中國的例子告訴我們好幾點
one is: preserve choices for people .	其一是:保存人們的選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:在正確的規模上運作 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你嘗試改變一個村莊的規則 , 你可以這麼做 , 但一個村莊會太小 , 無法得到你能得到的好處 , 如果你有數百萬人在良好的規則下工作 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你嘗試改變國家的規則 , 你就不能給某些人一個機會來持久 , 看看事情的結果如何 , 讓其他人往前放大 , 嘗試新的規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市給你創造新的地方的機會 , 有了人們可以選擇的新規則 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	而它們大到足以獲得我們所能擁有的所有利益當我們數百萬人在良好的規則下合作時
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以 , 提議是我們構想一個叫做 「 特許城市 」 的東西 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一個特定的章節開始 , 把所有需要的規則都納入 , 來吸引我們建造城市的人 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們會需要吸引投資者 , 他們會建立基礎建設──電力系統、道路、港口、機場、建築物 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你會需要吸引公司 , 他們會先聘請搬到那裡的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	你會需要吸引家人 , 那些會來到那裡的居民 , 永久住在那裡 , 養育他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子接受教育 , 得到他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	有了那個憲章 , 人們就會搬到那裡 。
the city can be built .	城市可以被建立起來
and we can scale this model .	而我們可以擴大這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一而再 , 再而三地
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	要讓它成功 , 我們需要好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	那些被捕捉在憲章裡 ,
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人們的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	這真的是建立在模型中 , 如果我們允許在未居住的土地上建造城市的可能性 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從未居住的領土開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以在新的章節下生活 , 但沒有人會被迫住 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後我們需要的是領導者的選擇 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	要達成我們想要的領導人的那種選擇 , 我們得要讓國家之間有合作的潛力:國家合作的案例 , 實際上 , 中國和英國合作的方式 , 先建立一點市場模式 , 然後擴展到整個中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國 , 不經意地 , 透過香港的行動 , 能減少世界貧窮 , 比上個世紀所有援助計畫所做的還多 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以 , 如果我們允許這種合作夥伴再次複製這個現象 , 我們就能得到這樣的好處 , 遍及全世界 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會涉及到責任的授權 , 一個國家的控制權 , 到另一個國家的授權 , 去接管某些行政責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	現在 , 當我這樣說的時候 , 你們有些人開始想: 「 嗯 , 這只是帶回殖民主義嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	並非如此 。 但重要的是要意識到 , 當我們開始思考這些事情時 , 會出現的那種情緒 , 可以讓我們從中獲益 , 可以讓我們拉回來 , 能夠降低我們的能力 , 以及我們對探索新想法的興趣 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這不像殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義的壞處在於 , 在我們的一些援助計畫中 , 殘酷的壞處在於 , 它涉及到強制力和執行力的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式都是關於選擇 , 不是為了領導者 , 也是為了那些會住在這些新地方的人們 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	而 , 選擇就是解除威脅和承認的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談這個如何能實踐 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	我們來看看一個特定的領導人 , raulcastro , 他是古巴的領導者 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	肯定想過 , 他有機會為古巴做些什麼 , 像是鄧小平為中國做了什麼 , 但他在古巴沒有香港 , 在古巴的島上 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 他在南部有一點點光 , 那裡有很特別的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	在關塔那摩灣周圍有一個區塊 , 一個條約給美國一塊土地負責一塊土地 , 大約是曼哈頓的兩倍大 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯楚去了加拿大總理說: 「 聽著 , 雅安基斯特有可怕的pr問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想要出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為何你不 , 加拿大 , 接管 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建造經營一個特別的行政區
allow a new city to be built up there .	允許一個新的城市在上面建設 。
allow many people to come in .	讓許多人進來 。
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓附近有個香港
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些公民也會搬進那個城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會緊緊抓住 。 但這將會是將現代經濟和現代世界連結到我的國家的大門 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	現在 , 這模型還能在哪裡被試驗呢 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	嗯 , 非洲 。 我和非洲的領袖談過 ,
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	他們之中有許多人完全得到一個人們可以選擇的特區的概念 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	以改變規則的規則
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	它是一種創造新規則的方式 , 讓人們不用強迫 , 不用強迫 , 就會反對 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解 , 在某些情況下 , 他們可以對長期投資者做出更有信賴的承諾 , 那些會來蓋港口的投資者 , 建造道路 , 在新城市中 , 他們可以做出更有信賴的承諾 , 如果他們和一個夥伴國家一起做的話 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	也許甚至在一些安排中 , 有點像escrow的帳戶 , 在那裡 , 你把土地放在escrow的帳戶中 , 而伴侶的國家也承擔責任 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲還有很多的土地 , 在那裡 , 新的城市可以建造 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是我在沿著海岸飛行時拍的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	像這片土地有著巨大的延伸 , 數億人可以住的地方 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們歸納一下 , 並思考一下 , 不僅僅是一、二個特區 , 而是數十個城市 , 能協助創造出數億個城市的地方 , 甚至數十億人 , 在未來的世紀 , 會移居到城市中 , 是否有足夠的土地給他們 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	嗯 , 在整個世界 , 如果我們晚上看燈光 , 有一件事誤導了 , 就是 , 視覺上 , 看起來 , 大部分的世界已經被建立起來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	所以 , 讓我向各位展示為什麼那是錯的 。
take this representation of all of the land .	把這代表所有土地的
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它變成一個方塊 , 代表地球上所有的可耕地 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表已經被三十億人口居住的城市所佔據的土地 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把點移到長方形的底部 , 你可以看到現有的三十億城市居民佔了地球上可耕地的百分之三 。
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以 , 如果我們想要為十億人建造城市 , 他們會是這樣的點 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們會從百分之三的可耕地 , 到百分之四 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們會大大降低地球上的人類足跡 , 做法是建造更多人們可以搬到的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市是由良好的規則所管理 , 它們可以是城市 , 人們安全不受犯罪、安全不受疾病和不良衛生 , 在那裡 , 人們有機會得到一份工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	可以得到像電力這樣的基本功用
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以接受教育 。
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 我們要怎麼開始建造第一座特區城市 , 把這個規模擴大 , 才能建造更多的城市 ?
it would help to have a manual .	擁有一本手冊是有幫助的 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授可以做的是撰寫一些可能進入這本手冊的細節 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們經營城市 , 走出去設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會讓學者在野外
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們去思考像這樣的問題 , 假設它不只是加拿大 , 和拉爾卡斯楚有關 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	也許巴西是參與者 , 也是西班牙人 。 也許古巴也想要成為四通八達的合作夥伴之一 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要如何寫出條約來做這件事 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	比那更少的先例 , 但那很容易就能解決 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何資助這個 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	新加坡和香港是城市帶來巨大的價值在他們開始時擁有的土地上 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以用土地的價值來支付像警察、法庭等等的東西 , 但學校系統和醫療保健系統也一樣 , 讓這成為更吸引人的地方 , 讓這個地方有更高的收入 , 順道一提 , 讓土地更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 協助建造這個區塊的人的獎勵 , 建立它 , 並建立起基本的規則 , 往對的方向走 。
so there are many other details like this .	所以 , 還有很多其他類似的細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們怎麼能讓低成本、負擔得起的建築物 , 給在第一份工作中工作的人 , 組裝出像iphone的東西 , 但卻讓那些建築物能有效率 , 並確保它們安全 , 讓它們不會在地震或颶風中倒下 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術上的細節是可以解決的 , 但是我們這些已經開始追求這些東西的人 , 已經可以知道 , 沒有道路 , 沒有任何障礙 , 除了想像力的失敗之外 , 還會讓我們無法傳遞真正的全球性雙贏解決方案 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片做個總結 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們之所以能這麼好 , 即使地球上有這麼多人 , 是因為思想的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和其他人分享想法 , 當他們發現它們時 , 他們會和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	它不像稀有的物品 , 分享的意義在於我們每個人都能得到較少的 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們都會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們用那種方式思考想法時 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一類想法:管理我們彼此互動的規則 ; 規則規則像是 , 讓我們有一套支支支撐研究大學的稅制 , 免費提供某種知識 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	讓我們有一個系統 , 在政府辦公室註冊土地的所有權 , 讓人們可以自立自發 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能繼續創新我們的規則 , 尤其是創新 , 想出改變規則的規則 , 這樣我們就不會陷入不良的規則 , 那麼我們就能繼續前進 , 真正讓世界變得更好 , 讓像尼爾森和他的朋友不用再在街燈下研究任何人了 。 謝謝大家 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	基因組學先驅克萊格•凡特從他史詩級的探險旅程中休息一會 , 來談談他團隊發現的數百萬個基因 , 到目前為止 , 用來繪製海洋的生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生物圈、生物科技、企業家、遺傳學、發明、海洋、科學、科技 。
craig venter on dna and the sea	克萊格•凡特在dna和海上
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	休息時 , 我被幾個人問到我對於衰老辯論的評論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	這將是我唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我了解樂觀主義者非常超越悲觀主義者 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	我要告訴各位的是 , 在我18分鐘內 , 我們要如何從讀取遺傳密碼轉換到開始自己寫程式碼的第一階段 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅在10年前 , 我們在這個月發表了第一個免費的有機體序列 , 即 「 嗜血桿菌流感 」 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這個計畫花了13年到4個月的基因組計畫 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以在2到8小時內完成同樣的基因組計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以 , 在過去十年 , 大量的基因組被加入:大部分的人類病原體 , 幾種植物 , 幾種昆蟲和幾種哺乳類 , 包括人類基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	從10多年前開始的這個階段來看基因組學 , 到今年年底 , 我們可能有3到5個基因組測序 ; 它的順序是好幾百個 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛從戈登和貝蒂•摩爾基金會取得一筆資金 , 到排序今年130個基因組 , 作為環保有機體的副計畫 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以閱讀遺傳密碼的速度已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但當我們看 , 外面還有什麼 , 我們幾乎沒抓到這個星球上可用的表面 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部分的人沒有意識到它 , 因為它們是看不見的 , 但微生物佔了地球生物量的一半 , 而所有動物只佔生物量的一半 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許是牛津人不太常做的事 , 但如果你有機會到海裡 , 你就會吞下一口海水 , 記住每一毫升的細菌數量大約有一百萬隻細菌 , 依照一千萬隻病毒的順序 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	兩年前 , 少於5 , 000種微生物物種的特徵 , 所以我們決定為此做點什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開始了sorcer二號探險 , 我們在哪裡 , 和偉大的海洋探險隊一樣 , 試圖每200英哩採集一次海洋 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們開始在百慕達進行測試計畫 , 接著搬到哈利法克斯 , 在美國東岸 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬運河 , 穿越到加拉巴哥群島 , 然後橫越太平洋 , 我們現在正在穿越印度洋的過程中 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常艱鉅的責任 ; 我們在帆船上做這件事 , 有一部分是為了幫助年輕人對進入科學的研究感到興奮 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只要把海水過濾它 , 然後在不同的過濾器上蒐集不同尺寸的生物 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們在洛克維爾的實驗室 , 在這裡我們可以每24小時完成一億個基因密碼的序列 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	透過這樣做 , 我們有了一些驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	舉例來說 , 被認為是我們眼中的視覺色素在環境中只有一兩個有機體有著相同的色素
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎所有在海洋的上半部地區的物種都有這些相同的感光感受器 , 並將陽光當作它們的能量和溝通的來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個地點 , 從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了一百三十萬個新基因 , 和五萬個新物種一樣 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們把這張圖延伸到空中 , 帶著來自史隆基金會的獎金 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們正在測量有多少病毒和細菌 , 我們所有人每天都在呼吸 , 特別是在飛機上或關閉的禮堂上 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們透過一些簡單的儀器過濾 ; 我們每天只收集十億微生物的次序 , 來過濾在紐約市的一棟大樓上 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	而我們現在所處的過程中 , 把這些定序在當下 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	就在資料集的一邊 , 就在我們穿越加拉帕戈斯的地方 , 我們發現 , 幾乎每200英里 , 我們在海洋中的樣本中會看到極大的多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些合乎邏輯 , 以不同溫度的梯度來看 ,
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張衛星照片 , 根據紅色標示溫度 , 藍色是溫暖的 , 我們發現溫暖的水樣本和冷水的樣本有著極大的差別 , 就豐富的物種來說 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一件令我們吃驚的事是這些光感應器偵測不同波長的光 , 我們可以根據它們的氨基酸序列來預測 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	而這些巨大的變化 , 從地區到地區 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	或許不意外的是 , 在深海裡 , 那裡大部分是藍色的 , 感光感受器通常會看到藍光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當周圍有大量葉綠素時 , 他們會看到很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們有更多的差異 , 可能是朝向紅外線和紫外線前進 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了試著去評估我們的基因遺傳狀況 , 我們把所有資料都集合起來 , 包括我們所有離探勘還很遠的資料 , 這代表了地球上一半以上的基因資料 , 總計大約有2千9百萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些放進基因家庭裡 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們只是發現已知家庭的新成員 , 還是發現新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因家庭 , 但我們在環境中採集的每個新樣本 , 會在這些新家庭中加入線性時尚 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	所以 , 我們正處在這個星球上基本基因、成分和生命的最早發現階段 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看所謂的演化樹 , 我們就在右上角 , 和動物一起 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	在大約兩千九百萬個基因中 , 我們的基因組只有兩萬四千個 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有動物集合在一起 , 我們大概只有不到三萬個 , 可能只有十幾個或幾千個不同的基因家族 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我覺得這些基因現在不僅僅是演化的設計元素
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為 , 在以基因為中心的觀點 , 或許可以回到理查德•道金斯的想法 , 而非以基因為中心的觀點 , 這些基因組成的結構不同 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna , 合成dna的能力 , 在過去十年或二十年間 , 已經改變了dna定序的步調 , 越來越快速、非常便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們首次想到合成基因組學 , 是在1995年我們將第二組基因組定序後的1995年 , 和它的生殖器 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤 , 上面寫著: 「 我把生殖器關在心 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是一種微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它有大約500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	嗜血桿菌有一千八百個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們只是問了這個問題 , 如果其中一個物種需要800 , 另外的500 , 是否有一組較小的基因 , 可能會產生一個最小的作業系統 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以 , 我們開始做轉子突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	轉接器只是基因密碼中隨機插入的一小塊dna 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果他們插入基因的中間 , 就會瓦解其功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以 , 我們做了一張所有可以取用轉基因插入的地圖 , 我們稱之為 「 無證基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但事實證明 , 環境對此非常關鍵 , 你只能根據環境中的東西來定義出一個必要或無害的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也試著將13種相關有機體的基因組和基因組做比較 , 我們試著比較所有這些 , 看看它們有什麼共同點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們得到這些重疊的圓圈 。 我們發現只有173個基因 , 只有13個有機體 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	如果我們忽略了一顆細胞寄生蟲 , 它會擴展得更大 , 當我們研究核心基因時 , 大約310個左右 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以 , 我們認為我們可以擴大或收縮基因組 , 取決於你的觀點 , 大約是500個到400個基因 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	要證明這些想法的唯一方法 , 就是用這些基因組建構人造染色體 , 我們必須在以鑄造為基礎的時尚中做到這一點 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現 , 在大片中 , 合成精確的dna是極度困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	hamsmith和clydehutchison , 我的同事研發出令人振奮的新方法 , 讓我們合成一個5000個鹼基對的病毒 , 只需在兩週內 , 準確度是100% , 就其序列和生物學而言 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	那是個相當令人興奮的實驗 , 當我們把合成的dna片段 , 注入細菌中 , 突然間 , dna開始驅動病毒粒子的生產 , 轉過頭 , 然後殺死了細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是第一種合成病毒──小兒麻痺病毒一年以前就被製造出來 , 但它只有十分之一活躍 , 而且花了三年才成功 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix174結構的漫畫 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這個案例是軟體現在建立自己的硬體 , 這就是我們對生物學的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們馬上跳到生物戰爭的擔憂上 , 我最近在參議院委員會前證實了 , 和一間特殊委員會 , 美國政府設立了重新審查這個地區 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 很重要的是要記住現實 , 和人們的想像力會怎麼樣 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 今天任何已被定序的病毒 , 基因組可以被製造出來 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們馬上會對伊波拉或天花感到害怕 , 但這個生物的dna不具傳染性 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使有人做了天花的基因組 , dna本身也不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	安全部門真正擔憂的是設計師病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯兩國 , 致力於創建生物戰爭代理人 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果那個研究真的被打亂了 , 在知識上應該沒有什麼活動可以在未來製造出設計師病毒 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為在兩年內 , 單細胞有機體是有可能的 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	很有可能 , 真正的細胞 , 是我們擁有的 , 在十年內就有可能做到的 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	所以我們現在正在製造數十種不同的構造 , 因為我們可以改變種姓的基因 , 進入這個人造染色體的基因 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵在於 , 如何把所有其他的
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些碎片開始 , 然後我們有一個同源重組的系統 , 將它們重新組合成染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從一個有機體衍生出來的 , deinococcusradiodurans , 可以承受三百萬個放射線 , 不會被殺 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	它在輻射爆炸後的基因體在大約12到24小時內重新組合 , 在它的染色體被完全拆解後 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種生物在地球上無所不在 , 可能因為我們的旅行而存在於外太空 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是在50萬個放射線之後的一個玻璃製造器 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒和破裂 , 同時微生物坐在海底變得更快樂、更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這裡有一張實際狀況的圖片 , 上面顯示了一百七十萬次輻射後的基因組 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體真的被炸開了 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	這裡有同樣的dna , 24小時後自動重新組合 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	這些有機體真的很驚人 , 我們可能有上千種 , 如果這星球上有上萬種不同的物種 , 能夠做到這一點 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組被合成之後 , 第一步就是把它們移植到一個沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	所以我們認為合成細胞將會有極大的潛力 , 不僅是為了了解生物學的基礎 , 也為了希望環境和社會的議題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	舉例來說 , 從我們排列的第三個有機體中 , 甲烷佔有jannaschii , 它生活在沸騰的水溫中 ; 它的能量來源是氫氣 , 而它的碳來自於環境中的二氧化碳 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道許多不同的路徑 , 數千種不同的生物 , 現在住在二氧化碳之外 , 可以捕捉到它 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 與其從石油取得的合成過程中使用碳 , 我們有機會從大氣中捕捉碳 , 將之轉換成生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一個有機體存在於一氧化碳之外 , 我們用它來當作降低水分 , 來產生氫和氧 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 還有許多途徑可以改造代謝甲烷 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦有一項主要的計畫 , 有了挪威的現狀 , 用來捕捉並將天然氣場中的甲烷轉換成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	短時間內 , 我認為將會有一個新的領域 , 叫做 「 組合基因組學 」 , 因為有了這些新的合成能力 , 這些廣大的基因陣列修復和同源重組 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 每天可能製造出一百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 隨著生物學的發展 , 透過篩選 , 不論是篩選氫氣產量 , 或是化學生產 , 或只是可行性 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	若要了解這些基因的作用 , 就會在觸手可及的範圍內運作良好 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試著修改光合作用 , 直接從陽光產生氫氣 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用是由氧氣來調節 , 我們認為有一種氧氣敏感的氫氣 , 會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也在結合細胞酶 , 將複雜糖分解成簡單糖和發酵的酵素 , 在同一個細胞中 , 產生乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	製藥生產已經在使用微生物的主要實驗室裡了 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化合物的化學成分 , 比我們最好的化學家所能產生的更加複雜 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為 , 未來工程的物種可能是食物的來源 , 希望是能源的來源 , 環境的補救 , 也可能取代石化產業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我用倫理和政策研究來做結尾 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	我們在1999年延遲了實驗的開端 , 直到我們完成了一年半的生物倫理審查 , 審查是否該嘗試製造人工物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每個主要的宗教都參與了這個活動 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這其實是個很奇怪的研究 , 因為各種宗教領袖把他們的經文視為法律書籍 , 他們找不到任何東西 , 禁止製造生命 , 所以它一定是沒問題的 。 唯一的最終關注是生物戰爭方面的關注 , 但給了我們開始這些實驗的原因 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	現在sloan基金會剛剛資助了一項多元制度的研究 , 想找出對社會的風險和利益是什麼 , 以及像我自己的科學團隊在這個領域應該要用的規則 , 我們試著在前進的階段設定好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的議題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了生物恐怖主義的威脅之外 , 它們在很多方面都很簡單 , 我們能不能設計東西來產生乾淨能源 , 或許能透過各種簡單的過程 , 改變發展中國家能做的事 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家菲利普•津巴多說幸福和成功 , 根源於我們大部分人不認同的特質:我們朝向過去、現在和未來的方向前進 。 他建議我們在時間上校正我們的外觀 , 作為改善我們人生的第一步 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、快樂、心靈、心理學、科學、科學 。
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	菲利浦津巴多開立一個健康的時光 。
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些關於時間的秘密力量的想法 , 在很短的時間內 。
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好 , 開始時鐘 。 30秒的工作室 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	保持安靜 , 安頓下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	大概是時間 。 結束序列 。 拿一個 。
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	10 , 9 , 8 , 7 , 6 , 5 , 4 , 3 , 2......
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利浦津巴多:咱們來調整一下亞當的誘惑對話 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 來吧 , 亞當 , 不要這麼發真 。 咬一口吧 。 」 「 我有 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 一口咬一口 , 亞當 。 不要放棄艾娃 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 我不知道 , 各位 。
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好吧 , 一口一口 , 什麼地獄 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	生命是誘惑的 。 一切都是為了生育、抗拒 , 是的 , 是的 , 不是 , 現在 , 晚點 , 衝動、反思、當下焦點和未來的焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	承諾的美德會落在當下的熱情之中 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	在未婚的青少女中 , 她們承諾了性墮胎和處女和處女──謝謝妳小布希──多數60%、60% , 在一年內 , 她們受到性誘惑 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	他們大部分都沒有使用節育器 。
so much for promises .	這麼多的承諾 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在讓我們誘惑四歲的孩子 , 給他們治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在可以擁有一顆棉花糖 。 但如果他們等到實驗員回來之前 , 他們可以有兩顆 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然它會付錢 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 等待 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	發生的狀況是三分之二的孩子給予誘惑 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等 。 當然 , 其他的 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 。 他們延遲了現在的延遲 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	沃爾特•密歇爾 , 我在史丹佛的同事 , 在十四年後 , 回去 , 試著去發現那些孩子的不同之處 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	在很多方面 , 抵抗的孩子和反抗的孩子有很大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	那些反抗分數250分的孩子們 , 地點比較高 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	那很巨大 。 那就像是一整套不同的智商點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有惹上麻煩 。 他們是更好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們有自信且有決心 。 今天對我來說 , 關鍵在於 , 他們是把未來的焦點 , 而不是以後的焦點 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 時間的觀點是什麼 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	時間的觀點是研究個人 , 我們所有人 , 把你人類經驗的流動分成時間區域或時間分類 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而且你會自動且無意識地
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	它們在文化、國家、個人、社會階級、教育程度之間有所不同 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 它們會變得偏頗 , 因為你會學會過度使用它們 , 並低估了其他的 。
what determines any decision you make ?	是什麼決定了你做任何決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你決定要採取行動 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人而言 , 只有在立即的情況下 , 其他人在做什麼 , 以及你感覺到什麼 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而這些人 , 當他們在那樣的形式下做決定時 , 我們會稱他們為 「 現狀 」 , 因為他們的焦點是現在的 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在是不相關的 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是在說: 「 我過去經歷過的這種情況是什麼樣的 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以他們的決定是基於過去的回憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們會稱這些人為 「 遺忘者 」 , 因為他們把焦點放在 「 什麼 」 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對他人來說 , 這不是過去 , 不是現在 , 只關乎未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是有關預期的後果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們要稱他們為 「 未來導向 」 。 他們的焦點在將來會變成什麼 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想要辯論 , 時間的悖論 , 會影響你所做的每一個決定 , 你完全沒有意識到 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	也就是說 , 你有這些偏見的時間觀點的程度 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實有六種方法 。 有兩種方法可以用 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式可以被遺忘 , 有兩種方式可以成為未來 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在 「 正面 」 , 或 「 負面 」 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以是 「 節奏主義 」 , 也就是你把焦點放在人生的喜悅 , 或 「 現代主義者 」 ──這不重要 , 你的人生是被控制的 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以以未來為目標 , 設定目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你可以是超然的未來:也就是 , 生命始於死亡 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展心靈靈靈活性 , 轉換時間觀點 , 會依情況的要求而流暢 , 那就是你要學會做的事 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 最佳時間檔案是什麼 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	高度正面 。 高度正面的未來 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	和在 「 現在共和主義 」 上保守 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是在負面和現在的情況下降低 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最佳的 「 顳葉混合 」 是你從過去的正面給你的根源 。 你連結你的家人、身份 , 和你的自我 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	你從未來得到的 , 是翅膀 , 用來翱翔到新的目的地 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從當下的享樂主義得到的 , 是能量 , 探索自我的能量 , 地方 , 人 , 人 , 感性 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何過度時期的看法都比正面的看法有更多的負面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來為成功犧牲了什麼 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲了家庭時間 , 犧牲了朋友時間
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲有趣的時間 , 犧牲個人的疏通
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲嗜好 , 犧牲睡眠 。 所以這會影響到他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	而他們活著工作、成就和控制 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我敢肯定 , 和一些ted成員產生共鳴
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	它為我產生共鳴 。 我是南布朗克斯ghetto的一個貧窮的孩子 , 一個西西里亞家庭 , 每個人都生活在過去和現在 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我來這裡是身為一個走過頂端的人 , 他做了這些犧牲 , 因為老師介入 , 讓我成為未來的方向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那顆棉花糖 , 因為如果你要等你拿到其中兩個 , 直到我學會了平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加上了 「 現代主義 」 , 把焦點放在 「 正面 」 , 所以 , 在76歲時 , 我比以往更有活力 , 更有生產力 , 我比以往更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想說 , 我們把這個應用在許多世界問題上:改變學校孩子的輟學率、組合成癮、增強青少年健康、治癒 「 時代隱喻 」 的隱喻 , 提高了奇蹟能促進永續和保育 , 降低身體復健的速度 , 讓有50%的機率的人喪失自殺的恐怖分子 , 並改變家庭衝突 , 將家庭視為時間區 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	最後我想說:許多生命的謎題可以透過了解你的時間觀和他人的觀點來解決 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法是如此簡單明顯 , 但我認為後果真的很深遠 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	一百年後 , 有多少今天的頭條新聞會很重要 ? 1000年 ? kirkcitron的《漫畫新聞報導》收集的故事 , 不但今天很重要 , 還會引發數百年來的共鳴 。 在ted2010年 , 他強調了近期的頭條新聞 , 帶著我們未來的潛力 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來、全球議題、媒體、新聞、科學、科學 。
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:現在 , 真正的消息是
we are drowning in news .	我們淹沒在新聞裡 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	光是路透社每年就有三百五十萬則新聞報導 。
that's just one source .	那只是一個源頭 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:長遠來看 , 那些故事中有多少其實是很重要的 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這就是長遠新聞背後的想法 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這是長久以來的基金會 , 由tedsters所創立的計畫 , 包括凱文凱利和史都華布蘭德 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	而我們正在尋找的新聞故事可能在50、100或100 , 000年後仍然重要 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你透過這個過濾器看新聞時 , 很多事情都是由此而來 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	為了從去年的a.p.這裡 , 這將在十年內有所關注嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這在50或100年後會很重要嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 那真是很酷 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但去年的頂端故事是經濟 , 我打賭 , 不久後 , 這種特殊的經濟衰退將會是老消息 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	所以 , 什麼樣的故事可能會對未來造成改變 ?
well , let's take science .	嗯 , 讓我們以科學為例 。
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小機器人會透過我們的血液來修復東西 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	有一天如果你是一隻老鼠 , 就已經在這裡了 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	最近一些故事:奈米生物用真蜜蜂毒液來捕捉腫瘤 ; 它們將基因送入大腦 ; 一個他們建造出來的機器人 , 可以爬過人體 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	資源呢 ? 我們該如何餵飽九十億人 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	今天我們要餵飽六十億人 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	正如我們昨天聽到的 , 有超過十億人在挨餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	不經基因改造作物 , 英國就會餓死 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	幸運的是 , 比爾•蓋茲已經賭上十億人在[不清楚]的研究上 。
what about global politics ?	那全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	世界會變得非常不同 , 如果中國設定了議程 , 他們可能會 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們把美國當作世界上最大的汽車市場 , 把德國當作最大的出口者 , 開始在孩子們身上做dna檢測 , 選擇他們的職業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們正在找到各種方法 , 來推回我們所知的極限 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	一些近期的發現:阿根廷的螞蟻群現在已經擴散到每一塊大陸但南極洲 ; 有一個自我導向的機器人科學家很快就發現了 , 科學可能不再需要我們了 , 生命可能不再需要我們了 ; 一個微生物在120 , 000年後醒來 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	看來 , 不論與否 , 生命都會持續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但我去年為這個長新聞所做的選擇是這個:在月球上找到水 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	使得蟻群在上面放置得更容易 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果美國太空總署不做 , 中國可能會 , 或是在座的某人可能會寫很大的支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:長遠來看 , 有些新聞故事比其他新聞更重要 。
